I, the author of this book, have completed it for you, my sons, as a part of the knowledge in medicine, complete and perfect. I have reached the goal with its clarity and simplicity. Now I see fit to finish it with this practical section which is an exercise in doing by hand.
For practice by hand is rare in our land and time, to the point where its science was almost forgotten and its effect ceased. And only a few small sketches of it remained in the books of the ancients, which were worn out by hand and obscured by errors and imperfections until their meanings became obscure and their benefits were lost.
So I saw fit to revive it and compose this section in the manner of explanation, clarity, and brevity, and to provide the images of all surgical instruments as it is an increase in explanation and a means for what one may need.
And the reason that there is no skilled artisan by hand in our time, for the craft of medicine is long and its master should be trained beforehand in the science of anatomy which Galen described. until he knows the benefits and health of the organs, their commingling and separation, the number and exits of the bones, muscles, nerves, and arteries, and the place of their exits.
Therefore Al-Bukhart said that the doctors in name are many and in deed are few, especially in the craft of the hand, and we have mentioned a part of this in the introduction to this book.
For whoever is not knowledgeable about what we have mentioned from anatomy will fall into error and kill people with it, as I have seen many who pretend to this science without knowledge or understanding.
And I have seen an ignorant doctor cut on a sow's wart on the neck of a woman, so he tore some of her neck veins and the woman bled to death before his eyes.
I have seen another physician remove a stone from a man who had been stabbed in the bladder and the stone was large so he broke it with an instrument made of a piece of the catheter. The man died about three days later and I was called to remove it, so I saw from the stone and the bladder what I estimated would have been the case.
And I saw another physician who was a barber among some of our countrymen who practiced medicine.
Then I told a young black boy who had a fracture in his leg near the heel with an open wound, and the physician rushed foolishly and tied the fracture tightly to the wound with ropes and pieces of cloth so as not to let it breathe.
Then he left him to his desires and then let him be for a few days and ordered him not to loosen the bandage until his leg and foot swelled. And I supervised the destruction.
Then I was called to him and I quickly loosed the bandage, so he regained his relief and calmed from his pain, but the corruption had taken hold in the member and I was unable to reverse it.
And the corruption continued to spread in the member until he died.
And I saw another physician who cauterized a malignant tumor and it ulcerated after a few days until his victim became enormous, that being that if the cancer is pure from black bile then it should not be exposed to iron at all.
But only if it is in an organ which can be entirely excised.
And therefore, my sons, you should know that the practice by hand is divided into two parts, a work which goes with safety and a work which goes with corruption in most cases.
And I have warned wherever the operation from this book is done which involves danger and fear, that you should beware of it and reject it.
Beware that the ignorant will not find a way to operate and incise, so take care of yourselves with firmness and safety, and tend to your sickness with compassion and certainty.
And use the best method leading to safety and a praiseworthy outcome, and fight against the dangerous and difficult diseases that are cured.
And take precautions for yourselves so that you are not led astray in your religion and world, it is more worthy to your dignity and will be raised in this life and the next by your destiny.
For Galen has said in some of his advice, do not treat a bad illness lest you be called bad doctors.
And this text is divided into three gates.
The First Gate.
In the furnace by fire, and in the sharp medicine, hastily prepared from ancient times to modern days, and pictures of instruments and furnaces for cauterizing, and all that is needed with the hand.
The Second Gate.
In incisions, cuts, venesection, cupping and bloodletting, and in surgical wounds, removing arrows and the like, all of it hastily prepared and ordered, and pictures of instruments.
The Third Gate.
In cupping and trephining, and in treating the scrofula and the like, all of it hastily prepared from ancient times to modern days, and pictures of instruments.
The First Gate.
In Cauterizing.
And before mentioning its use, it is necessary to mention the way of its benefit and harm, and in which temperament it is used.
And I say that the discussion about the way of the benefit and harm of cauterizing is a long speech, and a precise science, and a subtle secret, and a group of wise men have spoken about it.
And they disagreed in it, and I have shortened their little speech for fear of lengthening.
I say that honey is beneficial in general for any bad temperament, whether with a substance or without it, except for two temperaments: the hot temperament without a substance and the cold temperament without a substance.
As for the cold temperament with a substance, they have differed regarding it; some have said that honey is beneficial in it, while others have contradicted them saying that honey does not cure an illness which is due to heat and cold.
And it is unlikely that someone suffering from a hot and cold illness would be cured by a hot and cold medicine. And the one who contradicts [this] has said that honey with fire may benefit someone suffering from a hot and cold illness which occurs in the bodies of people. For when you have mixed the body and moisture of man with the temperament of fire, the body of man becomes cold.
And I say, because experience has shown me this many times, except that it should not be imagined by one who does not know and is not experienced in the matter of honey. And I have considered the differences in temperaments among people, and the condition of illnesses themselves, their causes and symptoms, and the length of their time.
And as for the other temperaments, have no fear from them, especially cold and moist illnesses; all physicians have agreed on this and have not disagreed that honey is beneficial in them.
Know, my son, that the fire treatment with honey is a secret of healing and its excellence over the hot medicine treatment because fire is a pure essence that does not exceed the action of the limb it cooks, nor does it harm another connected limb except for a slight damage.
And the honey treatment with hot medicine can exceed its action to what is beyond the limbs, and perhaps it will cause a disease in the limb that is hard to cure, and perhaps it will kill; but fire, because of its nobility and the purity of its essence, does not do this except if it is excessive.
It has been proven to us through experience, the length of service and care for craftsmanship and standing on the facts of the case.
So I have refrained from lengthy speech, and if not for the fact that it would not befit this book, I would have told you in secret, more obscurely and by what manner it is done on the bodies and repelled with diseases with philosophical words, evident proofs to make you understand.
Know, my sons, that they have differed in the time suitable for the cautery and have made the best time to be the spring season.
And I say that the cautery can be suitable in every time, so that the damage caused by time is absorbed into the benefit which is brought about by the cautery. And especially if the cautery is for strong and severe pains that cannot be delayed, because of fear that it will follow with more intense suffering which is worse than the damage caused by time.
And do not think, my sons, that the cautery which cures a disease so that it will never return again is a remedy.
And you are not to think that the cautery is merely a remedy which adjusts the temperament and dries up the moistures which are the cause of the pains.
Except that the cautery is preferred over medicine by its quick success, strong effect and sharp power.
And it is possible that the disease may return after a time, according to the temperament of the patient and his constitution and strength, and what accumulates in him from impurities and neglecting himself in acquiring them from food and things like that from the causes.
God forbid that the disease in which the cautery is used is a mild disease and in an organ with little impurities and moistures. Similar to the relief of dental caries from pain and the like, it may not return in this case, at least.
And as for the saying of the common people that the tooth is the last remedy, it is a true saying, but not in what they say by which they believe that there is no cure that benefits either with medicine or without.
And the meaning of that the tooth is the last remedy, is that we have used types of treatments for a certain illness and those drugs did not benefit then we use the tooth as a cure, and from this comes the saying that the tooth is the last remedy. No, in the sense which the common people and most of the ignorant physicians have gone to.
And the early ones have mentioned that the tooth made of gold is better than the tooth made of iron, and they said this because of the moderation of gold and the nobility of its essence, and they said it does not spoil the place of the tooth, which is not at all.
Because I have tried that, and found it to do so in some teeth rather than others, and the tooth with it is better and more excellent than iron as they said, except that if you heat the alloy in the fire of gold, you will not know when you protect from the fire that causes redness of the gold.
And because cold rushes to it quickly, and if you increase on it in heat it melts in the fire, and if you hesitate it fails, so the craftsman falls into trouble because of that, for this reason the tooth made of iron has become quickest and nearest to the right in our practice, God willing.
And I have regulated this chapter on the tooth into sections that I have arranged from head to foot, so it may be easy for the student who wants it, God willing.
The first section.
In the tooth of the head, one tooth.
This remedy is useful against the dampness and coldness which cause headaches, frequent fevers on the head towards the eyes and ears, excessive sleepiness, toothache, and throat pain. In general, for every disease caused by coldness, such as paralysis, epilepsy, lethargy and similar afflictions.
An image of this remedy is to have the physician first order a purging draught that cleanses the head, three nights or four as the physician deems necessary for the strength and condition of his patient.
Then have him shave his head with a razor, then make him sit before you reclining, with his hands on his chest.
Then place the tip of your finger at the base of his nose between his eyes, and where you reach with the middle finger mark that place with a pin.
Then light the resinous torch which this picture shows.
Reveal from the bone as much as a fistful of hair or a nut, then lift your hand if it comes loose otherwise go back with the same instrument or something else if it becomes cold. Until you see from the bone what I have told you, then take some salt and dissolve it in water, let him drink a dose of it, put a poultice on the place and leave it for three days.
Then load a poultice soaked in fat on him and leave it until the pricking from the burning goes away then treat him with the greasy ointment until he is cured if God wills.
And they said that an open wound, as soon as it becomes foul, lets out the badness and is better and more beneficial.
And some of them mentioned that the skin should be cauterized to the bone and hold the torch until a part of the thickness of the bone is burned, then it will be stripped after that what has been burned from the bone is treated.
They said it should be irrigated abundantly until it has a strong effect on the bone, so that it falls from the bone like the small gemstone or small pearl. They claimed that vapor rises from that place and the wound remains open for a long time.
Then it is treated until it heals. I do not see these two kinds of irrigation at all except in some people, and through deceit and leaving me better and safer if it were to occur. The head swells when its natural connection is disrupted, as we have seen in the rest of the organs.
And especially when the patient's head is weak by nature. The first kind of irrigation is safer and better in my opinion, and I have seen it work well, so try it if Allah wills.
The second chapter.
In the irrigation of the head also.
If a persistent and prolonged headache occurs in the patient, along with chronic pain, and he has used bandages, poultices, plaster casts, paints, dressings, especially if one type of irrigation that we described was tried on him without benefiting him from it, then look. If the patient's head is strong in constitution and not weak, and he finds a severe burning sensation, then irrigate him with another kind of irrigation on top of that lightly. Then irrigate each of his temples with a kind of irrigation until the skin thickness is reduced and the amount that we described on the bone becomes apparent. And irrigate a kind of irrigation in the back of his head in the place known as the saw, and lighten your hand in this, do not expose the bone because the patient will find it painful, unlike all other head irrigations, and I will mention this irrigation in its place.
And it is desirable that the irrigating instrument used for the temples and back of the head be softer than the one used for the middle of the head, and this is its shape.
Chapter Three.
In a case of chronic suppurating fistula.
If a wound occurs on the head accompanied by headache and headache extending to the eye, the healer should purge it with cleansing medicines for the head, and apply all other treatments mentioned in Tashbih al-Amradd as was said previously. If that does not succeed, apply cauterization to both faces. Either by applying the hot caustic drug or with iron.
And as for cauterizing with the hot drug, take a single clove of garlic, peel it and cut its edges from both sides, then make an incision in the place of the pain on the forehead with a wide probe until there is a space under the skin that will hold the clove.
Then it is put under the skin until it disappears, then a strong thread is tied over it tightly and left for as long as fifteen days, then it is removed and the garlic taken out. The wound is left for two or three days, then it is covered.
Over it a string soaked in fat is applied until the area becomes septic, then it is treated with ointment until it heals, if God wills. And if you wish, do this with some of the caustic medicines that I mentioned in chapter eighteen on caustics.
And as for cauterizing it with iron, do so in this manner: Protect the metal instrument that looks like:.
It is called the iron rod, the mizmar, because its head resembles a reed with some bulging and in its middle is a small nail.
Then you place it on the site of the wound, and hold your hand steady as you rotate the iron rod a little at a time, and the amount that burns through the thickness of the skin is about half of it. Then you raise your hand so that the vein beneath does not burn and cause bleeding, then soak a string in salt water and place it on the site and leave it for three days. Then take the quill with fat then treat it with ointment until it is healed if God wills.
And if you wish to cut this joint with the sharp side of the scalpel coming from the lancet and to beware of cutting the artery in this non-chronic joint.
The Fourth Chapter.
In a chronic joint.
If you have treated the joint with what has been mentioned from the preceding treatment and what has been mentioned in dividing the diseases, and the treatment has not benefited and you have seen that which cannot be treated by applying the first treatment with medicine or cutting with fire. You must preserve the sharp lancet until it whitens, then you learn on the place of pain with a stroke as long as half a finger or so and leave your hand once and pull it tightly until you cut the artery and reach towards the bone.
But you must beware of cutting the jaw that moves when chewing so as to burn the muscle or the nerve driving it, causing twitching.
And be on guard and beware of arterial bleeding which you have cut because in its cutting is a pitfall. Especially for one who is ignorant of what he does and has not been proven by the way and to leave the work first.
And the treatment of bleeding from the artery on its face will be mentioned in its place in this book if God wills, if you see that which cannot be treated by this cutting.
And if you saw the body of the patient being swollen, then apply the lancet in the middle of the head as we have described and treat the wound until it is healed if God wills.
And if you wish, then use the lancet which we have mentioned in the chapter of cutting the vein with the lancet having two sharp edges because it is a better and safer cut than this.
The Fifth Chapter.
In ears which are inflamed.
If there occurs in the ear inflammation due to cold and it has been treated with poultices and all the treatment which we mentioned in the classification, but the pain does not go away, then clean out the cavity which is called the point shown in this drawing.
Then cauterize it with it after heating it, around the ears all over as they turn or around them both if there is pain in both. And it is removed from the beginning of the ear a little after the place has been marked with ink, and the caustic is as much as ten points in each ear or so, then the places are treated until they heal if God wills.
The Sixth Chapter.
In cauterizing the deafness.
The deafness which is treated with caustic is from the type which occurs from phlegm as I mentioned in the classification of diseases.
And a caustic is avoided for the type that occurs from membranous and convulsions of the nerve.
If you have treated this type of deafness with ceruse and safflower and mustard paste, but your treatment did not help, then the patient should be cauterized with three caustics. One at the root of the ear and the second a little below the nostril and the third at the meeting of the lips.
And make your caustic opposite to the sick side because relaxation occurs on the healthy side.
And a drawing of the caustic is that you apply it to the tip of the upper ear, a little below the horn of the head, and another one in the nostril, and its length should be as much as the eyebrow.
You lower your hand with the caustic until you burn as much of the skin as half its thickness, and this is a drawing of the cautery and it is a type of scorifying which we mentioned earlier but it is a little softer than that, as you see. It is necessary that the needle be in it a little thicker, then treat the place as was mentioned above until it heals with God's will.
Chapter Seven.
In case of chronic ulcers.
If you have treated the ulcer and done what was mentioned to us, but your treatment did not succeed and it is not due to fever, then take four cauterizations. On every hundredth of his head a cauterization and a cauterization in the middle of the head as we mentioned and a cauterization on the nape of his neck as was said before.
The recipe for the cautery as mentioned, and also he may cauterize a cauterization on the mouth of the stomach, it will be more effective, then treat as was said before.
Chapter Eight.
In case of forgetfulness (or perhaps "forgetting" being a euphemism for mental illness) .
The one who is from phlegm should be given the patient a drink first of large purging herbs for the brain.
Then he should shave his whole head and carry on the back of his neck a poultice of turmeric written in an article for indolence it is repeated sometimes because it is a cure.
And do the same on the rank mentioned there exactly then it is blameless, otherwise take three cauterizations on the back of his head they should be arranged from the top of the head to the neck.
Make a thickness of a finger between each cauterization and the next one then treat the cauterizations as was said before, if you wanted to increase it and the patient is able for that then take the middle cauterization.
If you wanted to increase it then take on the hundredths and treat him until he heals, and the cautery is olive-like in the form that was mentioned before.
Chapter Nine.
In case of apoplexy and relaxation of all the body.
It is necessary to proceed with cleansing the head with aloe and what we have mentioned, then shave the patient's head and put three stitches in the middle of the head and one on each horn of the head and one at its back.
And three on the vertebrae of the neck, if he was in a paralysis of relaxation of the body and it is necessary for him more than that and the patient is liable to this and the disease is strong and firm, then put four stitches on the vertebrae of his back. And inform him to put stitches until they burn most of his skin and raise your hand then treat him as mentioned before until he recovers if God wills, and the stitches should be olive green.
The Tenth Chapter.
In case of epilepsy.
It is necessary to clean his brain first with large aloe and all the treatment which we mentioned in the classification if the patient is big and liable to take medicine.
But if he is a boy who cannot take medicine, then the cathartic and cleansing emetic for the brain should be used before that by many days with his nourishment being improved.
Then shave his head and put a single stitch in the middle of the head as mentioned before, and another stitch at its back. And on each horn of his head, a stitch, if the patient is strong and liable to it, then put the stitches which we mentioned in the case of paralysis of relaxation of the body on the vertebrae of the neck and the back, and the stitches should be olive green as mentioned previously.
If the patient is a boy then make the stitches gentle in this form.
The Eleventh Chapter.
In case of malnutrition.
If the cause of malnutrition is foul humidity and thick phlegm, administer to him the medications we mentioned for one with epilepsy.
If the cause of malnutrition is a tendency towards blackness and the body of the patient is wet and foul, purify his brain as mentioned in the division.
Then shave the head of the patient, then make a tight cake from flax like a circle and place it in the middle of his head; the patient sits upright with it grasped on all sides. Then take one pound of old goat fat.
Then heat it on the fire with moderate heat until the finger can be placed in it; then pour it into the middle of his head, in the circle, and leave it until it cools. You do this for the patient once a week along with his other good treatment, until he is cured, if God wills.
And if you wish to cool him, put many small pieces of ice without grasping the mortar with your hand but rather with a spoon; for this kind of medicine moistens the brain moderately.
Then place on him a cloth that has been dipped in lard or chicken fat.
The Twelfth Chapter.
In case of water flowing into the eye.
If you find that water has flowed into the eye at its onset, as indicated by the signs mentioned in the division, first purify his head and protect him from all moisture, then bathe him in a bath immediately for some days.
Then shave his head and administer a medication in the middle of the head, then apply two medications on the temples if water flowed into both eyes initially or into one eye alone if it flowed into only one.
Then cut with the mortar all the veins and nerves under the skin, so that the medications be placed in them from the width of the temples, and preserve him from bleeding.
If you see anything of it, cut it off from the place with any treatment you can and we will come to wisdom in ligating the blood vessels and cutting them and cautioning against bleeding.
And it may have a boil beneath the bones, two severe ones.
The Thirteenth Chapter.
For chronic tears.
If the eye discharge is chronic and permanent, and it comes from the vessels and blood vessels that are outside the head and you have found out that this is due to a large amount of thick cold mucus then apply the remedy I have described for running water. A poultice on the middle of the head and two poultices on the temples and two poultices under the bones at the back of the head, and if you need to add more then apply a poultice each side of the eyebrow with a small cloth.
The Fourteenth Chapter.
For a nasal polyp.
If you have treated him with what we mentioned in the division and the treatment has not been successful then take him to a wetter place for three nights, then shave his head and apply the middle poultice with an olive cloth. Then apply with a chamomile cloth two poultices above the eyebrows under the hair a little and caution from the blood vessel, do not cut it, and this is the picture of the chamomile.
The Fifteenth Chapter.
For a poultice to relax the eyelid.
If the eyelid has relaxed due to an illness or moisture then apply a poultice to the eyelid with this helianthus cloth.
And if you want then apply above the eyebrows a little two poultices in each direction and separate from the temples and let the length of each poultice be on the length of an eyebrow.
Do not overdo with your hand, but to the extent that a third of the skin burns, and the appearance of the cauterizing is like this.
Chapter Sixteen.
For cataract in the eyelid.
If its threads have turned inside first, then the cauterizing within it is of two types. Either the cauterizing with fire or the cauterizing with a burning medicine, as for the cauterizing with fire then the operator should command that the threads be left before doing so if they are of those which he removes in order to let them lengthen and even out.
If they are removed when it is sprouting, then bind his eyes with a bandage so that they do not move until it has grown. When it has grown and evened out, put the head of the operator in your hand, then teach him on the eyelid with ink an indication like the shape of the leaf of Asa tree.
The indication begins close to the threads, then place a cotton swab soaked in egg white or the spittle of a gazelle under the eyelid, and protect the shape of this cauterization.
Then cauterize on the shape which you taught him a little at a time, many times until the surface of the skin which is in the shape of the leaf of Asa tree all burns and becomes clear, and the sign of the success of your work that you see the eyelid has firmed up and the hair has risen from the fold of the eye.
Then lift your hand and leave him for three days, then place a cotton swab with fat on it until the hairs of Khashkrish fall out, then treat him with ointment until he recovers if God wills it, in case some hair returns after time and the eyelid relaxes.
Then repeat the cauterizing on that place as you did first, and if there is hair in the lower eyelid then burn it until it returns to its natural place without harming the eye's hair, and as for cauterizing with a burning medicine then it is that you command the operator to leave the threads until they lengthen and even out.
Then make a figure from paper of a linen cloth. And take from the accustomed soap and unextinguished gypsum, each a weight equal to a dinar or about that, grind them together well and do this with a mill so they don't dry out. Then spread some of it on the paper you made like a linen cloth and put it on one eye or both. And put under the eye a moistened swab in white egg whites and the tip of the probe in your stone.
And put your thumb on top of the medicine and compress it a little while you move it whenever the probe finds the bitterness of the medicine because it finds a sting like fire. As long as it finds the sting, leave the medicine and move it with your finger. If the sting subsides, remove the medicine and wash the eye with water.
And look, if you see the eyelid has risen like it rises when burned with fire or by cuts. If not, then apply more medicine to the place where the medicine did not take effect and was not absorbed until you complete your work and scorch the eye, then put on it a cotton soaked in fat so that the blister of burn disappears.
Then treat it with ointment or its equivalent until it heals. And you must be extremely cautious when working so that nothing of the medicine falls into the eye, for if the eyelid relaxes after a few days and hair grows inside the eye.
Then reapply the medicine to that place in the eyelid which relaxed especially as you did at first, then treat it until it heals. And this is an image of a linen cloth.
Know that the eyes of people can differ in size and largeness, so according to that let your treatment be, and do not think that the correct way is easy for one who has an ulcer with this craft.
Chapter Seventeen.
Regarding the transparent membrane which is exposed in the eye's corner.
If you treated the transparent membrane with what we have mentioned in the sections on diseases, and your treatment was not effective, it should be applied with this quality.
The patient should place his head in your lap and a servant hold his head between your hands, holding it firmly so that it does not move or strike against anything.
Then you put a wet cloth in the white of egg or in the saliva of the hyena on his eyes, then cover the compress which is in this form.
It should be folded like the shape of a swan's feather from one end which is the part with the membrane, and if you wish it to be perforated at the other end and if you wish it to be sealed like a jar, but this foldable one is better for your treatment, God willing.
Then you squeeze the transparent membrane if it is open, and let out its contents and clean it, or if it is not open then you should open it and take out its pus, then put the compress on it which is very tightly held by your hand until you reach the bone.
And keep your hand a little away from the membrane, from the eye towards the nose, so that your hand does not err or the patient becomes anxious and the compress falls into the corner of the eye and damages it. And if you reach the bone with the first treatment, and otherwise, then redo the compress again as needed.
And leave it for three days, then put on him a cloth with fat and treat him with the dried ointment until he is cured. And if forty days pass and he does not get well, then put on him the sharp and potent medicine until the bone is revealed, and refer him to what will be mentioned about this in its chapter, God willing.
And another method of treating the transparent membrane mentioned by some earlier people, is to make an incision on the place of the membrane and then put a thin cup in the same cut.
You place in it the weight of a dinar of molten lead, and hold your hand with a good firm grasp. The patient should not stir at all, lest the molten lead run into his eye. You should put on the eye of the patient a moistened cotton pad, either in the white of an egg or in water.
If the lead corrodes the navel, it burns its place and cures it in a wonderful manner. If the navel is cured with what we have mentioned from treatment and medication, then that is good. Otherwise, there must be the use of an incision into the nostril and returning the navel to the course of the nostril as will come next about this.
The Eighteenth Chapter.
A treatment for a cut lip.
A split in the lip is often called a "shu'rah" and especially so in the lips of children, for it often occurs. If you treated this split as we mentioned in its division but the treatment was unsuccessful, then bring near a small, thin iron blade like this.
Its hollow is against the edge of the blade, then you place it over the splint with the wheel until the treatment reaches the depth of the split. Then treat it with cauterization until it heals, God willing.
The Nineteenth Chapter.
A treatment for a boil occurring in the mouth.
If there appears in the root of the gum or in the tonsils or at the roots of the teeth a swelling, then it becomes an abscess and bursts and became a foul-smelling boil, then you treated it but the treatment was unsuccessful, then you should bring near a cautery to fit into the boil.
Then you insert it into the boil, heated, through a puncture in the boil and hold your hand until the cautery, covered, reaches its top and bottom. You do that once or twice then treat it after that with what we have mentioned from treatment until it heals, God willing.
If the material (tissue) is dry and has been evacuated, then it is sufficient. Otherwise, one must explore the site and remove the putrid bone as will be mentioned in its chapter if God wills.
The Twentieth Chapter.
In loosened fistulas and gaping ulcers.
If the ulcer has loosened due to moisture and the fistulas have been moved and treated with medicines but did not heal, then place the end of the instrument on your knee before you shape the handle which will be shown after this, after placing the tube over the molar.
Then the instrument with a handle, warmed up by turning a wheel, is inserted into it and your hand is held firm until the heat reaches the root of the tooth. Then you raise your hand and repeat the process as desired. Then the patient fills his mouth with saltwater.
And hold it for an hour, and then throw him. For the moving tooth will be fixed and the loosened ulcer will tighten, and dry out the rotten moisture.
The Twenty-First Chapter.
In cases of severe toothache.
If the toothache is from cold or there are worms and treatment with medicines did not heal it, then a poultice is applied on the two cheeks either a poultice of fat or a poultice by fire.
As for the poultice of fat, take cow's fat and boil it in an iron basin or a caldron. Then take a thread and wrap it on one end of the stick then immerse it in the melted fat and put it on the painful tooth by turning the wheel and hold it until it cools down.
Then repeat it several times until the heat reaches the root of the tooth. And if you want to immerse a wool or thread in cold fat and put it on the painful tooth, and place a heated iron shield over it until the fire reaches the bottom of the tooth.
As for cauterization with fire, this is that you should proceed to a copper or iron tube and it will be in its contents some thickness so that the heat of the fire does not reach the mouth of the instrument. Then tie the cloth which comes in its shape and put it on the same side and hold your hand until the cautery cools down; do this several times.
For the pain will go either with its sight on that day or another, and it is advisable after that cauterization to fill the instrument's mouth with good fat and keep it for an hour then discharge it, and this is the shape of the cautery.
It will be cauterized at any point you wish and as best you can; and this is the shape of the tube.
Chapter Twenty-Two.
On cauterizing pigs.
If the pigs are full of phlegm and cold moisture and have not been seasoned with medicine to be cooked quickly, then tie the hollow cautery which has this shape, the ends being perforated.
Let the smoke come out from the other end at the cauterization, and put it covered on the same boil once or twice if needed until it reaches the depth of the boil; and if the boil is small then make the cautery to the size of the boil.
Then leave it for three days and carry a cord soaked in fat on top of it until what has burned with fire is gone then treat it with ointment and bandages until it clears up, God willing.

Then cover with the cloth having two folds the one which its form is shown here.
Then pound with it the skin until it penetrates to the other side and the form of the pounding appears four poundings, and it can be pounded with a cloth having three folds so that the form of the pounding is six poundings and the folds are on the surface of the wound.
And this is the picture of the cloth having three folds.
And one can be added to this number, so the poundings will be eight. Then it is carried on top of the pounded parts with crushed pepper and salt then bandaged with a warm wet cloth and the limb is not moved until it is strong, and if there was an avulsion above that happens rarely.
So pound on the hip one well-ribbed pounding or many poundings with a dotting so that the joint gets strong and the moisture goes away and the swelling subsides.

Chapter Forty-two.
For the piles.
If there occurs pain and inflammation in the perineum, and this is due to coldness and catarrh, and the treatment mentioned in the section has not been effective, and time has elapsed, then it is advisable that the cause of the trouble be relieved from thick mucus by means of the oil of the mastic or the oil of the Saburah and similar things.
Then cauterize it and apply the cautery to the pile itself on two forms, either a caustic or fire. The cauterization by fire is performed on many faces, one of them being that you apply three caustic pieces in this shape.
It becomes a healthy depth and there will be, between each caustic piece and the next one, a thickness equal to that of the finger. The cautery is olive-like. A caustic may also be applied in the middle on the top of the perineum itself so that it becomes four pieces. In order for the ring to encircle all of the perineum and burn all its thickness, this is the form of cauterization in piles if the pain is constant on the perineum itself and does not extend to the thigh or leg.
If it extends to the thigh and leg, then cauterize two pieces, one on the thigh in the place indicated by the pain itself and another above the perineum with four fingers towards the external side a little. The cautery is very thin and the depth of the cauterization is only as thick as the skin.
And if it indicates that the pain extends to about the length of a foot, then cauterize where it indicated for you with a thin cautery point three or four or more times as needed. And if it indicates pain under the knee towards the leg, then cauterize there one thin cautery piece.
All vessels are preserved from cutting to the skin, until an artery or large vein is cauterized. This will leave a bad and prolonged ulcer on the wound.
And I have seen one person and another, in whom the vein was cut above the ankle and it ran to the wound. Then the leg swelled until gangrene reached the foot and all of it became putrid. And then diarrhoea and death occurred afterwards. If the pain is in both legs in the same manner.
And some of the wise men have mentioned making a catheter for an intestinal fistula, in this manner: it is made from metal and its diameter is half a finger's breadth. It has at its mouth thickness like that of a date stone or slightly less. Inside it there are two other catheters, one inside the other.
And there is a space of the breadth of a thumb between each catheter. The catheters are open on both sides and their height is around the breadth of one or two thumbs. It has a metal handle attached to them which holds them firm, this is its form.
Then it is heated in the fire until it is red-hot, and then embers are placed upon the fistula, and the patient lies on the healthy side. Three rounded cauterizations are made at one time, and it is left for three days. Then it is plugged with fat and the wound is left open for a period of time.
This type of cauterization is rarely used because it is troublesome and its appearance is frightening, and most people do not have the patience for it. However, it is a good type of cauterization for someone who can endure it and suffers no harm from it.

Then you treat him with ointments until he heals. If the pain extends to the thigh or leg, a poultice is made for him as was done on the hip, in the same way, and this is the characteristic of hot water and I have proved it in the chapter on treating diseases.
You take from the moist salt and unheated gypsum, each a part of one, crush them together and put them in a new pot that has been pierced with a small hole at the bottom, like the size of a reed. Then you place under the base of the pot another pot filled with a mixture.
You pour on the salt and gypsum from sweet water so that they are submerged by a finger. After you have kneaded them well with your hand, leave the pot until the hot water flows into the lower pot filled with mixture. And it becomes very hot in its severity, it will be effective in many activities of medicine and in all the other members because it does to the effect of fire exactly. And among the medications that can be used on the hip is thapsia and honey of balsam with crushed gypsum and soap.

Until he may enter the bath carried and come out cured, it being to take from the green chicory then if the green is not found the fresh one is taken and its root is crushed with some fat and put on the hip where the pain is or in the leg or in the thigh.

The Twenty-Second Chapter.
A plaster for the pain of the back.

The Fourth Chapter on the Forty-fourth Type.

The Forty-Fifth Chapter.
For the treatment of boils.
If a boil appears in the groin and some of the discharge and pus have flowed into the testicles and this is happening soon, it is advisable to order the surgeon to let him abstain from eating for a day and to use what causes evacuation by stool from his abdomen.
Then he lies on his back in front of you and order him to hold himself until the pus or discharge becomes prominent, then push it with your finger, then mark with a pen under the boil on the os pubis an indication resembling half a circle with its ends towards the upper body.
Then protect this shape of the awl.
Until it comes white and expels the pus, then discharge the matter or pus into his abdomen. Then put a servant's hand on the place so that the matter does not come out again. The servant has placed himself between the surgeon's legs and I have placed a cushion under him and another servant has tied his legs.
Finally, he takes hold of the patient's chest with both hands. Then, the instrument is lowered onto the same mark and a pressure is applied with it standing upright until the bone is reached or returned to its place again if it was not reached on the first try.
And be careful not to press the instrument too hard while you are chipping, so that it does not burn him. For if this happens to the patient either death or a great fracture will result. And know that whenever you do not reach the bone with the chisel your operation has failed. And the chisels for children should be soft on their limbs and for adults on theirs.
Then treat the place of chipping with fat for three days until the redness goes away, then treat it with bandages until it heals. And let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is closed.
And it is necessary to make his food for the duration of his treatment soft, so that the contents do not emerge when he defecates or urinates. Then if he wants to get up after forty days use a strong bandage and hold him fast for another forty days, and reduce his fatigue, fullness from food and drink, and loud shouting.
For if he is treated in this way, he will be completely healed, God willing. And I will mention the treatment of an abscess by cutting into it through its opening, God willing. And as for the perforation that occurs in other parts of the abdomen and was initial, if you want it not to increase, then make a straight chisel incision from it according to its size. And make an incision in the skin like a third of it, then treat it as we mentioned, for he will not increase, God willing. The Forty-Eighth Chapter.
On The Scissors.
If an injury occurs in some organs due to a fall or blow and the pain persists for a long time and treatment with medicine does not cure it, one should then apply pressure with a blunt instrument; every organ should be compressed according to its size, weakness and strength.
And if the pain and swelling subside from it then he is cured of the first pressure; otherwise, one should apply the pressure again to it because it is customary for these pains to move from the organ to what is next to it so one should follow them with the pressure until the sick part heals.
The Forty-Ninth Chapter.
On The Scarring of Leprosy.
But those afflicted with leprosy may benefit from the pressure greatly, especially the type of leprosy that occurs due to putrefaction of phlegm and blackness.

And it will peel off from him scales which are easily exhaling heavy fumes and also compressing it with the same pressure on the navel as mentioned above; and if the leprosy has continued on the sick part and a clear sign of it appears, then one should compress these pressures that were mentioned on the head. Bandages on the tip of the nose, two bandages on the cheeks, two bandages on the neck vertebrae, six on the back vertebrae and a large one on the scrotum when the penis is limp, another above it in the same table, two on each thigh, one. Two on the knees, one on each knee, two on the shoulders, two on the elbows, two on the armpits and compressing on every joint of his fingers and feet bandage and on every heel of his feet and wrist of his hands.

The Eighth and Forty-Eighth Chapter.
If the numbness of a limb or part is treated with medicines, ointments and bandages but it does not heal, then cover the same limb or part with bandages according to its size whether large or small like your hand and arm in thickness of skin slightly.
Then treat it with ointment until it heals. And sometimes the numbness which is exposed to hand and foot on the back vertebrae, when the nerve that moves this member goes out, the numbness will go away.
And none should be attempted except by one who is knowledgeable about the anatomy of members and exit points of nerves that move the body.
Chapter Forty-Eight.
On the Treatment of Leprosy.
If the leprosy has progressed and no remedy of medicine has been effective for it, put on him a dressing in depth slightly according to the thickness of the skin until the whiteness goes away and its colour changes.
Then treat him with a mixture of fine wormwood, crushed rose mallow leaves and either the blood of a sheep or the blood of a cuttlefish, each one part, all mixed together and spread on a cloth and apply to the affected area until it heals.
Chapter Fifty.
On the Treatment of Cancer.
If the cancer is in its early stages and you wish to stop it, apply a caustic ring around it as it turns. Some wise men have mentioned that one should apply a strong dressing in the middle of it, but I do not see anything in this because I fear it will suppurate and I have seen this happen many times.
The correct method is to cauterize around it with a ring as we said, or with many dressings.
Chapter Fifty-One.
On the Treatment of Erysipelas.
If erysipelas has occurred in one of them and it has slowed down in healing either due to the active humour that caused it or due to old age, which is a weak constitution, or due to time, and you want to speed up the healing process then cauterise around it with many small dressings sprinkled.
Then leave it alone because it will speed up in healing; and if you want to stop its progress with a caustic, then let the flame of this instrument be the one.
And let it down in the middle of the erysipelas until it penetrates the skin; and let the caustic be below so that evacuation will become easy, then treat it as it should be until it heals.
The second and fifty-second chapter.
In the mouth of the eater.
The eater is a corruption that seeks in the body that it eats, just as fire seeks dry wood. If you see the eater in a place that can be inflamed by fire, treat with many small and large cauteries according to the need of that place where the eater is.
Then treat it from all sides until the corruption is completely eliminated, and nothing of it remains at all. Then leave it for three days and carry on the burnt places with sulphur powder mixed with oil until the eschar forms completely and all the corruption leaves.
Then treat it with poultices suitable for flesh. If you see after three days that the flesh is growing healthy growth without corruption in it, and otherwise make the caustic again on what remains of the corrupted places, and the eater can be treated with hot medicine.
For it has a place that serves with fire more quickly and better, and I mentioned its treatment with hot medicine in the classification, so take it from there whenever you need it.
The third and fifty-third chapter.
In the treatment of iron splinters, whether inverted or not.
This condition often occurs in the soles of the feet and is a harsh, rough thing that afflicts the man. The treatment for it is on two sides, either by cauterization with fire or by hot water.
As for the treatment with fire, it is that you make a heated cautery similar to the feathers of an eagle made from iron, according to what surrounds the splinter on all sides and with a thin edge. Then place it over the splinter and turn your hand around the cautery until it reaches deep into the splinter.
He should leave it for three days when he intends to drain it, then tie it up with crushed wild leek, salted and smeared on, leaving the dressing on overnight. If it comes out from its roots, then treat the site of the wound with a poultice made from the juice of plants that cure flesh until it heals, if the splinters are not inverted.
And it often occurs on the surface of the body, especially in the hands and feet. It is necessary to take a tube from copper or iron or eagle's feathers and insert it over the splinter or boil then pour into the tube hot water in a small quantity.
And grasp the hand with it as you turn it a little with a slight squeezing of the hand so that the rim of the tube affects the base of the splinter and the hot water finds its way to penetrate into the base of the splinter, and the patient endures for an hour the heat of the water.
Then leave it, for the splinter will come out with its roots. Do this one by one until all of them have been removed from the body, then treat their places after they have come out with a poultice made from what plants juice cure flesh.
The 52nd Chapter.
For the abscess.
If it occurs to one abscess from the cold on a nerve or a quart of fever or other such thing, then apply to it four or five poultices on a backrest between each poultice and in his chest a poultice. And to his stomach, a poultice with olive oil, for the abscess subsides and the chill of the disease is quickly resolved.
The 55th Chapter.
For the poultice of boils that occur on the body.
It may break out on the body with foul boils that are caused by thick and rotten cold substances, therefore it is necessary at their first appearance to apply a soft poultice to the head of each boil made from an alder twig that has been set on fire or the tip of a long absinthe plant or olive wood.
And the bloodletting should be done in its beginning flow on this quality, so it will not increase and the cause of the ailment is cleared from it, except that it should be after evacuation of the ailment by venesection.
The 52nd Chapter.
When cutting the artery.
A severe bleeding of blood often occurs from an artery that has been severed when a wound is exposed from the outside, or when cutting and excising a tumour or part of a limb and the like, making its cutting difficult.
If it happens to anyone, then hasten with your hand to the mouth of the artery and put your thumb on it and press it gently until the blood is contained under your thumb and nothing comes out from it. Then place a number of small and large laurel twigs in the fire and fumigate them until they become very smoky.
Then take one of them, either small or large according to the wound and the place where the artery burst open, and put the twig on the same spot after you remove your thumb and hold the twig until the blood stops.
If the bleeding bursts forth when you lift your finger from the mouth of the artery and the twig cools down, then take another twig with forceps from the twigs in the ready fire and keep doing that one after another until the blood stops.
And you should preserve, not burn a stick that may be used and cause another bleed on the ailment, and know that if blood is bleeding from an artery then it cannot be cut or especially if the artery is large except in one of four ways: either by cutting as we said, or by amputating it if it has not been severed. And if it is severed, its ends will contract and the bleeding will stop. Either bind it with tight threads or put on medicines whose purpose is to stop the blood and bind it tightly with ligatures.
But as for one who attempts to cut it with a bandage or by tight traction or placing burning objects and the like, then it does not get cut at all, unless in rare cases. If there is an exposure of that sort and it is not treated by a doctor or medicine, let him hasten to place his forefinger on the mouth of the wound itself as we have described.
And he should tightly compress it until the blood becomes constricted and flows out from above the wound, and on the artery and finger, let not cold water be removed from him always so that the blood may coagulate and become cut off. And during that time, one looks to see what kind of thread or medicine it requires.
The Second Chapter.
Concerning the incision, the cut and the cupping and wounds similar to them.
Al-Khalkh said: We have already mentioned in the First Chapter the illness in which thread is applied with fire and burning medicine, its causes and reasons and tools and forms of cauterization, and we made that into chapters from ancient times.
And I follow in this chapter the very same way as it was, so that it may be easy for the student to obtain what is required from him.
Before I begin with that, you should know, my sons, that this chapter contains more complications than what was in the First Chapter.
And because of that, it is necessary to be more cautious in this chapter, for the work in this chapter often results in hemorrhage from the blood by which life is maintained when an artery is opened or an incision is made on a tumor or abscess or surgical treatment or removal of an arrow or incision on a stone and the like, all of which are accompanied by complications and fear, and death often occurs in most of them.
And I advise you against falling into what is doubtful, for it may happen to you in this craft that there are types of people with various illnesses, among them some who have grown tired of their sickness and are resigned to death.
Those whose pus and swelling are severe, and whose condition is such that it suggests death, among them are those who give you their wealth in the hope of being cured, and their illness is a struggle. It is not fitting for you to assist any of these people at all.
Be cautious with them as much as you desire and are eager, do not proceed with anything of this kind except after a certain knowledge that leads to the good outcome which will befall them. Use in all treatment of their illnesses the precept of knowledge and warning of what will lead to safety.
For you in that is a support for gaining praise and glory, mention and thanks. May Allah guide you, oh sons of prudence, and do not prevent you from what is correct and from the guidance. That is in His hand, there is no god but Him.
And you have dealt with this chapter in the best way that has been mentioned in the chapter of the cure for what is old since ancient times, so may Allah make it easy for you to ask from him what you want.
The First Chapter.
In the treatment of water that accumulates on the heads of children.
This pus often presents to children at birth if the mother presses the child's head without gentleness and it may also be due to a hidden affliction that is unknown.
I have not seen this affliction in anyone but children, and all of them whom I saw died quickly from it. Therefore, I have seen that work is left undone with them. And I saw a child whose head was full of water and the head increases every day. Until the child was unable to sit up due to the swelling of his head and the moisture increasing, until he died.
And this moisture is either between the skin and bone or under the bone on the peritoneum. The treatment for that, if the moisture is between the skin and bone and the swelling is small, is to cut a single incision in the middle of the head from front to back until the water flows out and here is the appearance of the instrument used.
If the humidity increases and the swelling becomes greater, make it two crossing incisions in this shape:.
And if the humidity is under the bone, and its sign is that you see the seams of the head open from every side and the water drops down when you press it with your hand to inside, and not lightly on this you should make three incisions in the middle of the head like this shape:.
And after the incision, all the humidity comes out then the incisions are tied with linen and silk, and it is soaked from above with drink and oil until the fifth day, then a bandage is applied and the wound is treated with resin and ointments and you do not leave the head tightened nor feed the patient with dry food little moisture.
until the member becomes strong and healed, another way of making an incision is that you look where the bone of the swelling appears and the gathering of water because it may be in the back of the head more or in front of it or in the right or in the left.
meaning by the incision where you see the swelling and the fullness of water, so cut it as much as you can, being careful not to cut through a vessel and cause bleeding which would kill the patient with the draining of the humidity.
The Second Chapter.
Cutting the two arteries behind the ears known as the carotids.
When one of severe falls to the eyes or to the chest was presented and I timed that and it did not heal with the treatment of drugs, then the treatment in this was cutting these two arteries.
So if you wanted to cut them, you should shave the head of the patient with a razor then rub the place with a coarse cloth so that the artery appears then tie the neck of the patient with his own clothes then look where the pulse beats and their two hidden places which are behind the ears and rarely concealed except in some people.
Then teach it to him with ink, then cut them with a sharp knife cut completely to the bone and this will be at the head's width. And if you wish, insert the knife from under the artery and push it up in cuts. The length of the cuts will be about two folded fingers.
If the nerve is cut, blood will exit a pulsating and rapid flow in front of him. And if the artery does not appear to the touch, it should be measured from the ear after a measure of three fingers, then teach with ink and incise to the bone. What should be done.
The blood will send a quart on the pulsing and maybe it sent more or less all of that according to what appears to you from the strength of the artery and its fullness. Then look at the wound, if something remained from the membrane on the bone, cut it off.
So that a hot swelling is not exposed, then tighten the wound with a thread of torn linen and treat it with ointments until it heals.
Chapter Three.
Cut the arteries in the inguinal region.
If an inguinal abscess has formed in a person or sudden severe swellings from flowing liquids and heat in the muscles of the inguinal region or a severe and lasting headache and like that, and he was treated with kinds of treatment of medicine but it did not benefit him, we have tried in this illness to cut the arteries in the inguinal region or cauterize them as we described.
The procedure for cutting it is that he should shave the artery in the inguinal region, and what is meant by this is the visible artery in the groin, as its pulsation will be evident to you and rarely will it conceal itself except in a few people.
Or if it is very cold, and it has concealed itself from you, then have him draw his neck cloth tightly so that you can see the artery, and then rub the place with a cloth or dampen the area with hot water until the artery becomes clearly visible. Then the surgeon takes what he has cut from here. Then he carefully flays with it the skin until he reaches the artery, then inserts in it an instrument and pulls it up until he brings out the vessel from the skin and frees it of all the adhesions under it from every side. If the artery is thin, then he dilates it with the edge of the instrument. Then he cuts off from it a portion as much as its ends may spread apart and constrict, so that there is no bleeding. For indeed if it was not resected or severed the blood does not flow at all. Then he drains out blood from it with six or three [absorbent?] pads.
If the artery is large, it should be tied in two places with a strong double thread. The thread will be either of silk or of the tendons of the bowstring so that before the wound heals decay does not reach it and bleeding occurs.
Then cut off the excess between the ligatures. She does this either at that time or after a longer period, and if you wish to compress it tightly onto the bone with a blunt instrument until its edges are resected. It performs this action in his place or better as we said.
But if the wound is with fever or he has a bad temper because the compression helps in the destruction of moisture and it becomes more solid for benefit, then after tying the arteries, the place should be stuffed with moist lint and on top compresses are put and after healing he treats with dry medicines which make flesh grow again, with poultice until it heals God willing.
If during your work there is bleeding from the artery, then hasten to cut it off either with a clamp or fill the place with alum and bind your hand until the blood stops. If nothing comes to you, put your finger in it so that the blood clots.
Wanna al-mawd' bi'l-ma'i ash-shadi'd il-barid hatta tusakin al-hadda wa tastadhahu 'ala ma yanhaj, wa mimmahu akhaffa wa ashal min sall al-shiryan an tukwa al-'arq biha'thi al-mikwah dati'ssakinayn ba'da annata'almawadiin bil-maddad.
Wa tanzilha hamiyyan jadda hatta tublig ila'l-'azm wa ynqata' al-'arq fi mawadiin lake yataba'du ma bayna tarifihi fainnahu la yaltaham bihadih al-mikwah al-bittah, wa hazihi surat al-mikwah.
Takuu hada al-sakinayn tihsab al-mukaddati al-saghirayni illa anha takun akall hada min al-sakkin kathiran in kannatuhuma hadatin kalsaki sakkin asra' ilayhuma al-barad wa lam yinqata'l-ham bu'sran, fa in kan lahum ba'du mukaddatin amtasak fihim har al-nar.
Wa qata'ta'l-ham bu'sran, wa hazihi al-'amilu a'zhimu min kulli 'amilin wa akhaffa wa ashal, wa likin ba'da ma bayna al-sakinayn kadru ghluz al-a'sab.
Al-fuslu ar-rabi'.
Fii 'ilaji saylan ad-damu' al-harrati'd da'imah ila'l-'aynin.
Idha kana't ad-damu' da'imah wa kan saylanaha min al-'uruq allati 'ala qhaf al-ras min kharij lam yantafa'da fiha shay'an mimma yu'alli bi'l-ilaaj at-tibbi bi'al-adwiyah wa raayt wajh al-'ilal qad ahammar. Wa yuhassu fi jabinhi dibibun kada dibib al-naml wa 'aynahu mahzulatan ratti'atan qad takkalt ashfarihuma wa tashabbut ajfanahuma min hada ad-damu' fa'adzartat al-awliya' fi 'ilajiha ila hadih al-'amilu wa yusammuhu al-'ilaaj bi's-sif, wa huwa an ta'amru'l-ilal bihiyal shahr allazi fii jabinhi.
Then make three incisions parallel to each other along the forehead, with each incision being about two fingerbreadths long. The first incision should be in the middle of the forehead, running lengthwise with the nose. The second incision should be a little way from the movement of the muscle above the eyebrow, and the third incision should be on the other side.
And preserve yourself from cutting the arteries that are in the sides. Keep your hand away from the connection of the jaws, and after each incision make a distance of three fingerbreadths with a closed fist. And be sure to have with you pieces of sponge or many cloth rags so that the blood may be absorbed.
Then insert the sharp instrument into the sides, as shown in these drawings. Then insert the instrument into the incision next to the eyebrow, and peel off all the skin in between the two incisions along with the serous membrane on the bone. Then do the same thing from the middle incision to the third one, then withdraw this instrument. And also insert into the first incision another instrument called a sharp skinner from one side and a blunt one from the other side, as shown in this drawing.
And its sharp side will be directed upwards towards the skin-covered flesh, and its blunt side towards the bone. Push it until it reaches the middle incision and cut all the vessels that come from the head to the eyes without reaching the outer layer of the skin.
Then do the same thing from the middle incision to the other one. After a moderate amount of bleeding, squeeze out the clots from the cut blood vessels. Then insert a thread made of linen or cotton into each incision and apply a compress that has been soaked in wine, oil or vinegar and fat.
So that a hot abscess will not form. And on the third day, the dressing will be removed and much thread soaked in warm water will be used to tie it, then treat it with pomegranate ointment smeared with rose ointment and all that is used to treat wounds until it heals with God's will.
Chapter Five
In the treatment of tears and abscesses coming to the eyes from within the head.
When there occurs in one of them a lot of sharp abscesses which are persistent, and the eyes flow with pus from them, their vision has become weak and the conjunctivas have been ulcerated, and eyelashes have fallen out from them. And there will be in the depth of the head a sharp and severe pain, followed by a continuous headache. Know from these signs that those materials and abscesses come from many deep veins. The best treatment for this is to order the patient to blow their nostrils through their forehead then make one incision in the middle of the forehead.
And there will be in the depth of the head a sharp and severe pain, followed by a continuous headache. Know from these signs that those materials and abscesses come from many deep veins. The best treatment for this is to order the patient to blow their nostrils through their forehead then make one incision in the middle of the forehead. Or slightly elevate the skin and begin the incision from the left temple to the right temple, and the incision will reach the bone. Keep your hand far from the moving muscles of the jaws when chewing, so that if the bone is exposed and you have cleaned all the blood with a sponge.
Then separate the edges of the incision with a lint or a piece of linen thread. Then draw from above with string and soak the string in drink and oil so that there will be no hot abscess. When you have cleaned it and seen that the hot abscess has broken, you should scrape the bone until new flesh begins to form.
Then treat it with the dry remedy which makes flesh grow, like taking from barley flour two parts and from onion four parts and preparing a plaster from them, and using in growing flesh in wounds of this type.
Chapter Six
In the treatment of what falls into the ear.
All that falls into the ear is of four kinds, either a hard metal stone like iron and glass or a plant seed like sesame seeds and the like, or something liquid such as water and vinegar etc.
If it is an animal, then when a stone has fallen into the ear, whether it be a small or large stone that cannot get out of the ear, take the sun in the ear. If you see the stone only grease it with juice from the purslane plant or the Syrian plant then try to extract it by moving the head or using an aspirator tube. Close the nostrils when sneezing comes after putting a collar of wool or hair around the ear and inclining the ear upwards. Often it will come out with this treatment. If it does not come out, otherwise try to extract it with a soft sponge which is shown here.
If it comes out with the sponge, otherwise try to extract it with a soft, almost straight forceps. If it does not come out with that and then make a copper tube and insert the tip of the tube into the ear canal yes.
Close the area around the tube with a thin layer of wax ointment so that the air does not have a way other than the tube. Then pull it with your breath pulling strongly and often it will come out with this treatment. If it does not come out as we described, otherwise take from Balsam of the Nabateans or from a well-tempered resin which is taken with birds put a small amount on the tip of the spatula.
After wrapping a tight thread around it then insert it gently into the ear canal after the ear has dried out of moisture. If it does not come out with all that we described, hasten to the incision before a hot abscess or swelling occurs.
The recipe for the incision is that you cut the instrument in a mortar first and let out as much blood from it as its strength allows, then put the instrument between your hands and tilt the ear upwards and make a small incision in the root of the ear at the fatty part when it is lowest.
And the incision will be crescent-shaped until it reaches the stone then remove it with as much of the instruments as possible and stitch up the incision quickly and treat him until he recovers.
And as for if the thing that has fallen into the ear is from one of the plants that grow and swell, try to take it out with what we have mentioned. If you are unable to take it out, then take a thin, gentle lancet in this shape.
And try to cut with it the type of plant that has fallen into the ear. You do this only if you are certain that the seed has become attached by the heat of the ear until it becomes small fragments, then remove them with a blunt forceps or a soft spatula or a gentle scoop.
As we mentioned, it is easy to take it out. And as for the water that has entered the ear, it is necessary to use a syringe with a wick first, and he has filled his ear with something of soft flax and is lying on that ear which contains the water; then take it out with that.
And if not, then take a number of small stones on the smooth palms and heat them slightly with fire. The operator will insert one into his ear canal and step with one foot from that side and hit with another stone on the one in the ear.
And he will continue to do this with a stone, a stone, until all the water is gone. And sometimes the water will come out by taking from wool or one hair and putting its tip into the ear and having the other end burned in fire until most of it burns then return another hair.
He will do that several times until all the water comes out or is drawn with the syringe as mentioned in the stone. And as for removing the animal that has entered it, look; if it is small in body like a mouse and the like, remove it with what was mentioned in the division, and as for.
If its body is large and can be felt, try to take it out with a spatula and forceps and this is easier than all that enters the ear. And as for removing the worms that have generated in the ear if you treated them with what was mentioned in the division in the article of the small things and your treatment did not succeed.
Look at the ear towards the sun. If something of a worm appears, remove it with a spatula or fine tweezers. If nothing is seen, take this tube.
It is narrow at the bottom and wide at the top. Insert the thin end into the ear to the extent that the drill can hold it, then twist it strongly several times until all the worms come out. If they do not come out, seal around the tube with wax as I mentioned to you about a stone.
If they do not come out as we mentioned, use the syringes which I mentioned, and you will find that the first ones have used it to kill the worms, and it is in the treatise on syringes. Pour oil and medications into the ear with this instrument. Here is its shape:
As you see, it is made from copper or iron, narrow at the bottom with a small hole and wide at the top. If you want the pipe inside to be of iron that is strong, or if you want, take a rod and wrap cloth tightly on its end.
Then pour oil or juice or what you want from these medications into the tube which is in the ear. Then insert the rod with the cloth on its end from above and squeeze it gently with your hand until the oil goes deep inside the ear and you feel it.
With the drill inside, let what you pour into the ear have been slightly warmed in the fire. And beware that it not be very cold or very hot, for the ear cannot tolerate that.
The Seventh Chapter.
In the treatment of the stoppage opposing to the ear.
Some children may come out from their mothers' wombs with their ears unperforated.
And also some people may have a stoppage in the passage of the ear from an injury or flesh growth within it, and this stoppage can be deep inside the hole of the ear that cannot be seen with the eye.
And he may show a little outside the puncture and be seen with the eye, for what shows in depth of the ear and is not seen with the eye will be in most cases difficult to remove, and that which can be seen should have the patient's ear put into the sun. And you look at it; if you see a membrane visible then open it with a fine syringe, this is its appearance:.
It has one end with some protrusion a little limited in some of it and the rest of the syringe is smooth on both sides so as not to hurt the ear. If the membrane from flesh had grown in the passage of the ear, then grasp it with a fine forceps and cut it off gently until all the flesh is removed.
If the membrane is in depth of the ear, then take a fine malleable object smooth it, heat it slightly in the fire and insert it into the passage of the ear. If you feel the membrane with what the patient feels from heaviness of hearing then file it gently.
And be careful not to injure the auditory nerve, then insert into the ear a thread as large as the size of the puncture that you tied in the Egyptian ointment. Do this for several days until you are certain about closing the wound or take a thread and dip it in water and sprinkle on it powdered alum.
And use it. If you see the ear has become inflamed and a hot abscess, then you should remove the thread and replace it with another thread that you tied in rose gum so that the hot abscess calms down, then treat it until it clears up.
If bleeding occurs, then soak a sponge or cloth in cold water and place it on the ear and apply the rest of the treatment that stops the mentioned bleeding in the chapter of cauterizations.
The eighth chapter.
In the treatment of blisters that appear on the vulva.
These blisters that appear on the eyelids may be watery and dry; it is necessary to grasp them with a pincer or forceps and cut them out from their origins, then apply powdered zaja on the place.
If it bleeds from them, cover it with a soft lentil-like cotton wool and it is better to wash it after cutting; often it returns if something remains of its origins, and when it is burned with fire those origins are burnt out and do not return.
The Ninth Chapter.
In the treatment of conjunctivitis that appears on the eyes.
Often something similar to cold in its severity and softness is presented on the eyelids.
And so it was called the cold, which is a gathering of thick moisture in the upper eyelid and lower eyelid; and in its treatment look at it: if the cold appears prominent on the surface of the eyelid move towards one direction or another then the matter is easy: incise it with an incision from outside.
Then gently scrape it from all sides until it is eliminated, then tie it with forceps and cut it out. If you are not prepared to cut it except after the eyelid has been perforated by the incision, that will not harm the patient at all; if the incision was large, gather it together with a suture and treat it until he heals.
And if it is small, do not worry about it; the ointment will hold it and heal it. And if the cold is leaning towards the inner surface of the eyelid towards the inside surface, turn over the eyelid and tie the cold with forceps without needing to make an incision and scrape it from all sides.
And if the eyelid perforated by cutting, that will not harm anything; then wash the eye with salt water after cutting the cold and treat the place with what heals until the patient recovers.
Chapter Ten.
In the treatment of corneal ulcers that are exposed in the eyelid.
The corneal ulcer is a growth that occurs in the upper layers of the eyelid, and it most often affects children, who are weighed down by their eyelids and exposed to eye infections from dust, and they cannot look towards the light of the sun. So that tears may rush to them.
So they always lie on their faces and sleep with tears streaming down, and their eyelids are moist under the eyebrows, puffed up, and if you press the place with your fingers, you will feel the corneal ulcer between them, and the way to treat it is for the doctor to put his nose close.
Then take a flaxen cloth and prepare an ember from it, and make from that ember a circle of the same size as what encircles the corneal ulcer on all sides, then place it on it and compress with your fingers from all sides so that the corneal ulcer gathers in the center of the circle.
Then cut in the middle of that moisture with a sharp scalpel cut, and it should not be larger than the cut which is made in an incision, but as for depth, you should cut all the skin until you reach the corneal ulcer.
Then in most cases, the corneal ulcer will protrude from the cut in the shape of a piece of white fat, you should draw it out with a cloth that you have wrapped around your fingers outside and as you turn your hand right and left until it is removed, and beware of increasing the incision lest the scalpel touches the eye and harms it.
If the corneal ulcer does not protrude from the cut at first, then it is necessary to increase the incision a little gently until it emerges, then pull it out as we said, and then dip a cloth in vinegar and water and place it on the place and bind it with a bandage, and some people crush salt.
Put it in the cavity of the incision so that what remains of that moisture will dissolve, then treat him until he is clear. If an ulcerous sore occurs in the place, cure him with soothing poultices until he clears up.
The Eleventh Chapter.
In kinds of eye bandaging.
If a growth occurs in the eyelid, excessive hairs outside of their natural course under the normal hairs and I pluck them out, for they harm the eye and cause types of disease such as permanent tears, laxity of the palpebrae, white spots, and thickening until that becomes a reason for blindness of the eye.
Eye bandaging is done in four ways, either by cauterizing with fire or by the hot medicine as mentioned in the chapter on cauterization, or that the bandaging be by stitches and sewing or with reeds as I remember.
You should place the tip of the needle in your hand then turn the eyelid with your left hand, if it turns over and so on, else you insert a thread into the lower eyelid and guide the needle through from above, and it will be near the hair itself, and pull the thread up with the eyelid.
