You turn it over with the roller then cut in the inside of the eyelid, without the excess hair, with a sharp blade from the larger opening to the smaller one, then you guide the thread and put under the eyelid a small pad of cotton or a cloth, then stitch on the eyelid with a needle.
Like the shape of a paper mulberry leaf, but it should be shaped to your liking in raising the eyelid because people differ in that, so some may need you to cut from the eyelid an appropriate amount, according to how much the eyelid has relaxed.
And some may need you to cut less, all that according to the relaxation of the eyelid, then you sew with a blade along the two stitches I made and start from the larger opening to the smaller one, and the single incision will be near the natural hair like the thickness of the roller.
Then insert the pincers into one of the skin corners, then peel off all of it. Then gather the lips with a needle and fine wool thread and clean the blood and seal what remains of the threads on the eyebrows with something that adheres.
If you wish to do so and otherwise do not care, then the stitching and threads will remain for three or four days, then treat it, and if you wish leave the wound without stitching and treat it with what dries and contracts. The eyelid rises when the wound is closed and joined together, and stitching is better.
This face from the cataract I have mentioned that the old ones have described, except that there is a burden on the eye lid and it is one of good works and no danger in it. And another face in the cataract also that you learn a shape on the eyelid like the shape of an aspen leaf as we have described. Then lift the eyelid with three pincers that are separate or grouped in this shape:.
Then cut what remains of the eyelid with a small scissors as shown, cuts gently.
If you cannot hold the pincers and it is not firm for you, then take a needle with thread and insert it in the middle of the shape and insert another thread near the larger corner and a third thread near the smaller corner and gather between your fingers the threads gently then lift up your hand gently.
Then lift up the skin that has been learned on it all as we have described, then gather the lips of the wound with stitching and treat it until it heals. If there is a red and hot pimple at the place you cut or opened, calm down that pimple with calamine and similar soothing ointments.
And the lower eyelid may also turn its lashes over, it is necessary that you apply to it what we have mentioned from cutting and stitching and cauterizing with fire and hot medicine and cauterizing with fire or hot medicine more effective and lighter on the eye than cutting and stitching in both of them.
Cleaning with reeds is done in this manner: you turn the eyelid and cut the incision from inside as I have described, then make two or three thin rods of equal length to the eyelid and less in width than that of the knife.
And I have made on the ends of each of them, from both sides where the threads cling, then brought them together gently upon what remained of the eyelid and tightened the rods from both sides tightly and left them for some days; because the tightened skin dies and blackens and decays.
Until it falls away by itself; if I delayed, then I cleaned it with the mortar and treated it until it healed. If there was adhesion, the eyelid rose and the lashes of the eye did not fall out. This is the shape and size of the rods that are made in this way.
The Twelfth Chapter.
On elevating the eyelashes that have fallen from the eye with a needle.
If it is a hair or two that the operation is for, take a fine needle and insert into it a thread of fine silk that has been smoothed out, then tie its ends tightly in a very gentle knot; let its length be about the length of a finger.
Then pass another fine thread under the knot in the needle and tie its ends if you wish, then place the needle on your hand close to the sun so that it can be seen clearly; because it is a delicate operation. Then insert the needle with the thread into the root of the excessive hair.
And perform it within the eyelid with the drill until it comes out from above the natural hair, then pull the thread up over the knot and insert into that knot the hair if it is one or two or three at most.
Then pull your hand with it until the hair comes out with the thread within the eyelid along with the natural hair. If you pulled the thread and did not bring the hair with it, then pull the thread downwards with the silk thread that you made in the needle until the thread comes out through the upper hole.
Then you redo the hair in it and pull them, do that until they rise in the upper hole and you see it with your eye. Then release the ligatures and the thread and take it out and pull the eye and leave it tightened for two or three days until the hair takes its place and flesh grows on it.
If the hair is short, either add to it a long hair from natural hair so that it rises with it or leave it until it grows after a period of time. Then raise it.
The Thirteenth Chapter.
In the treatment of scarring that occurs in the upper eyelid of the eye.
The one that is exposed to this scarring is called an eye twitch and this scarring is either natural or adventitious, the adventitious being from the spread of a wound or cut or tear and the like.
And the manner of treatment is to cut that stratum and separate its edges and make a thread from linen and tie it until it heals, and it should not be treated with things that dry and contract.
If you did that, the scarring returned in a more severe form than it was, but if you used things that swell like soap and gum with water that has been poured into it, and an ointment of diachylon mixed with something from paint and dyed on the thread and treated with it.
And the goal of treating it is to strive with all effort that it does not stick together in its original shape, and this operation which we mentioned is only some repair of the scarring, not that the place returns to its former shape at all.
The Fourteenth Chapter.
In the treatment of scarring that occurs in the lower eyelid.
This scarring which occurs from the lower part is what is called a scar and it is either natural or adventitious, the adventitious being from a wound or cut or tear and the like.
The method of performing it is to take a needle with two threads and pierce the flesh, then carry the needle from the left side to the right side until the thread reaches both ends of the flesh. Then raise the flesh with the needle and cut it off with a wide scissors.
If the fold of the eyelid returns to its proper form, otherwise take a spatula and place it on the site of the incision and turn with it the eyelid and make two cuts inside the eyelid so that their ends meet and thus form an angle. Until they meet, its shape will be similar to this shape:.
And it will resemble the Greek letter lambda. Then remove that flesh as much as its sharp edge is below what follows the eyelid, then gather the scattered parts with two stitches and sew him with a wool thread. Then treat him with the mentioned ointments and plaster until he heals.
And if the cleft has been exposed from a cut or stitch or knot, then it is necessary to make a small incision without cutting off the eyelashes as mentioned above. Then spread between the lips with a plaster as we have mentioned.
And in the treatment of a cleft whether from above or below, one should proceed according to what is available for its appearance. For it may have many differences in form, and the craftsman finds a way to deal with it as best he can.
Until its shape returns to its natural form or approaches it, and the same disease guides you on what is suitable for him in terms of treatment and tool in most cases.
The Fifteenth Chapter.
For the adhesion of the eyelid to the lacrimal or to the canaliculus.
This adhesion may be exposed to many people so that the upper eyelid adheres to the whiteness of the eye, preventing it from moving easily and hindering it in its natural actions. It is necessary to insert the tip of a spatula under the eyelid.
She places it above or with a gentle curette, then cuts the adhesion with a fine syringe so that the cut is not sharp like the cutting of the curette, lest the surgeon be disturbed and the curette slips out, harming the eye. Your cut should be as though you are scraping off that adhesion.
She waits until the eyelid returns to its natural state and the adhesion is completely gone, then she pours into the eye a salty water which cleanses it with that or injects into it from the zinc calamus dissolved in water, then she spreads between the eyelid and the eye with a cotton thread.
She places above the eye wool moistened with egg white, and after the third day she uses the saturated syringes until it clears.
The 16th Chapter.
For cutting the nail plate and the flesh of the paronychium.
The nail plate is either sensitive and resembles a thin hard spike, or not sensitive and resembles a frozen white dampness which becomes solid if touched with iron or taken with the curette it will be cut.
And a curette is not placed in it, and both kinds start from the larger paronychium until it spreads a little bit to cover the observer and prevent light and eye movement, and the way of working in cutting them is that the surgeon places his head in your hand.
Then he opens his eyes and you lift the eyelid with your hand, then you catch the nail plate with a gentle curette and stretch it upwards, then you take a needle and insert into it a hair from a horse or cow and strong thread, and bend the tip of the needle slightly and push it into the middle of the nail plate.
She carries it out with the needle and ties it with a strong thread, then stretches it upwards and scrapes with the hair the side of the nail plate which is next to the pupil as if she were spreading it with the hair until its end, then cuts the rest at the root of the paronychium with a fine syringe or small scissors and leaves the natural flesh of the paronychium.
Oh no! If it does not expose the cut of constant bleeding, then the nail plate is probed with a file and wire alone as we said before. Then it is peeled off with a smooth lancet on that end whose picture is shown here:.
And it is guarded that the lancet should touch the conjunctiva, and a fistula would occur, so tears would flow. Then after cutting, something of powdered salt or zingiber root powder is put in the eye and left until another day, then treated as it needs until it clears up.
If the nail plate is not sensitive and an injection needle cannot be inserted into it, nor can a file be fixed in it, then this type of nail plate is often treated with medicines until it clears up as I described in the section. And if you want to cut it, open the eye of the patient.
Take a smooth and soft lancet with a light edge as shown here:. And peel the nail plate off with it gently from above. If you see that it is becoming loose and breaking apart, and the peeling has only affected the surface, then instill something of zingiber root powder or red pepper powder or powdered salt into the eye, and close the eye until another day.
Then, reapply the treatment to it until all of them are gone, unless a hot pimple is formed in the eye; then leave it and treat the hot pimple until it clears up. Then, reapply the treatment to it with the peeling until it clears up. As for the thickening of the eyelid skin.
For if the thickening is painful to the eye, then bind that thickening with a file and cut some of it away, do not be precise in cutting so that a constant bleeding does not occur. Then sprinkle in the corners zingiber root powder or red pepper powder until it clears up.
The 17th Chapter.
In cutting away purulent growths and what springs from excess flesh in the eye.
There may grow in the eyes of some people red flesh-like tissue until it covers or comes close to or overflows onto the eyelids and perhaps the lids turn outward resembling a rose's thorn.
And as for the treatment, have the patient sit with his head on your knee then open his eyes and catch all that red flesh with suitable forceps.
Or take hold of it with a needle or spatula then cut the first bit after the other until all of it is completely removed from the eye and preserved from harming it, and your cutting into it can be either with the razor that we described in removing nails or with a small scissors. As for cutting off what protrudes from the eyelid in a similar way to how you cut away the threads as shown in the chapter on that, which is below this one.
If you have cut it and all the purulent growth has gone, then fill the eye with ground salt or scatter red powder-like drugs in it and place a piece of white linen from outside over the eye to prevent the hot swelling.
But if some purulent growth remains and bleeding occurs and you fear the hot swelling, then leave the eye alone and treat it with what calms the swelling, then go back to it and do the operation again until it clears up, and likewise act similarly with the excess flesh that protrudes in the eye of this kind.
Unless it is fitting for you to avoid treating any weak eye either by nature or exposure with ironwork and not insert your hand in anything of this type of work until you see that the organ is capable of that operation.
The 18th Chapter.
In cutting away threads from the eye.
Threads are red blood vessels that weave on the eye of whoever is prevented from seeing, and weaken the eye with the passing days. It is fitting for you to look first; if the eye in which there are threads is strong and there is no other disease except the threads.
So then, the laceration; that is to say, order the patient to place his head in your lap. Then tie these veins together with a single or double forceps as you see fit. The forceps will be gentle in curvature like this:
Or they may be two double forceps in one body like this:
Then catch those veins with a gentle pincer, gently and wipe out the blood little by little until you see that the eye has gone of them and the bleeding has stopped. Be careful not to harm the eye with the ends of the pincer. May your work be half the day in front of the sun.
And be very careful in your work so that you do not cut other than those veins. When you are finished, insert into the eye a green or red blade to eat up whatever is left of the blood vessels. If you cannot cut them all in that time, compress the eye with what soothes the pain of the eye.
And leave it for a few days until the pain subsides and the warm swelling goes away. Then repeat the same operation on it with the same eye until the marks of the pincer are erased from it.
And leave it [and the patient's head will be in the apprentice's lap and the other one wiping away tears and examining the anterior and posterior part of the eye]. The original intention in this work is to open the eye with openings that are stable or triangular which the apprentice holds.
Hold and the patient's head will be in the apprentice's lap and the other one wiping away tears and examining the anterior and posterior part of the eye. By choice start the laceration from the top or bottom of the eye, and the first is to have two forceps in the upper eyelid, one at the end and the other at the beginning.
And hold them between the eyebrows and the bridge of the nose, then tie forceps under them, then hold them between the canthi and the plica and pull your hand gently until you see all the vessels have risen. Cut the smaller vessel on the side if it has been caught by the pincer or the gentle probe.
A patient should be sewn up on the eyebrow and all paths cleared so that he may be raised above the lint. But do not cut the bandage for, the tears and blood will become sticky on it.
Then cut with scissors from above and below what is in excess of the lint, so that there will not remain anything but on the gauze. If you can raise him up on the gauze, sew with the meht that it is better, and it may be easier for some people.
If you have to cut him, let him stay for a few days to bleed and rest from the swelling, then return to work on him.
The 19th Chapter.
For the removal of an arrow from the nose.
Physicians call the arrow "Nasura" if it is treated with the strongest or hottest medicine as previously described, and it does not clear up. Then one should cut through the swelling when it becomes hardened and remove all moisture inside or filth.
Until the bone is revealed, if the bone is revealed and you see in it decay or discoloration then remove it with an instrument such as this shape:.
And it is called the "Kashn" (or) head of the skull, made from Indian iron, its head being twisted like a vessel, on which you have engraved the engraving or scraping of the file or scullery in fine script. You put it on the place of decay from the bone then turn it between your fingers and you rub your hand slightly until you know that the decay has been removed.
And you do this several times then strengthen the place with dried and adhesive medicines. If the place is sealed, flesh has grown on it and the wound has healed after forty days without any repetition or ulceration or new event happening in it.
Therefore know that he has been cured, otherwise there is no remedy except to return the arrow to its original hole in this manner: by exposing the bone again with iron or hot medicine. If the bone is exposed then take a wick on this shape:.
The edge of the instrument will be triangular and its handle cone-shaped, curved towards the end as you see. Then place it on the bone itself; this is near the middle and a little further from the eye than your hand. Move your hand with the reamer until it penetrates the bone and you feel it with your sense.
So if the pus comes out of it when he holds his hand on its nostril, then at that time press the place with sticking and dried medicines as I have taught you. If the flesh grows back and the place hardens, then the material which was directed outside will return to the nostril and that will be lighter for the patient if Allah wishes.
The Twentieth Chapter.
In the root of the eyelid.
If the eyelid becomes swollen with its whole part and does not cause any defect or loss in the sight, it is necessary that the instrument be smoothed out then separated from the calotte. Then put a compress on the socket without any condition and moisten it with a thin bandage.
Then put on the eye a poultice made from vinegar, myrrh, and galbanum, and saffron. Then pull the eye upwards on the poultice with great benefit. The recipe for the compress is to take many linen cloths and fold each one into four folds to make many of them.
Then put them one on top of the other as much as the eye needs, then pull a firm cloth tightly over it with a strong draw. Then repeat the compress with a bandage without any condition. Then remove the compress and leave the eye pulled upwards for a day and night.
If the bandage relaxes during that time, it should be tightened again. Then remove the bandage after a day and night as we said. If you see the eye has returned to its place, otherwise redo the poultice, compress, tightening, and bandage until it returns.
Chapter Twenty-One.
In cutting the tendons.
If a hernia appears in the tendon layer, and it bulges out outside the abdomen like a walnut and its appearance is like that of a human, because of which you wish to cut it, then do as I have described.
And you enter a needle from below to above into the core of the walnut, and then another needle with a doubled thread from the incision site, and pass it through while leaving the first needle in place.
Then cut the place of bending of the doubled thread, and tie some of the walnut around the needle, and pull it tight then bring out the needle and put a wool soaked in egg white on the eye, and leave it until the threads fall with the walnut, then treat the eye with what will strengthen it.
Until the wound heals, and you may tie the walnut from all sides with a bandage in a circle so that the eye becomes very swollen, then bathe it with a thin cotton swab reaching into the depths of the eye so that the egg white liquid flows down and the eye becomes calm then tighten it until it heals.
Chapter Twenty-Two.
In treating cataracts.
This disease which is called cataracts, is a liquid that gathers in the eye, similar to pouring water without any, and the work in this case is that you sit the patient on a chair elevated then take their head with your hands from both sides.
And move it until you see the liquid descend below with your eye, then fix it and it does not go away, and the light passes and the patient sees things as he used to see them, and if it did not descend below as we mentioned, know that it is water, and if it was not ready for descent as we mentioned.
And if not, then sit the patient in front of you, and take a thin probe and cut it with it slightly above the corneal membrane at the point where the crystalline lens meets the corneal membrane in the pupil until the liquid comes out.
If only water has been emitted in the eye, hot water mixed with aloe or water that has been heated with opium and aloe is used to treat it until it clears up.
Chapter Twenty-Third.
We have mentioned the kinds of water in the classification, and which one is suitable for the hollow with a detailed explanation so that it is taken from there on health. Therefore, when this happens, the patient should sit facing you, raised up near the light near the sun.
She ties the healthy eye with a clean cloth and tightens it tightly, then she raises the eyelid of the affected eye with her left hand if the affected eye is the left one or with her right hand if the affected eye is the right one.
Then she places the tip of the hollow near the conjunctiva with a blunt forceps in the same plane as the eye, from the side of the smaller pupil. Then she pushes the hollow strongly while turning it with her hand until it penetrates into the white of the eye and she feels that the hollow has reached something empty.
It is necessary that the hollow should go as far as the depth of the eye from the surface to the black part, which is the conjunctiva of the eye, because copper is seen by the observer in the same plane as the white of the eye due to the transparency of the corneal membrane. Then the hollow goes up towards the place where the water is.
Then she holds it down a few times, if the water has come out of its container then the patient sees what is opened in front of her with her sight and the hollow in her eye, then she sits quietly. If the water rises again, then let it go down again without taking the hollow out.
If it settles and does not rise, then take out the hollow gently while you are relaxing your hand a little bit at a time. Then dissolve some pure salt powder in the water and wash the eye from inside with it. Then put all of the surrounding area around the eye soaked or woolen.
A white and smooth vein, which is tied up with a healthy eye. As for us and the people of our time, we place on it a well-pressed poultice along with the whiteness of the egg. If the cup does not enter into the eye due to its hardness because there are people whose eyes are very hard. It is necessary that you take the scraper which is called the "braid" whose shape is this:.
You should puncture with it the conjunctiva itself only, and do not be precise about the puncture, rather just reach the cupping vessel to a soft place then enter the cup as we have mentioned. And when you have finished your task prepare for sleep lying down firmly on your back in a dark room.
He will abstain from all movements and coughing, and let his food be what naturally softens it, and do not let him move his head to the right or left at all, and the bandage will remain in its state until the third day, then remove him to that dark room and try his sight.
She will try to see things, then return the bandage until the seventh day, and it is not desirable that you do this during the treatment or after cupping from your time, but rather should avoid doing so before the water rises quickly with a severe look.
If there is a red and hot lump, then you should uncover the eye before the seventh day and correct that with what soothes the lump until it subsides, if it subsides, then release his sight and put a cloth on his face to gradually acclimate him to seeing through it for some days while he is in that dark room then.
He will go out of the house gradually and behave in his affairs, and know that cupping is not accomplished without the student seeing it some times, then he proceeds to work, and I have been informed about some Iraqis that they mentioned making a cupped vessel which is inflated to absorb water.
I have not seen anyone in our land who has made this, nor read it in any of the first books. It may be an innovation, and these are images of types of catheters so that one may stand on them due to their ignorance:.
It is made from copper specifically and its tip has this very texture, triangular with a sharp end.
The Twenty-Fourth Chapter.
For the treatment of flesh that grows in the nose.
It may grow in the nose different kinds of flesh, some resembling scorpions with many legs, and some being a cancerous flesh that is hardened in color, and from it some being a fatty flesh not hardened in color.
As for the flesh that is fatty and not malignant or cancerous, you should sit in front of a window facing the sun, open your nostril and insert the forceps into that flesh, then pull it out and cut with a sharp thin lancet from one side what you have reached of it.
Until you know that all the flesh has been removed, if there remains something that you could not cut it, then scrape it with one of the gentle instruments gently until nothing is left. If blood or a hot abscess breaks out.
Then meet it with what is appropriate, or if it is from the malignant ulcers, then be quick and insert until the blood is cut off and all the flesh goes away, then insert into the nose after cutting a powder of vinegar or water or a liquid, for if the nose opens up and moisture flows to the throat.
Then know that he has been cured, if the moisture does not pass as it should then know that inside him is a growing flesh in the hollowed bones which the tool did not reach by cutting to it. So now you should take a cord of cotton with some thickness.
And make knots in it many times and put between each knot a length of a finger or less. The surgeon will insert the end of one cord into his nose with a probe or whatever he can, after having made it like threads and draw out its breath until it reaches the pharynx.
He comes out on his nose and many times does like this boy's action, which is easy for one who wants it, then the ends of the thread are gathered, the end which came out in the mouth and the other that remained in the nostril.
Then the flesh is spread with the knot that is in the thread until you know that the flesh has been cut by the thread's knot, then the thread is removed and it is inserted into the nostril after wiping away the blood a string that I have absorbed in the Arabic ointment, you do this for three days or more.
Until the ointment is eaten all that remains of the flesh, then the last thing in the nostril becomes a lead tube for some days until it heals. If needed to be treated, I dried and used it.
And this is the image of the catheter with which the pomades and medicines are poured into the nostril:.
He places a small candle-shaped thing made of brass or copper, open at one end and having a channel likewise.
And if you wanted, make the tube closed like a trumpet and grease the catheter smooth.
It has a handle at its end as you see, holding it if you grease with fat or any of the strings or things that are elastic.
The 25th chapter.
In nasal polyps that grow on the tip of the nose.
Many times a polyp grows at the end of the nose, it becomes large and increases with time until its appearance is ugly.
Therefore, it should be cut in its first appearance and all of it removed, then carry either the caustic or the burning medicine which acts as a caustic on the place. If its cutting is late until it becomes large, look if it is hardened stiff like burnt skin with little sensation.
Do not expose it to iron, for it is a cancerous tumor; and I have often seen that when this tumor has been cut out from him, a large abscess has returned on his owner. And if the tumor is soft in texture and pale in color, as I have observed, then cutting can be done entirely. Let the physician drain it and cut it out without caution or delay, and treat the site with what dries and constricts until it heals.
Chapter Twenty-Sixth.
In stitching the nose, cheek and ear. If the connection of its parts is loosened due to an injury or something similar, know that when this loosening has occurred in one of these cavities, few are those from whom successful treatment can be achieved except for some people.
When one of these things is presented, look and see if the wound is bloody; then gather the edges of the wound with sutures and treat it until it heals. And if the loosening has caused the two sides to separate and each side is healthy in itself, then you should scrape off the surface of each side with a skin scraper until it bleeds.
Then gather the two sides with sutures and tighten them, and sprinkle on it the zinc and linseed powder mixed together. And put over it a plaster of the thin ointment or some other adhesive ointment and leave it tightened for two or three days then remove it.
And replace the treatment and leave it until the threads come out by themselves, then treat it with ointment until it heals. The recipe for suturing is to gather the loosening of connection either with needles as we have described in stitching the abdomen or with thread as I have explained to you there.
Chapter Twenty-Seventh.
On removing the abscess that appears in the lips.
Many people have small hard nodules in the inside of their cheeks, some similar to a wooden splinter and some smaller or larger. The cheek should be turned and a suture placed on each nodule and attached to the bandage.
She cuts it from all sides then fills the place after cutting with powdered alum until the bleeding stops, and compresses with vinegar and salt and treats the places as for burns until the wounds heal.
The 28th chapter.
For cutting excess flesh in the mouth.
Often a redundant flesh grows on the gum, which the ancients called Abalus. It should be tied with a bandage or held with tweezers and cut at its root; then the bleeding stops and powdered alum is placed on the place.
Or any of the dry and hard growths; if that flesh returns after treatment, it often comes back again. So cut it a second time and eat it, for it will not return after being eaten.
The 29th chapter.
For extracting teeth with iron.
There may form on the surfaces of the teeth from within and without, and between the gums rough and foul scabs which may rot and turn yellow and green until their decay reaches the gum and spoils the teeth.
So sit the dentist in front of you, with his head in your lap and extract the molar and tooth from which the scabs and things resembling dust have appeared until nothing remains. And also do this with the yellow and green and other colors until it is purified.
If what is extracted from the first extraction is gone, then re-extract it again and again for a second and third time until your goal is reached. And know that a molar often needs different types of extractions with many shapes according to what suits your work.
In order that the tooth which is cleaned from within by the cleanser may be cleaned differently than the one which is cleaned from without, and different than the ones which are between teeth in another shape. These many cleansers should all be prepared with you:.
The Thirty-Fifth Chapter.
In the removal of teeth.
You should treat the tooth from its cause with every trick and delay its removal, for it is a noble substance, even if its removal is necessary.
So when the practitioner decides to remove the tooth, it should be steady until the pain of the tooth has subsided. For often the practitioner is deceived by the pain and thinks it to be in a healthy tooth, so he removes it then the pain does not go until the diseased tooth is removed, as we have seen that done many times by the barber-surgeons.
If the pain of the tooth is in a healthy state with it, then it should be surrounded around the gum with a forceps that has some strength until the gums are relieved from all sides, then move it gently at first a little bit, a little bit, so as to loosen it.
Then the forceps can grasp it strongly, and the practitioner's head between his knees has been set down not to move then pull out the tooth straight so that it is not cracked. If it does not come out, or else take one of those instruments and insert it under him from all sides gently and a motion in moving it as was done at first.
And if the tooth is perforated or loose, it should be filled with a cloth and sealed well with a thin end of a thread so that it does not come out in when you grasp it with forceps and you should investigate by probing around the gum from all sides.
Be careful with your effort, lest it be wasted and some of it rebound on the patient in a more severe way than his original condition. And beware of doing what ignorant manipulators do in their bridges and approaches to it, without using what we have described.
For often they cause great hurts on people that are easier to heal if the tooth had broken and its roots remained all or some of them. Or that he extracts with some of the jawbone, as we have seen many times, then he stuffs it afterwards with a drink or a concoction of vinegar and salt; and if bleeding occurs from the place, it often happens that it ceases after having taken something from the pus and filled with it the place.
And if the poultice did not benefit you, then take an ivory file, like these smooth calabashes which move the tooth first. Its shape will be long in the branches, short in the handle, thick so that it does not bend when you grip with it on the tooth. And this is the shape of the large files:.
It will be as you see, thick in the handles so that if you grip them firmly they do not slip and do not bend. And it should be of Indian steel or of carefully tempered iron, with the branches well-forged at their ends, each one entering into the other; and then grasp them tightly and securely.
And the branches can be made like the shape of a file so that they are also strong in gripping.
The 83rd Chapter.
On the extraction of tooth roots and removal of broken jawbones.
If the root of the tooth remains, having been cracked during its extraction, it is necessary to put on the place a poultice with grease for a day or two until the place relaxes, then enter into it the file or calabash. The one that resembles its parts is the mouth of the bird called Balurja and this is an image of the Kullaib.
It is made like a rasp from the inside or like an Eskefaj, and if it does not give you relief to exit with this Kullaib then you should drill on the axis and expose all the flesh with a probe, then insert the instrument that resembles the handle of a small flute, which is its image.
Short and thick at the end, it should not be sharpened lest it break. If the axis is removed with that then otherwise take the other instrument whose image is this, the first one is triangular at the end with some thickness.
A gentle-looking image of a triangular one.
And we also make use of this instrument with two horns, whose image is also this.
And other instruments and flasks that have been mentioned in the inventory of abscesses, and we also make use of this instrument which resembles a large pincers, whose image is this.
Triangular at the end, with some thickness little by little lest it break, and not be sharpened. And know that instruments of abscesses are many as well as all other instruments which cannot be counted, and the skilled craftsman with his cleverness may invent for himself instruments according to what the work and diseases themselves indicate.
Because among the diseases, that which was not mentioned by the ancients is an instrument for its different kinds, then if a bone from the jaw or one of the bones of the mouth has broken or rotted, you search for it in its place with any of these instruments and Kullaib that were mentioned in removing axes.
And we make use of this instrument, whose image is shaped like a scoop.
There is some thickness in it little by little so that the bone is adjusted with it, lest the bone escapes until the bone comes out, and we treat the place with the suitable medicines for that. If the bone has a slight decay then strip it of its decay and rust until it is clean, then treat it until it heals.
Chapter Twenty-fourth.
In the treatment of suppurating swellings that have developed elsewhere.
The swellings, if they have erupted in an unnatural way, become ugly and are especially so when this occurs in women or servants; one should take a look, and if the swelling has appeared behind another tooth.
And it is not possible to drain or to stop it, then tie him up; and if it is adhering to another tooth, cut it off with this instrument whose shape is this:.
It resembles a small pointed beak and should be made of an Indian steel, very sharp at the end; it is best to cut with it for many days so that the tooth becomes hard and so that other teeth are not disturbed. And if it is erupting and has been drained, then drain it by means of a file from Indian steel will have this shape.
It is all from Indian steel, and the engraving on it is very fine, resembling a file with which needles are made; it cools the tooth little by little over many days with great gentleness so that the tooth does not become dislodged and fall out, then grasp it again and scrape it off with some forceps.
And if a tooth has cracked off some of it and is painful when speaking, then one should cool it as well so that the pain of the crack will go away, and become even and smooth, so that it does not hurt the tongue or spoil speech.
Chapter Thirty-third.
In wiring moving teeth with threads of silver or threads of gold.
If the front teeth become loose and move with a blow or fall, and the patient cannot grasp anything to eat lest they fall out, and having treated them with adhesive remedies did not cure in that.
The trick is to tie with a thread of gold or silver, and gold is better because silver tarnishes and becomes rotten after some days, while gold remains unchanged always. The thread should be of medium thickness on the softness and thickness according to what fits between the teeth.
The picture of welding, that you take the thread and insert its bend between the two healthy molars then sew with the ends of the thread between the mobile teeth one or more until the sewing reaches the other molar from the other side.
Then return the sewing to the side from which you started and hold your hand gently and wisely until it does not move at all, and your thread should be tight at the roots of the teeth so that it does not come loose, then cut the ends of the thread with pincers and join them together and twist them and hide them between the healthy molar and the mobile tooth.
So that the tongue is not irritated, then leave it like this stretched as long as it remains, if it comes undone or breaks its stitches, redouble them with another thread and you will enjoy them like this for all eternity, and this is the picture of the teeth and the condition of the welding in two healthy molars and two mobile molars as you see:.
And the single molar or both may fall into their place and be welded as we have described and remain, but this is done by a skilled craftsman, and he may carve a bone from cattle bones to make it in the shape of the tooth and put it in the place where the tooth has fallen. And he sews as we said and it remains and he enjoys that.
The Thirty-fourth Chapter.
For cutting the ligament which is exposed under the tongue in those who prevent speech.
It may be that this ligament which is exposed under the tongue is either natural born with man or it may be an accidental one from a wound that has healed.
And the procedure for it is that you open the patient's mouth and his head in your lap, then lift up his tongue and cut that nervous ligament with a lancet until the tongue is released from its grasp. If there is some hardness and complexity within it and that was from a wound having healed, then insert a drill into it and cut it with a lancet until the ligament becomes loose and the knot unravels.
Beware that the incision be in depth of the flesh so as to cut vessels there, and thus cause bleeding; then apply compress in effect of the cut with rosewater or vinegar and cold water, then place under the tongue a thread of linen which the barber holds every night.
Lest it become sealed over again, for if there be bleeding of blood, then place on the spot Zaja crushed; and if the blood overwhelms you, bind the place with a lens-shaped compress suited to that. Then treat him with the rest of the treatment until he recovers.
The Thirty-Fifth Chapter.
For the removal of the toad born under the tongue.
It may occur under the tongue a swelling resembling the small toad which prevents the tongue from performing its natural act and perhaps becomes as large as to fill the mouth; and the treatment is that the barber opens his mouth opposite the sun and looks at the swelling.
If he sees it swollen, of a black or dark colour, hard and having no sensation for the barber, do not handle him; for it is cancer. But if it inclines to whiteness and contains moisture, then insert in it the forceps and cut it with a sharp knife, freeing him from all sides.
If the blood overwhelms you in the time of your treatment, place on it crushed Zaja until the bleeding ceases, then go back to your treatment until you remove it completely, and then apply compress with vinegar and salt.
Then treat him with the rest of the suitable treatment until he recovers.
The Thirty-Sixth Chapter.
For the treatment of swelling of the tonsils.
And whatever grows in the throat from other tumours may expose within the throat glands resembling the glands which are exposed from outside called tonsils if they were treated with what I mentioned in the section, but they did not recover.
If it is a hard tumor, its color is pale and unresponsive to touch, do not treat it with iron. If it is red in color and its origin is thick, do not treat it with iron either, lest you cause bleeding. Rather, leave it until it ripens; it will either become soft or burst of itself.
If it is white in color and curved, and its origin is thin, this is what should be cut. The procedure for this is to look before operating, whether the tumor has calmed its heat completely or decreased somewhat in intensity.
So then sit the patient in a place exposed to the sun, with his head near you. Open his mouth and take a stick between your hands and compress his tongue downwards with it (as is shown).
You make it from copper or iron, thin like a razor. If you compress the tongue with it and the tumor becomes clear to you and falls upon it with your sight, then take a forceps and insert it into the stone and draw it outwards as much as possible without drawing any of the serous membranes with it.
Then cut it with a tool like this one, resembling scissors but with both ends curved and very sharp. It is made from Indian steel or Damascus iron.
If you do not have this instrument then cut it with a razor like this one, (its shape is) shown.
A sharp one from one side and not sharp from the other. After cutting one stone, cut the other in this same type of cut itself. Then after cutting, have the patient gargle with cold water or vinegar and water.
If bleeding appears, have him gargle with water that has been steeped in the shells of walnuts or the leaves of mulberry trees or something like that from the galls until the bleeding stops. Then treat him until he recovers. And sometimes growths other than the two stones appear in the throat, so cut them as I mentioned in cutting the stones themselves, whether it is one thing or the other.
A woman was treated for a tumor that had grown inside her throat, causing numbness and potentially blocking the airway. She was unable to eat or drink water because of it.
And she was on the verge of death if she had stayed for a day or two, and the tumor had grown branches that poked out through her nostrils. She quickly used an awl to pierce one of them, then pulled it out with the awl, pulling out a suitable piece.
Then she cut it where she had caught hold of it from the nostril, and did that with what poked out from the other nostril. She then opened her mouth and pressed her tongue down, then inserted the awl into the tumor itself, and cut some of it off, and only a little bleeding occurred.
Then the woman's throat cleared, and from that moment on she began to drink water, then ate food. And I have not seen any recurrence of that tumor for a long time, and the tumor would leave behind another in its place until it passed away with her.
And the tumor inside her throat was alleviated and it stopped increasing, then it migrated to another location and I do not know what God did with her afterwards.
The Thirty-seventh Chapter.
Concerning the cutting of a tumor on the neck.
The one that is called a plexus if its nodule has descended to the neck and become inflamed, and was white and rectangular; it is then called a column. And if it was thick at the bottom and rounded, it is then called an obelisk. If it was treated with what we mentioned in the division, the treatment would not be effective.
And I have seen the hot tumor to subside from her, and it was thin, so it is necessary to cut it. And if some of it was united and rounded, and did not have length, and its color was bloody or black or had no sensation, then it is necessary to avoid cutting it.
There is a blemish on the face, so if you see it as described in terms of its whiteness and length, you should have the patient sit in the sun's shadow and compress his tongue with the instrument whose description has been mentioned before, then insert the awl into the nub.
And pull it down and cut it with one of the instruments mentioned in cutting the two tonsils, and you should not cut more than what increased the natural condition without excess because if you cut more you will harm the voice and speech.
Then after cutting, you should use what we described in cutting the two tonsils to treat it until it heals. If the patient is shy about cutting it, you should employ a trick on him without fear or caution and the trick is that the patient puts his head into your lap.
Then compress his tongue with the instrument we mentioned, then take from the hot water mentioned in the chapter of cautery a handful that is not lukewarm and make it neither thick nor thin and fill this mixture into the cauterizer and its shape is: .
Its end where you put the medicine has a cauterizer like a spoonful of syrup, and place the instrument with the medicine on the same nub and the patient lies on his side so that saliva flows from inside his throat lest anything descend into his throat and harm him.
Then hold your hand with the medicine and press it on the nub for half an hour until you see that it has darkened and been stilled by the bite of the medicine. And if you want to take a thread then wrap it on the tip of the instrument and have the thread become soaked in the medicine.
And insert the instrument with the thread into the tube from above until the thread sticks to the nub, do that repeatedly until you reach the desired level of cauterization then leave it alone because it will soften and fall off after three or four days. And if you need to apply the medicine again, reapply it.
After the application of the medication, wash around the boil with a compress soaked in fat and dry it with what is around it from the medicine. Then take a drink of cold water and be treated externally by bandages and internally by poultices until you are cured. This type of treatment is more secure than cutting and far removed from fear.
And the boil can also be treated in a softer way than with cauterization and cutting, it is treated by steam. Take fungi, zufa, sa'atar, citron, marjoram, rue and similar herbs. Gather all of them or some of them together in a pot and immerse them in vinegar.
And it is boiled and the pot is sealed with a covering of clay, and there is a hole left in the lid, through which the steaming vessel is placed, which is made from silver or copper.
The end containing the aromatics is inserted into the patient's mouth until the steam rises up through the tube until it satisfies the boil, then more can be added to it several times until it softens. And beware of making this treatment at first appearance of the boil.
For it often increases in the boil and it is desirable to do this when its hot boil subsides. And if you do not have this instrument, take a reed and attach a coating of an eggshell to its end so that the mouth of the patient does not burn.
Because the coating of the eggshell prevents the heat of the steam from burning the mouth and this is one of the good treatments with its safety.
The Thirty-Eighth Chapter.
For the extraction of thorns and what arises in the throat other than that.
Very often a bone or thick thorn arises in the throat, or something else; it is necessary to remove what appears and falls into sight after compressing the tongue with an instrument at sunrise.
Let it be known to you what is in the throat, and what has not appeared to you that hides in the throat; you should induce the patient to vomit before his food gets digested in his stomach, for perhaps the thing emerging will come out with the vomit or the patient will swallow a piece of lettuce leaf or the root of parsley.
or he will swallow a crust of dry bread or take a piece of soft sea sponge then tie it to a thread and swallow it; if the thread reaches the place of the hook, pull it quickly, do that several times.
Often times the hook or bone gets stuck in there and comes out; if it doesn't come out as mentioned, then use an instrument of lead like this:.
It will be thicker than a probe slightly and at its tip there is a constriction that the patient puts in his loop gently while he raises his head upwards and guards against touching his larynx lest it cause him to cough, and pushes with the lead or bone, or the physician enters it with his hand,.
And entering the probe into it is better for his knowledge of the place of the emerging thing, and he pushes down or pulls with the instrument to upwards, all that as much as he prepares himself until it comes out,.
The 39th Chapter.
In the removal of the phlegm that has emerged in the throat.
If you have treated the phlegm as mentioned in the treatment with medicine and it did not work, then look at the throat of the patient when the sun is out after you compress his tongue with the instrument which I described to you.
If your sight falls on the phlegm, then grasp it with a small forceps or with a soft and firm spatula; if you are not able to do so, then take an irrigated tube and insert it into the throat of the patient near the phlegm, then insert a cauterized needle inside the tube.
He performs the treatment several times and has the patient abstain from water for a whole day. Then he takes permission, filled with cold water, and opens his mouth in it and rinses it with it without swallowing even a drop of it and moves the water here and there with his hand sometimes after another.
If the quinsy feels the water, it will drop to its place. If it does not come out as we described, clear the throat with urine and with a spittle instrument which I mentioned in the treatment of the boil. Do this several times; it will come out.
The method of the treatment by boiling is to take a vessel and put it in front of a flame until it is hot, then cover the vessel with a cloth which has an opening in its centre. The instrument will be placed through this opening and the vessel will be thrown into the boiling water, then the patient will have his mouth on the end of the instrument and close his mouth so that he knows that the boiling substance has reached his throat.
If the quinsy drops, if not, then boil it several times. The patient should endure thirst and eat salted foods and garlic but not drink water; it must come out with this treatment. This is a picture of an instrument which attracts the quinsy from the throat if sight falls on it.
And it is like a calabash as you see, except that it has this groove which enters the throat and its end is like the beak of a bird with the roughness of the file if it bites something without leaving it.
And another instrument which presses the tongue, and it is a wide iron ring that fits in the mouth above the tongue. It enters the mouth standing upright on its side and keeps the mouth open without the patient's will and he cannot remove it at all until it is removed.
The description of the instrument which opens the mouth to this size exactly.
Chapter Forty-four.
Make an incision in the tumor and excise it.
The tumours are of many kinds, specified one by one in this book, and they differ in their incision and excision from two aspects: the nature of the tumour itself and what it contains of moist substances.
And the second type is according to the places where they occur in the body, because the tumour occurring in the head is not like the tumour occurring in the buttocks and the tumour occurring in a place of fat is not like the tumour occurring at a joint; each has its own ruling.
And among the tumours there are those which should not be incised except after fermentation has occurred in them and they have become complete, and there are those which should be excised while still fresh and unfermented, like the tumours that occur near the joints.
For the tumour, if it occurs near a joint and its matter becomes putrid for a long time, it may corrupt the ligaments or nerve of that joint, so it will become a cause of atrophy of that limb, or it is near a main organ.
For if you delay incising it until it ferments, you will damage the main organ or it is near the buttocks, so you cut it fresh and not completely fermented like the tumour which occurs near the buttocks lest the pus ferments and spreads inside the buttocks and becomes gangrenous.
And you must learn the time to excise tumours which have completely fermented, and that is when there is calmness and pain in the tumour, and the fever has subsided, and the redness and pulse have decreased, and the head of the tumour becomes threatening and other symptoms.
And you should aim to incise the tumour below its place if possible, so that it is easier for the pus to drain down or in a more prominent and harder area of the tumour. And the incision should run along the length of the body if the tumours are on the hands and feet.
Places of muscles and tendons and nerves and vessels in general in all places which do not bend, and as for those that bend he goes with the poultice according to that place, and if the swelling is in the places of flesh then it is better to leave it without the poultice.
Until his swelling settles as we mentioned, you should not apply a poultice to him before that time, for it would cause an excessive discharge of pus from it and much dirt and filth, and perhaps it would harden his lips and nostrils, and some tumors would be applied on the surface of the body when necessary or according to what the member needs.
It is to be used in small tumors a single poultice, and in large tumors a wide poultice or many incisions as much as the size of the swelling, and there may be tumors which it is necessary to scrape the skin from them and cut if they have become like a rag.
And it was to the extent that it had died like what is exposed in many ulcers and abscesses, some of which cut a slit with three angles and some of them cut out from them like the shape of a paper plane or a cornaline.
And some of them are used with a circular incision and a crescent-shaped cut and similar ones from the incisions, and as for what does not have a head like smooth flat tumors then it is to be treated with a simple poultice only, and it is necessary if the swelling is large and has collected pus in several times and has been poulticed that one should not hasten lest all the discharge comes out at that time.
Rather he would take some of it out then tie the swelling until another day then take some of the pus also, doing that gradually until all of it comes out.
And especially if the patient is weak or a pregnant woman or a small child or an elderly person, for the vital spirit often dissolves with the discharge coming out suddenly and the patient may die without you feeling it, so be wary of this matter extremely.
After you have pounded on these growths, it is necessary to clean the wound and look; if the wound of the growth is small or there was only one simple slit, then use lint from flax or cotton wool. If the growth is large and there were many slits in the growth.
You should then insert a thread into each slit until they meet one another; and if the growth has been cut off from the skin or pared it, you should pack it with dry cotton wool or lint from flax without moisture and tie it up for three days.
Then remove it and treat it with whatever ointments are necessary until it heals; if there is bleeding on the site of your work, then use cold water and vinegar after you have soaked a flax cloth in them and placed it on the bleeding site several times.
If the bleeding continues, you should use the treatment, therapy and remedies that we have mentioned in many places of this book and in the chapters; if it is winter time and the site of the growth has many nerves, then soak the poultice with wine and hot oil.
And place it on the site, and if you are in summer time and the sites have a lot of blood vessels then carry the poultice soaked with water and oil or wine and oil, all of that cold, until if the third day as we said it is necessary to have the growth heal and be removed.
And use in its treatment what is mentioned until it heals, this is what you need to know about the treatment of growths in general and as for the specific method I have mentioned how to treat each growth briefly.
The forty-first chapter.
In the cut on the boils that appear on the scalp of the head.
There are small growths on the scalp of the head, which are types of scabs that contain pustules, they have a condition like a chicken's coop, and their kinds are many; some are fatty and others contain moisture resembling pus.
Among them is what contains moisture similar to broth and the like, among them is what is hard and frozen. All of them are harmless in cutting and removing them as long as nothing prevents you when cutting them a vessel.
And the procedure in cutting it is to probe it first with a tool that resembles this one called the meds which comes after this, until you know what it contains. If what it contains is moisture then cut it with a longitudinal incision and a simple incision on this pattern:
And start by cutting from line ~b~ to line ~j~, and if the moisture is released then cut the sac that contained that moisture and cut it completely, leaving nothing behind. For often it recures if something remains.
Then dip a thread in the resinous ointment, if it is available and not, then in saltwater, fill with it the wound and leave it until another day comes. For it will eat what remains of the sac, then redo on it the thread with the resin again and again as needed.
Until you are certain that there is nothing left of the sac, then treat the wound with ointments until it heals. And if the swelling contains fatty material then cut it along this pattern:
Make a longitudinal incision and spread the edges of the wound, and cut it out from all sides, and exert your effort in removing the peritoneum that contains it. If a vessel opposes you then do what I have described to you afterwards. And also do this for the swelling if it is hardened from the incision.
And the treatment of it as I have mentioned, and the incision on the hardened swelling is easier because it has little blood and moisture. And some of these swellings in the head of some people may not have any moisture with them at all, that being why I made an incision on a swelling that was in someone.
Head of an elderly woman, I have made the lump as hard as solid stone, with a white skin that could not be crushed and if thrown would break a beam. And this is different from other lumps which occur on the head like those which appear in the heads of children.
And when the ears have roots, split them all with a simple incision and make the opening from below so that the substance may flow down easily then treat it with what is suitable for it.
The 24th Chapter.
These lumps are often found in the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and they can occur all over the body. Sometimes a single one is found in the neck and sometimes many are found there. Some of them originate from others.
And every pig from this kind is in a special sack inside it, as are the growths and lumps of the head which we have described. And there are many kinds of these pigs, some of them hardened, some of them filled with moisture, and some of them are malignant and do not respond to treatment.
I have not seen one of them in good condition by touch, and it was close to the color of the skin, moving in all directions, neither attached to the nerve of the neck nor to a tendon or artery, nor swollen. It should be split with a simple incision from top to bottom of the body in this shape from line J to line B.
You should scrape it all around and stretch the skin with a scalpel or two or many scalps as we said about the lumps of the head, and bring it out little by little, so that it does not cut off a vein or a tendon, but the knife must not be very sharp.
Lest your hand gets cut or the patient becomes anxious and you cut what does not need to be cut, if you cut a vein or an artery and you are prevented from working, put powdered ze'z in the wound or some of the powders that stop bleeding.
Allow the wound to heal and leave it until the inflammation subsides and the wound relaxes as it begins to decay. Then, cut off any remaining blood clot with your index finger and take out any small pieces of flesh or membrane that remain.
If a large vein remains in the piglet, you should not cut it from its source, but rather tie it with a thread as thin as possible and leave it until it falls out on its own without causing any harm. Then fill the wound with cotton that has been soaked in the medicated ointment and treat it.
And if you cut the piglet all up, gather its edges together and sew it from side to side once you have made sure that there is no longer any bleeding. If you find that there has been considerable bleeding due to the size of the piglet.
It is advisable to cut near its root and base, then use suturing and what we have mentioned. And if the piglet contains moisture, bind it with a thin cloth where you see that it has become firm, placing the cloth below as we said.
Then use a poultice after the cloth is removed, made with the medicated ointment and similar substances so that it may consume what remains of the decay. Until you see that the wound has purified, then treat it with the emollient ointments for flesh until it heals.
The 43rd Chapter.
For an incision in the throat due to a swelling inside the esophagus.
The ancients have mentioned this incision in the throat, and I have not seen anyone in our country who has done it. And as for those suffering from strangulation of the esophagus, they should avoid making an incision in the throat, as it does them no good.
In order that all the bronchi and lungs be empty, but as for those who have a hot swelling in the mouth or throat or tonsils, if there is no affliction in the trachea, then an incision in the throat should be used to escape from the trouble which will result from suffocation.
If we wish to do so, then the larynx should be incised under three circles of the trachea's circles or four small cuts in breadth between two circles as much as the cut would be in the peritoneum not in the pleura and this place is suitable for the cut.
Because it is lean of flesh and its blood vessels are distant, if the doctor is cowardly then he should cover the throat skin with an iron instrument then cut the skin until reaching the trachea avoiding the blood vessels if he sees any.
Then he should cut the peritoneum which we have described and he should feel the incision of the trachea from the sputum that comes out from it along with what is ruptured and the cessation of voice, and he should leave the wound open for a time until the fear of choking goes away. Then he should gather together the lips of the wound from the skin.
And he should make an incision alone without the pleura, then use medicines that promote flesh healing until it heals. He who wrote this book said: The explanation of these words which we have mentioned is if they see the ulcer has closed his throat one of those tumors which they mentioned.
And the patient was near death and he himself thought that his breathing would stop, so they went to incise the larynx in order for the patient to breathe on the place of the wound some breaths and be saved from death. And they were ordered to leave the wound open until the crisis is over and its period becomes three days and so on.
So then they were ordered to sew up the wound and treat it until it heals. And what I have seen with my own eyes that a servant took a knife and sent her on her throat cut some part of the bronchus, so I was called to treat her, but she was as bad as one who is slaughtered, so I uncovered the wound.
I found the blood that came out of the wound to be little, and I became certain that it had not cut a vein nor an artery. The breath was coming from the wound, so I stitched the wound until it healed, and nothing but a murmur in the voice was presented to the servant.
And she returned after some days to her best state, so from here we say that cutting the trachea is not hazardous.
The Fourth Chapter Forty-fourth.
In cutting on the swelling that appears from outside in the bronchi.
This swelling which is called the tumor of the bronchi is a large swelling on the color of the body and it is common in women and there are two types.
It is either natural or a complication, so as for the natural one there is no remedy for it and as for the complicated one it will be of two kinds, one resembling fatty goods and the other resembling the tumor which forms from a twisted artery and in its incision there is danger. It should not be attempted with iron at all, except if a small part of it is probed and searched with the probe and I found that it resembled fatty goods and was not connected to anything of the vessels, so I cut it as one cuts on fatty goods. It should be taken out along with what it contains in the sac if it is in a sac, otherwise all of it should be investigated and then treated as needed.
The Fifth Chapter Forty-fourth.
In cutting on types of fatty goods.
Fatty goods are many in kind and I have mentioned all their kinds in the classification, and it is necessary to inform here of the difference between fatty goods and abscesses, for they are complications. So I say that an abscess will be with heat and fever and severe pains until the pus subsides. When the purulence has been completed, then fever and rigor seize it; and neither heat nor fever nor pains remain with it. It is contained in a membrane which is its special envelope and which is of the colour of the body. Its beginning is like that of an abscess and it becomes larger or smaller.
It is of two kinds; either it is fatty, or it contains moisture. The colours of the moisture are many, as I have mentioned in the classification. Therefore, if you come to treat the purulence, you must first probe and investigate it with the instrument called the medissah, in the form that appears in the chapter which comes after this one.
Measure the size of the swelling, then withdraw the medissah and look at what comes out in its place. If a watery discharge comes out, whatever its colour may be, incise it with a small incision, as I have mentioned for all swellings. And if no discharge comes out after removing the medissah, know that it is fatty.
Incise it with a sutured incision in the form I have shown you, and tie it up with ligatures. Then remove the skin from all sides gently, and preserve it in a sac if possible so that you can take it out correctly with the purulence.
If the sac bursts during the operation and you cannot remove it correctly, that occurs often. Then take it out bit by bit until nothing remains. For if any part of it remains, whether little or much, the purulence is likely to do what happens most of the time.
If it prevails over you and only a small part remains, then sew up the wound with some sharp lancets when you have finished. Cover it with something to calm the hot swelling and treat it with all other treatments until it heals. And if the purulence is large, cut along its edge and treat it as I have mentioned for what requires suturing.
If a bleeding or non-bleeding vein obstructs you, take the powdered alum and apply it to the wound in abundance. Leave it closed for two or three days until the wound dries up and the bleeding stops, then return to cut what remains of the fabric.

Tools for various purposes.

The Forty-Ninth Chapter.
In the incision of the tumor which is exposed by an artery or a vein and is called aneurisma.

And the signs by which it can be known that the swelling and puffing are from an artery or a vein, if the swelling is from an artery it will be flatulent and accumulated in the depth of the body, and if you push the swelling with your finger you will feel as though there is a crust.
And if it is from a vein, the swelling will be curved in front of the body, and the incision on these swellings is hazardous, especially in the armpit, groin, neck, and many other places in the body, and they are very large; one should avoid treating them with iron.
And also, if it is in the limbs or the head, one should avoid treating them. As for that which is from a swelling of an artery, incise it on the skin with a long cut, then widen the cut with lancets, then remove the artery and free it from adhesions.

A boil will heal, then treatment is used which causes purulence until the strings come out. Then it is treated with ointments that are suitable for this until it clears up.

The 50th chapter.
In the boil which appears due to a nerve plexus.
As the boil is exposed in an artery and a vein, likewise it is exposed in a nerve if there is a blow or excessive fatigue has occurred in it, or something similar and that is more so in places of the elbows and armpits.

Chapter Fifty-One.
In cutting out ulcers which are exposed in the abdomen.
Many people are exposed to ulcers in their bellies and elsewhere, which are called fungal ulcers because of their resemblance to fungi, its origin is thin and its head is thick. Its edges may be transformed and some may become very large.
And I have seen a man with two ulcers in his belly, they resembled fungi more than anything else, their colour was white and thin at its base which had transformed into edges and become rough. Moisture always flowed from them. I cut them out and they weighed about 18 drachmas on one scale, and around 6 drachmas on the other.
And the operation in cutting them is that you observe, if the ulcer is moist and the colour of the tumour is white, moist and thin at its base then cut it out with a wide scalpel, and have vinegar nearby to heat over the fire, for often much blood spurts when cutting into them.
So you take a lead thread and tie it around the tumour which has this shape, leave it for two days then add more tightness to the lead thread so that it stays tied.
The more you intervene in the tumour until it is cut off and falls away from itself without any harm, if the tumour has a thick base then there is some fear and risk when cutting into it, especially when it is in the belly but sometimes half of it or part of it can be cut.
Then you cauterize it so that it does not return, and then treat the wound until it heals. And beware of cutting a tumour which is pale in colour, insensitive to touch, with an unpleasant appearance, for it is a cancerous tumour, and we will come to mentioning cancer after this.
Chapter the Second and Fifty-second.
In the treatment of a serpent's sting.
It is caused by a rupture of the peritoneum in the abdomen, from which there comes out an intestine or bladder, or it is a burst blood vessel, as mentioned before, or it is pus that has accumulated.
If it is caused by a rupture of the peritoneum and an intestine has come out, then the colour of the swelling will be similar to that of the body and there will be a lot of fluid without any pain, and the position will be obvious. And if it is caused by the bursting of a bladder, its position will be very different from what we have described. If you press on it with your fingers, it will disappear then return, and sometimes there may be a lump with it, and it will become very swollen when bathing and great fatigue sets in. And if it is caused by dampness, it will be fluid.
It does not disappear when pressed with the hand, nor does it increase or decrease. And if it is caused by blood, then in addition to these signs, the swelling will show blackness. And if it is caused by a tumour that has grown from fat, then the swelling will be swollen and hard, and will remain firm on one side.
If it is caused by pus, its touch will be fluid. The treatment for that is to observe. If the serpent's sting is caused by blood from a vessel or vein or pus, then you should abstain from treating it, for there is fear and confusion in doing so, as I have informed you in the chapter where I mentioned tumours caused by vessels and veins.
If the serpent's sting is caused by a burst intestine or intestine, then the practitioner should order him to hold himself and stand upright with his legs straight, then he should apply the medicated resin all around the swelling. Then order him to lie down in front of you on his back, then grasp the swelling with a broad lancet all around it at the place where you applied the medicated resin, then insert a large needle into the centre of the swelling upwards, then bind the place of the ligature tightly with a strong thread or a wet silk string.
The knot of the ligature will be tightened, then opened in the middle above the ligated mass. Insert your index finger into it and look for a bladder. If you find it, the ligature has taken hold of it. Loosen the knot and push the bladder back into the abdomen. If you find an intestine, draw it back with forceps.
Cut the hernia, and if an artery or vein blocks you, tie it off. Then go back to your work and take two needles with strong thread. Put the threads into the ligature that you made around the mass from four sides that you have passed through them, then pull the mass on the threads.
And if you want, remove the needles and leave the place until the adhered flesh rots and falls away or is cut off if it becomes rotten. Then treat it as needed with ointments until it heals. If there was a cyst in the inflamed flesh.
Or if there is dampness, you should compress the tumor as we said and take out the blood or dampness that you find in it, then treat it with what cures the place.

He is forced to cut again and the pain is resumed; and cleansing with a catheter does not guarantee cutting off the end of the urethra, because it may enter its hole; and as for cleansing with an awl, perhaps the skin will burst and your work will be spoiled or the skin of the child is short by nature...
Many of them are born like that and do not need cleansing, which I have seen; and as for cleansing with a razor and sewing with thread, experience has shown me its superiority because the cut is proportional so that the blade from above is similar to the one from below.
