The 48th chapter.
In the treatment of obstructed urine in the bladder.
Urine retained in the bladder is due to a stone, or dried blood, or filth, or flesh that has grown and the like. If you treat this as mentioned, then the varieties of treatment prescribed are to be followed.
And if the urine does not pass and you see that its retention is due to a stone in the neck of the bladder, then the patient should sit on his haunches, a man will ride on his back and stretch his belly against his back, and he should grasp himself as much as possible.
So the neck of the bladder is then forced to push the stone behind, and the urine will pass. And if it does not pass as mentioned and the patient's condition becomes worse, a device called catheter, which is its shape:, should be used.
It is made from thin, smooth and polished silver tube, narrow like a bird's quill, long about one finger-breadth and half. It has a small spout at its head, and the outlet of urine with it should take a twisted thread and tie it tightly on one end with wool or cotton.
And the thread is inserted into the lower end of the catheter, and it is moistened with oil or fat or egg white. Then the patient sits on a chair.
Then the bladder and urethra are squeezed with moistened liniment or oil and warm water. Then the catheter is inserted gently into the urethra until it reaches its root, then the urethra is bent upwards towards the belly button and then the catheter is pushed inside.
Until if the urethra is bent then the catheter is pushed inside until it reaches close to the prostate, the man leans down and the catheter is inside him, then he is pushed forward until it reaches the bladder and the patient feels that something has been reached empty.
He makes a catheter of this rank because the flow channel in which the urine flows is bent, then he pulls out the thread with the soft wool tightly, for the urine follows the soft wool; then he takes it out and lets the urine drain, and repeats the procedure.
She continues to do that until the bladder is emptied and the patient finds relief.
The Ninetieth Chapter.
How to Catheterize the Bladder with a Reed.
How to Catheterize the Bladder with a Reed. Instruments suitable for this are made from gilded bronze or ivory which have a long tube on one side, and wanted to squirt water and medicine into it, so that would be called the reed and here is its picture:.
It is made from gilded bronze or ivory with a long tube on a curved surface, polished all over except for one end which is closed. There are three holes in it, two on one side and one on the other as you see.
And the hollow place in which the catheters are placed is as much as fills it without any excess, so if you pull something with it from the moistures, it will be pulled and if you push it, it will move forward like what is made for throwing oil in naval battles.
If you wanted to drain the moistures into the bladder, then you would insert the tip of the reed into the moisture and pull with the catheter upwards, so that the moisture will be attracted into the hollow of the reed. Then you would enter its end into the urethra as we described in the catheters, and then push the moisture with the catheter.
For that moisture will reach the bladder as it should until the patient feels it, and here is a picture of another catheter which also drains the bladder.
It is made from bronze or ivory, its top resembles a small funnel and below it is a pouch in which the strap is placed. Then you take a bladder of a young camel and put into it the moisture that you want to catheterize with, then tie it tightly between the two pouches with a doubled thread.
Warm the moisture slightly over the fire. Then insert the end of the catheter into the urethra, and pull your hand on the bladder with the warmth tightly until the patient feels that the warmth has reached the bladder.
If the bladder does not contract, take a piece of linen and make a circle from it. Puncture it from all its sides, then insert a thick thread into that puncture as it turns around. Then gather the circle as one gathers cloth after putting what you want of moistures, paints and water in it.
Then tie it in the device and do with it as you did with the bladder, moving your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
Chapter 60.
On the Removal of Stones.
We have mentioned in the division the types of stones and their treatment with medications, and we have mentioned the differences between the stones that are formed in the kidney and those formed in the bladder, and their signs; and we have also mentioned the stone in which surgical intervention by hand or incision takes place.
And that is the stone formed in the bladder especially and that attaches itself to the urethra. I am describing it clearly and briefly.
I say that the stone formed in the bladder is more often seen in children, and one of its signs is that the urine comes out of the bladder with a thin, watery texture.
And it shows sand in it, and its presence is felt and tampered with, and it often hangs down and spreads out. The rectum also appears in many of them along with it. And the removal from children becomes easier until they reach fourteen years old, but it becomes difficult for the elderly. As for young men, it is moderate between that.
And what is more, the treatment of its stone becomes easier and what is smaller is the opposite. So if we are to treat it, then first the patient should be catheterized with a catheter that extracts all the sediment from his bladder, for it may prevent the presence of the stone when examined.
Then the patient is lifted up with a rod; he shakes and moves downwards so that the stone falls into the bladder neck or is thrown from a high place several times. Then you make him sit in front of you, erect, his hands under his thighs, so that the entire bladder tilts downwards, then you probe him.
And you probe him from the outside; if you feel the stone in the space, then rush to cut it; and if it doesn't fall down, leave it for a moment. It is necessary that you wipe the index finger of the left hand with grease if the patient is a boy or the middle finger.
If he is completely a boy, you put your finger into his penis and search for the stone until it falls under your finger; then you move it a little bit by a little bit towards the bladder neck and compress it with your finger and push it outwards towards the place where you want to cut it.
And order a servant to compress the bladder with his hand and another servant to extend his right hand towards the top and with the other hand to extend the skin underneath towards the place where the cut is. Then take the curved instrument whose picture is this:.
And you cut between the scrotum and the penis, not in the middle but beside the left groove; the cut is on the same place as the stone and your finger in the penis while you are pressing it outwards, so that the cut is wide from outside and narrow from inside to the extent that the stone can come out of it.
Not larger, perhaps you pressed the stone with the finger in the penis at the cut and it came out without difficulty; know that there may be angles and branches to the stone which make its exit difficult.
And among them is smooth like walnut and curved, so its exit is easy; but what has angles and branches to it, you increase the cut a little more; if it does not come out that way, then you need to hold onto it firmly with a grip that is sharp like a razor.
Correct the stone so that it does not slip from your hand. Then, either enter under it a gentle instrument with a blunted end, or if you cannot manage it, widen the incision slightly. And if something of blood overpowers you, cut it off with cauterization.
If there are more than one, first push the largest into the bladder then make an incision on it, then push the smaller ones after that. Do likewise if there are more than two. And if they are extremely large, it is ignorance to make a large incision on them, because either of two things will result from it.
Either he will die, or a constant dripping of urine will occur from him because the wound will not heal at all. But try to push it until it comes out, or turn it in its fracture with the calipers until it comes out definitely.
If you have finished your work, then close the wound with a compress and bandage, and tighten it. Then pour over it an infusion of oil or drink mixed with rose water and cold water to calm the hot swelling. The patient should lie on his back without having the bandage changed until the third day.
If it becomes suppurated, uncover the place with plenty of water and oil, then treat it with the resinous ointment and the ointment of saponaria until it heals. And if there is an excessive hot swelling in the wound, or inflammation and similar things such as blood freezing in the bladder and urine not flowing from it, this will be known by the blood coming out along with the urine.
Then insert your finger into the wound and remove that blood, for if it remains it will call to the corruption of the bladder and its stones. Then wash the wound with vinegar, water and salt, and apply all kinds of treatment as it has been described until it heals.
And it is advisable during all the time of treatment to bind the thighs together and tie them up in order to keep the remedies that are placed on the place, in a firm position. If the stone was small and became lodged in the urethra and urine did not come out from it, treat it as I have described before it becomes incised.
I frequently resort to this treatment in place of cutting, where one takes a piece of iron from the metal of a forge which has this shape:.
Like a triangle at the end, sharp and hooked on an end. Then one takes a thread and binds it to the catheter under the stone so that it does not return to the bladder; then one inserts the iron into the urethra gently until the instrument reaches the same stone.
And one turns the instrument with your hand in the stone a little, a little, while you try to pierce it until you pass it from the other side; then urine flows out of its opening. Then you grasp what remains of the stone from outside the catheter; it crumbles and comes out with the urine and the lesion is cured.
If this treatment is not available to you due to an obstacle that prevents you from doing so, then tie a thread under the stone and another thread over the stone; then cut on the stone in the same catheter between the two threads and it will come out.
Then the ligature will cover and clean the coagulated blood that has remained in the wound. And it was necessary to tie the thread under the stone so that it does not return to the bladder, and the other one above, so that if the thread comes loose after the stone is removed, the skin will go back into place and cover the wound.
Therefore, it is necessary for you to raise the skin upwards if you tied the upper thread so that it goes back into place and covers the wound as we said.
The Fifty-first Chapter.
For extracting stones from women.
Stones are rarely formed in women; if one of them presents with a stone, its treatment is difficult and refused by many reasons, one that the woman may be a virgin, and another that you will not find a woman who allows herself to be examined by a doctor.
If it is a virgin or one of the prohibited degrees and the third that you do not find a woman who excels in this craft, especially the work with the hand, and the fourth that the place of incision on the stone is far from the place of the stone, therefore you need to cut deep.
And in that there is a risk, if necessity calls for it, you should take a virtuous woman doctor, and little do they exist; if none are available, ask an innocent and trustworthy physician or a virtuous midwife who has knowledge in the affairs of women, or a woman experienced in this craft with some indication.
Have her prepare and command her to do all that she commands her to do in inspecting the stone first, this is that she look if the woman is a virgin, then let her insert her finger into her backside and inspect the stone; if she finds it and presses it under her finger.
Then command her to cut into her; if she is not a virgin and was married, then command the midwife to insert her finger into the woman's vagina and inspect the stone after that she put her left hand on the bladder and squeeze it well.
If she finds it, then have her guide it from the mouth of the bladder downwards to the extent of her ability until it reaches the root of the thigh, then cut into her at the meeting point of the middle of the vagina near the root of the thigh from whichever side is convenient for her and felt the stone in that direction.
And her finger does not move from the stone compressed under it, and let the incision be small at first then insert the rod into that small incision; if she feels the stone, she should increase the incision as much as she knows the stone comes out of it, and know that types of stones are many.
Among them are small and large, rough and hairy, long and turned, with branches; know their kinds so you can deduce what you want from it; if blood overpowers you, leave in the place of powder sprinkled on it and hold it for a moment until the blood stops then return to your work.
Until the stone comes out, work with yourself in mind to count among the instruments I mentioned for the removal of stones from men to help you in your job. If bleeding prevails over you and you have learned that the pulse of blood is from a cut artery then place sutures on the site.
And bind him with the strong bandages tightly and leave it, do not touch it and leave the stone, do not remove it. Perhaps the vein had died then treat the wound. If the intensity of the blood had calmed after days and the site had softened then go back to your work until you take out the stone.
Chapter Two and Fifty.
In the incision on the urinary bladder.
The urinary bladder is the gathering of moisture in the white omentum that is under the skin of the testicle surrounding the ovary, and it is called the scrotum. It may be enclosed in a special membrane, provided by nature on one side of the ovary.
Until he thinks it is another ovary and it will be between the skin of the testicle and the white omentum that we mentioned, but that will not happen except in rarity. This urinary bladder is produced from weakness that exposes to women so this matter is assigned to it and sometimes it is exposed because of a blow on the women.
And this moisture has many colors, sometimes its color is yellowish, sometimes it is reddish like blood, sometimes it is blackish, and sometimes it is whitish like water, and that is what it usually is. And the signs by which one recognizes it.
Where the water is gathered, if it is in the white omentum that we mentioned, then the swelling will be rounded a little to length like an ovary shape and the testicle will not appear because the moisture surrounds it from all sides.
And if the moisture is in a separate membrane for it, then the swelling will be rounded on one side of the ovary.
Because of this, man will imagine it to be another egg, and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicle and the white spermatic cord then it falls under the sense, but if you want to know the color of the moisture sprinkle the tumor with a rectangular lint which has been previously shown, what comes out in its effect I have ruled upon it according to what is inside.
If we are going to treat with iron, it should be that the healer orders to let blood if possible and you see his body is full then he lies on his back on a slightly raised thing and put many hot pads under him and you sit on his left side.
And you order a servant to sit on his right side and to stretch his penis towards one of your sides of the scrotum and toward the direction of looking at the belly, then take a broad lancet and cut the skin of the testicle from the middle lengthwise near the anus.
And the cut becomes on a straight line parallel to the line that divides the skin of the scrotum into two halves until it reaches the white spermatic cord and you scrape it off and be careful not to cut it, and your scraping should be from the side that sticks more with the egg and you take out as much of the scraped part as you can.
Then you sew the sac filled with water with a wide needle and thread and take out all the water, then you spread between the edges of the cut with stitches and stretch the sac upwards without touching the skin that contains it and you cut the sac as much as you can cut it, either in one piece or cutting by pieces.
And especially its thin part, for if you do not take out all of it then the water may come back in, and if the egg protrudes to outside from its skin while you are doing your work, when you finish cutting the sac turn it over then gather together both sides of the scrotum with stitching.
Then the treatment is that of other wounds until it heals. If the ovary has been damaged, it may have been spoiled by another disease; therefore, one must ligate the vessels in the groin out of fear of bleeding then cut off the testicle from the groin and remove the ovary and treat it as we mentioned.
If the water has collected on both sides, know that they have united; cut the other side as you did the first one whether it was your intention to do one operation or two, then wipe away the blood.
She enters into the incisions with a wool that has been dipped in oil or rosewater and it becomes from the outside another wool that has been dipped in wine and oil, she spreads it on the testicles and touches the belly then puts over it a folded cloth called the "rafid". And she ties it from above with a bandage that has six ends like this:.
Then two cloths are taken to be sewn and stuffed with the fluffy wool on this model, and the ends are made from wet cotton or wool that are tied together by pulling it tight in a belt of trousers, and one end is taken to the seat as far back as the back.
And the second one is taken as far down as the anus, and the ends are on the thighs from below and the remaining ends are on the bandages and all the pulling together in a belt of trousers, and this device can also be made with linen instead of cutting with iron.
And it is that you take a soft and thin iron instrument, with which you cut the skin of the testicles as we described until the white membrane containing water is exposed, then take another iron instrument like this:.
And it is like the Greek eye, then press with it that membrane until all the moisture comes out, then spread the membrane with clamps and scrape with an iron instrument the layer containing them and cut them as much as you can so that you eliminate all of them and preserve the ovary from the fire.
Know that this operation is more valid and safer than hemostasis, and better than the incision method; if you encounter in cutting or in ligating a hot embers or bleeding blood or something else it should be treated each time you encounter of that by treatment correct for it as mentioned above.
If the wound is stubborn and the patient did not tolerate this operation because of its severity, use a caustic as I have described it, which, if you apply to it according to the evidence we have mentioned earlier.
Know that the caustic is watery; sit the patient on a high chair, then squeeze the lump at its base with a wide spatula and put the caustic along the length of the body, and make the opening widely so that all the water flows out, then place on the spot cotton and bind it.
Leave him to sweat out the remaining water, then treat him until the wound is cured; if the bleeding occurs when you put it on him and it is because the white membrane obstructs in the mouth of the wound preventing the water from coming out.
So then it is necessary to enter into the wound a bird's feather or the instrument by which the water of emetics comes out, as its form has been mentioned before, or widen the opening of the wound slightly.
Know that the water may return and gather after six months or so; if it gathers, apply a poultice to him with the same condition and defend the patient for his days.
The 63rd Chapter.
On the incision into the bloody caustic and its treatment.

A tumor is in the groin and perhaps the tumor has become indurated its color like inflammation and it has no feeling. If you press it with your fingers and it should not be exposed in the least. As for what is from a dilation of veins; it does not disappear from being pressed by the fingers, and this kind can sometimes cut into him and all the flesh.

The 64th Chapter.

The Fifty-Sixth Chapter.
In the treatment of intestinal abscesses.
This abscess occurs from a rent that opens in the omentum spread on the belly about the twelfth of an inch above the navel so that the intestine falls out through this rupture to one of the testicles.
And this rupture is either from a tear in the omentum or its extension, and this type of abscess occurs due to many causes, such as being hit or thrown with something heavy and so on. And its sign if it is from the extension of the omentum that it develops gradually over time.
And it does not occur suddenly, and the abscess is flattened towards a depth before the omentum compresses the intestine. Its sign if it is from a tear in the omentum that it occurs from its beginning with great pain at once and the abscess is different appearing under the skin nearby.
This is done by the evacuation of the intestines and their exit to the outside of the peritoneum. It may come out with the intestine, it being called intestinal and purulent, or there may be an impaction in the intestine, which will lead to the death of the patient.
Because it causes severe pain and spasm, especially if he has an attack of diarrhea. The treatment by iron is a hazardous procedure that one should be wary of; the mode of action is to have the patient insert his hand into his belly to return the intestines back inside.
Then he lies on his back between your hands, raises his legs, and you stretch the skin that follows the pubic bone upwards. You make a cut in all of the scrotal skin by its length, then insert probes into the opening as much as is needed to open it with them.
The cut will be as much as the testicles can come out of it, then you peel away the peritoneal layers that are under the scrotal skin until the white dense peritoneum is exposed on all sides. Then insert your index finger into what follows the testicles.
Between the white peritoneum that is under the skin of the testicle and the second peritoneum, you loosen the adhesion behind the testicle. Then bend with your right hand towards the inside of the scrotal skin, while extending the white peritoneum upwards with your left hand and raising the testicle with the peritoneum towards the incision.
Order the servant to extend the testicle upwards, and you yourself loosen completely the adhesion that is behind it. You then inspect with your finger so that there is nothing of twisted intestine in the dense white peritoneum; if you find something, push it down into the lower part of the abdomen.
Then take a needle with a thick thread which has been twisted from ten threads, and insert it at the end of the peritoneum under the scrotal skin that is next to the incision. Then cut off the ends of the twisted thread until there are four threads. Then some of it is wrapped around each other in a sutured manner and tied with the omentum which we said was under the skin of the testicles, tightly bound from two sides. Then also tie the ends of the threads together, tightly until nothing from the vessels that nourish them can reach it. So that it is not exposed and a hot swelling forms, and the second suture also becomes outside of the first one far from it less than two fingers, and after these two sutures take out from the omentum under the skin of the testicles as much as the length of a finger.
So that it is not exposed and a hot swelling forms, and the second suture also becomes outside of the first one far from it less than two fingers, and after these two sutures take out from the omentum under the skin of the testicles as much as the length of a finger. The eighth and seventy chapter.
In the slackening of the skin of the testicles.
Often the skin of the testicles becomes slack in some people without the meat inside becoming slack and it is ugly to look at, so he who wishes to treat it should make the patient sleep on his back.

The Seventieth Chapter.
In castration.
Castration is prohibited in our religion.
So it should be for me not to mention this in my book, but I have mentioned it for two reasons. One is that the physician may know its treatment if asked about it and learn how to cure him who has been castrated. The other reason is that we often need to castrate some animals for our benefit.
Like camels, donkeys and cats and the like of animals, I say that castration can be done in two ways: either by burning or cutting. If it is by burning, then its method is that we sit the animal in hot water until the female parts relax and soften and become loose.
Then you burn it with your hand until it dissolves and does not become apparent upon touch. As for castration by cutting, it is necessary to catch the animal and press the skin of its scrotum with the left hand then bind the testicles and cut on each testicle a single cut.
Until if the testicles protrude, cut them after they have been flayed and do not leave on them anything but the thin peritoneum that is on the vessels. And this type of castration is better than the one by burning.
Because the burn may have left something of the female parts and the animal has lust for copulation, then treat the wound until it heals.
The Seventieth Chapter.
In the treatment of the hermaphrodite.
The hermaphrodite occurs in men of two kinds: one is that which appears below the pubes or on the skin of the testicles among women in shape like a woman's vulva with hair, and urine may flow from it which is found on the skin of the testicles.
And as for women, one kind occurs above the vulva on the perineum similar to small male genitals however born outside one of them like a man's penis and the other two like those of a woman, treatment of all three kinds.
The two kinds of men and the one kind of woman should have those excessive flesh cut off until its effect is removed, then be treated with the treatment of broken bones in order to heal, and as for the second kind of man from whom urine comes out that is on the skin of the testicles there is no treatment nor cure.
The Seventy-first Chapter.
In cutting clitorises and the flesh coming from vulvas of women.
The clitoris may have increased in size beyond the natural amount until it becomes ugly and its appearance is repulsive, and in some women it may become large like men's penises to the point of intercourse.
You should grasp the clitoris with your hand or a forceps and cut it off, and do not take much time in cutting nor especially deep at its root so that bleeding does not occur.
Then treat it with the treatment of broken bones until it heals, and as for the flesh that grows, it is a flesh that grows in the mouth of the uterus until it fills it.
And perhaps it comes out outside like an example of the womb. And because of this, some of the ancients call it a disease called the "dhambiy" so you should cut it like cutting the clitoris and treat it until it heals.
The second seventy chapter.
For the treatment of retention.
Retention is when the vagina is not fully opened or its opening is small, and this can be either natural at birth or a defect that has arisen; the defect being sometimes due to an overgrowth of flesh.
Or a thin or thick membrane, sometimes in the depth of the womb, sometimes on its sides, sometimes above it or below it; preventing coitus and childbirth and possibly menstruation. And this is known by looking at the woman's vulva.
If the membrane is visible, then if it is not visible, one must probe it with her fingers or a rod. If the membrane is thin and close to the vulva lips, she should begin to cut it by placing an object resembling a thread on the vulva lips then putting both of her thumbs on top of it.
And the woman is on her back, legs apart, then she extends the vulva lips with force until the thin membrane is torn and the membrane opens. Then she takes a cotton thread and dips it in oil and puts it on the place and tightens the woman every day so that the place does not stick together again.
If the membrane is thick and dense, it should be cut with a wide lancet resembling an aloe leaf. And if the membrane is from a growth of flesh, then one must remove it by means of thin forceps and sever it. And have remedies to stop the bleeding without haste, such as al-qaqia, ash-shayan, and al-laban mixed with egg whites.
Then she uses a large lead tube to prevent the wound from healing quickly, holding it for days and using flax seeds afterwards and then treating with the remedies for adhesion until it heals. And sometimes another growth of flesh may appear in the womb, which should be cut off in this manner.
If it is not a cancerous tumor, then the cancerous tumour which exists in the womb should not be exposed to iron at all.
Chapter Seventy-Three.
In the treatment of hemorrhoids, anal fistulas and red blisters that occur in the vagina of women.
As for hemorrhoids, it is an enlargement of the orifices of the veins until much blood flows from them constantly. If the hemorrhoids are presented they became anal fistulas, and we have mentioned their types and signs in the classification, and we will mention them here.
What can be treated and what cannot be treated from them, I say that hemorrhoids and anal fistulas if they are in the depth of the womb and have not appeared to touch then there is no treatment with iron, and as for that which falls on it the sense then it is the one that can be treated.
It is necessary that the woman enters a cold house, then insert the anal fistula with a file or a rough cloth and cut it from its roots, then tie on it when bleeding stops from one of the arteries cutting the blood without ligature.
Like pomegranate peel and almonds and similar things, then raise her legs to the wall for an hour, then lower them in cold water. If the bleeding continues, place her on a decoction of rhubarb, quince skins, and saffron and similar things, then take barley flour and mix it with honey and vinegar.
And plaster it on her back with it. If the bleeding stops, then bind a poultice of beaten plantain or the pulp of the birthwort plant or the juice of elderberry branches with saffron drink and seal the place.
If the tumour subsides, treat the place with ointment until it heals. And as for the red blisters, they are like the heads of henna, rough to look at. It is necessary to cut what appears from them according to what I mentioned in anal fistulas, whether it be or not, and treat it until it heals.
The 74th Chapter.
Concerning the swelling of an abscess which appears in the womb.

And she gathers her legs to the lower part of the abdomen, and her thighs are spread wide apart, and her arms are under her knees and they are bound with a bandage that is suitable.
Then the attendant sits on the right side and uses the instrument which opens the cervix, whose shape will be shown later. It is necessary if you want to use this instrument that you estimate by a ruler the depth of the womb of the woman so that what enters from the instrument does not exceed the depth of the womb.

And you hold the instrument and the servant turns the loop until it opens the cervix; if the abscess appears and is felt by hand and is soft like a thread, then it should be cut at its head with a wide lancet when the moment has been exhausted.

It is necessary that he abstain from treatment with iron, but he should be treated as we have mentioned in the classification.
The seventy-fifth chapter.
In the instruction of women, how they treat living foetuses if they come out in an unnatural shape.
It is necessary for the midwife to know first the natural shape of birth, and among its signs if she sees the woman move down and stretch to breathe in air and loosen what she has from flux.
And the birth of the child is hastened, know that this birth will be in its natural shape and his exit on his head with the placenta or attached to his navel cord, if you see these signs then it is necessary for you to tighten her belly so that the child may come out quickly.
But if it comes out on its head, the placenta comes with it and cleans out those clutters in a good way. And as for any birth other than this one, it is not natural, condemned because sometimes the child may come out on its feet, with its hands coming out before its head and feet.
And its single hand or foot comes out, or its head and one hand come out, or it may come out folded up, or it may be turned over on its back like this and other condemned forms. It is necessary for the midwife to be wise and gentle with all of these things and beware of error and mistake.
And I am describing every shape of it and how the trick is in it so you can learn from that and rely on it. If the baby comes out with its head coming out naturally, but becomes stuck on the woman and causes her difficulty in giving birth and I see that she has become weakened because of it, then I have her sit down on a chair and order the women to hold her back.
And I have her compress her womb with cooked poultice and wet leather, then the midwife inserts a small instrument between her fingers to tear it open or tears it with her fingernail until what is inside it seeps out and moistens the woman's belly so that the baby comes down.
If it does not come out, then the woman should be given a draught of saliva from the poultice with oil to lubricate her vagina, and I have her after the injection that she vomits and sneezes in its direction with a handful of wool, and she grasps her mouth and nose, for the baby will come out from its fist. If the baby's hands come out first, it should be gently pushed back into the womb little by little.
If they do not come out to enter, then have the woman sit on a stepladder and raise her legs up high, then shake the ladder on the ground and the woman should hold onto something so that she does not fall down when it is shaken. If the hands still do not come out and the baby has died, cut off its hands and pull out the rest of the baby.
Or tie its hands with a cloth and pull them out gently, for the baby will come out. If the baby comes out on its legs, then you should push them up high and turn the baby a little at a time until it is straightened, then take one of its legs and push it forward a little at a time.
If they come out to the thighs, then I have her vomit and sneeze in its direction with a handful of wool, for it will come out. If it does not come out as we have described and otherwise, turn the baby back a little at a time until it is straightened naturally, for it will come out smoothly then. If all that we have described refuses to happen.
Take from the sputum of the tracheotomy and the phlegm of the lung and fatty ointment for the throat and dissolved gum, and strike them all in a mortar with a good pounding. Then put it on the woman's vagina and lower abdomen. Then sit her in warm water until the poultices reach.
If you see that it has begun to flow downwards, make a pessary from mustard and have her bear it. If you hold the pessary for an hour then sit her on a chair, let her breathe, stop her mouth and nose, and press her lower abdomen gently; then the fetus will come out of its sac. The fetus comes out on its knees and hands.
If it comes out in this manner, occupy yourself with putting your hands into it a little by little. Then the woman lies on her back and stretches her legs downwards while she is resting on a bed and clasps her hands together. Then press above her abdomen gently by gentle pressure. Then take out what is under her feet from the pillows until it is lowered. If the fetus does not come out, take both her legs together and move them with a strong movement. Then press above the poultices gently by gentle pressure until the fetus ascends. Then the midwife will put in her hand and cover the fetus little by little.
And order the woman to get up until the fetus comes out. The fetus will come out with its hands and feet cramped, lying over one of its hands. Occupy yourself in retrieving her hand, if you are not able to retrieve it, then make the woman walk. If you are not able to make her walk, then have her lie down.
Then make her bedstead shake with strong shaking of her legs. Then use the instrument which I have mentioned from the devices, if she takes it, then sit her on a chair and treat in retrieving the hand and putting the fetus right on its natural shape. Let the woman breathe and order her to get up until it comes out.
The birth of the child on his mother's back with his arms extended and face towards her back, it is recommended that the attendant hold the child's hand then turn him little by little and swaddle him gently. When he is level, carry him on his mother's chest as we have described from ointments and clamps.
Then move her a little, if you do that sit her on the stool and order her to lean to the right side then have her undress and she should sneeze with the dust, as it exits, the birth of the child standing up on his side.
If it goes into the uterus mouth in this manner with the placenta, tear the placenta with your nails until it is free from moisture. If it has adhered to the baby's face and neck then cut them off from the sac so that it does not suffocate and die. Then push the baby back inside until you put it on what is required.
And order the woman to sneeze again, as it exits it comes out easily. The birth of twins or many fetuses, know that twins are often born and three or four may be born and live except that this is rare. And as for five, it is a thing outside of nature which do not live at all.
And surround them, and if they are many one placenta, and they separate by a ligature barrier between them attached in a sac each of them. And they may come out as the single child comes out naturally easy and they come out as we have described abnormally.
If some of them become difficult during birth and became as we have said in the forms that are not natural, treat them as we have described. And let the attendant be gentle and do what she does gently, patiently and considerate on every shape with whatever trick leads to safety.
Describing what appears in the womb to be fetuses, which they drop. Sometimes one, two, three, four, five, six, seven or more than ten will appear in it. I was told that a woman dropped fifteen of them all at once, all of them seen as such.
By the wise, all-knowing God, it is fitting that the woman know this, for perhaps such a thing will happen to her at some point, so she may receive it as is proper.
The 77th chapter.
In the delivery of a dead fetus.
If the treatment I mentioned in the section is applied to the dead fetus and it does not come out, and you are forced to intervene with your hand, then it is advisable that you look. If the woman is strong and there are no symptoms on her that she fears might be damaged by this, then the woman should lie down on a bed on her back.
And her head should be tilted downwards and her legs raised high, and a servant should hold her from both sides or tie her to the bed so that she does not move when you push the fetus.
Then she moistens the woman's vulva with wet ointments along with sputum and a poultice and linseed oil. Then she applies these ointments and poultices to the woman's hands, and then inserts them into the womb gently. She then searches for a place where the fetuses can be inserted.
Look, if the fetuses are coming down to his head then insert the instruments into his eyes or his neck or his mouth or his nose or under his chin or move them up or in places close to the shoulders or below the shoulder blades.

Until you reach something hollow then insert into it a second or third drill if needed so that the traction is uniform and does not tilt towards one side, then extend steadily without being only straight but moving in every direction.
To facilitate its removal, as is done with a tooth that has been cemented and needs to be extracted. It should be loosened in between, then the traction should be relaxed. If it joins the chest then, if not, cut on what you can. If it is below the belly and warm or has pus in it, then stop it until moisture comes out from it.
If the fetus is on its feet, then drawing it out is easy and bringing it into the womb is simple. If pressure is applied to the belly or chest, it should be drawn out with a cloth that has been wrapped around your hand and the belly or chest opened so that what is inside them will flow out.
If the rest of the organs have been removed and the head has been returned and placed, let the midwife insert her left hand. Then insert a forceps or two forceps and draw it out with them.
If the mouth of the womb has adhered to a hot tumour over it, then do not press on it, but rather in such a case use pouring wet thick things and apply poultices and sit in water that has been warmed and moistened.
And as for the fetus being on its side, if it is possible to place it straight, then apply what we mentioned concerning the living fetus. But if this cannot be done, then cut it into pieces and remove it. And it should not be left that anything of the afterbirth enters inside at all. If you have finished treating it, then apply what we mentioned concerning the treatment of the hot tumours that are exposed in the wombs.
If a hemorrhage appears, then sit down in warm water and apply the rest of the treatment. And I have seen a woman who was pregnant; her fetus died inside her, then she became pregnant again with him.
Then the other fetus also died and after a long time an ulcer appeared in her womb and swelled until it opened and made her discharge. Then I was called to treat her, and I treated her for a long time but the wound did not close, so I placed some strong adhesive unguents on it.
Then a bone came out from the place, then some days passed and another bone came out. I was amazed at that because the belly is a place where there are no bones in it. So I feared that it was from the bones of the dead fetus, so I searched the wound and took out many bones from the head of the fetus.
I did not cease following that until I extracted many bones from her and the woman was in her best conditions. And she lived for a long time, several months, from the place where the discharge is slight. It was only after arriving here that this rare thing happened to me.
Because in it there is knowledge and aid for what the healing physician endeavors with his hand from treatment,.

Chapter Seventy-eight.
On the delivery of the placenta.
If the placenta has become stuck after delivery, it is necessary to order the woman to take a breath then spit into it and grasp your hand on her mouth and nose, if it comes out in this manner, otherwise take a quantity.
And pierce a hole in the cover, place a medicine bag filled with an open poultice for the mouth of the uterus like fumitory and gentian and absinthe and papaya and myrrh and senna and cantorion, all these medicines or some of them, immerse it in water and carry it to the fire then put a silver tube on the hole of the cover and one end into the mouth of the uterus.
And hold it until the steam reaches the bottom of the uterus then spit as we said, and the placenta will come out quickly. If it remains after this treatment and does not come out, order the midwife to dip her left hand in a uterine salve or the sputum of the neck.
Then you enter it into the womb and search with it until it reaches the placenta. If it touches it, take hold of it and extend it a little at a time until it comes out. And if it is stuck in depth, insert your hand as we described until you find the placenta, then grasp it a little at a time being cautious.
So that the womb does not fall with a strong grasp, but rather it should be turned gently to the right and left sides. Then the amount of grasping is increased; thus it will loosen and get rid of the adhesion. And if the vulva was closed, we have described its treatment with fumigation, treatment of the fundament and the growths.
If it does not come out with all that we have described, then beware of being forceful on her in the re-grasping; but rather bind what has come out from it to the mouth of the womb to the thigh of the woman, then apply ointment to it. For it will rot after a few days.
It will be resolved and come out, unless it has rotted; for then it will emit a foul odor into the stomach and head. And that affliction is unpleasant; so appropriate fumigation should be used.
Therefore, and some of the first have tried burning aloeswood and dried dates. The form of the instrument with which the woman is fumigated when her menses and placenta are retained, and things like that.
It is made of lead resembling a pipe, or it is made from copper with the thin end being placed in the womb and the wide end on fire. The smoldering incense is held until it burns out and then another one is put on.
The seventy-ninth chapter.
In the treatment of an unbroken fundament.
Many male infants are born and their fundament is not perforated, rather it has been blocked by a thin membrane. The nurse should puncture that membrane with her finger, otherwise she should use a sharp spoon to cut it and be careful of the muscles lest they be damaged.
Then place on it a woolen cloth soaked in wine and oil, then treat it with ointments until it heals. If you feared it would close up, put a lead tube into the opening for several days and remove when the child wants to have a bowel movement.
And the seat may also be exposed to an ulcer or a tumor, so that opening should be cut and then treated with what we have mentioned of treatment and cautery.
The Eightieth Chapter.
In the treatment of boils that occur below.
The boils that occur below is an abscess and thickening that occurs near the anus from outside or in the rectum from one side and the boil is one or more.
If the abscess is lanced, it will open and a white or purulent watery secretion will flow from it. Some of these boils may be infected to the rectum and the intestines and will not be, and the ones that are infected can be recognized by what comes out of them in the feces and flatulence when using the enema.
And perhaps worms will come out of it. And some of them may be boils if they are infected in the rectum to the bladder and the urethra, or if they are infected to the hip joint and the anus, and what is known as the boil that is infected to the anus also from not being infected.
That you insert your index finger into the anus and insert a thin probe in the boil from copper or iron if there is no ulceration. If there is ulceration, then insert into it a lead probe or a hair of horse hair.
Until you feel the probe or the hair with your finger, if you do not feel it at all and nothing comes out of the opening from the feces or flatulence or worms as we said then know that it is not infected so hasten to treat it.
If the abscess is directed towards the bladder or the urinary tract then its sign is the urination of pus from it and the inability of the place to unite with medicines. And if it is directed towards the hip joint or the sacrum, then its sign is the reaching of the probe to there.
If there is no direction towards the bone and there is pain in a similar side and purulent discharge from it constantly, and no healing occurs in it nor does it unite with an ointment; all abscesses that are directed into the body are like this.
And its treatment is a hardship that is useless to those who take it upon themselves from the ignorant physicians. But if the abscess is not directed and not chronic, then one should hope for its healing with iron as I have described and tried, which is that you place the cauterizing instrument between your feet on his back.
You should pull his legs up and lean his thighs towards his belly, then insert a probe made of copper or lead into the abscess until you know where it ends. If the patient feels the probe towards the buttocks, then you should insert your index finger in the buttocks.
If you feel with your finger that the probe has proceeded uncovered, without feeling between it and him with flesh or fat, then know certainly that it is directed outwards, so do not tire in treating it because it will not heal as we said.
And they have said that it heals in some people rarely. And one of the treatments which hope for its benefit is to put a thin layer on top of the abscess, as mentioned above, and insert camphor into it until it reaches towards the buttocks, then return it two or three times.
Until you know that all those excess fleshes have been burned which are like a feather's tube then treat it with a moist poultice in lard until they come out, then treat it with medicinal ointments. If he heals.
And if not, then he will never recover with anything else. But if you had inserted the catheter, it did not reach your finger that was in the middle of the pelvis and between it and the catheter there was a thick veil of flesh or from fat, and you saw the navel on what followed the skin's surface then cut at once the skin from the beginning of the navel. And you pass through the incision with the catheter while it is in the navel until you reach by the incision where the end of the catheter came to an end and the catheter gets rid of itself and falls, then clean that flesh which resembles a tube of bird's feathers so nothing remains from it.
Then treat him with the medicinal ointments until he recovers. And if bleeding overpowers you and comes between you and your work, because of cutting that flesh then do the best you can and make the most benefit by burning it or with a strong drug since burning it gathers two good states: the burning of the excess flesh.
And cut the blood and ventilate the moisture, then treat him with the ointment saturated in fat or with sulphur mixed with oil until it infects the place and that burned flesh comes out in the infection. Then treat the wound at that time with the medicinal ointments planted for solid flesh.
And it is the medicines that contain opium and ventilate, for if it is suppurated then he is healed and there will be no relapse. And if the navel had reached to the depth of the pelvis and far from the surface of the body, then insert your finger in the pelvis and search with it.
For if you felt the catheter and there was a veil of fat or flesh between you and it, and it was close to coming out, then the work in that is only through greed and hope, that being that you try one of three things, either that you press him as we said.
If the anorectal fistula is split until its crater, in order to be able to introduce a tampon and treat it from close up. Do not proceed with splitting excessively lest the surrounding muscle of the rectum becomes cut off, causing involuntary defecation. Then treat it as we mentioned. It may perhaps heal like we said.
Either perform the closing of the fistula and scrape it after splitting it to near the rectum, as we said, either with a reamer or with another sharp-pointed instrument. Then cleanse all the clots in the split, wherever you can, by probing.
Then drain the discharge from all of the wound, along with the split and upper opening, until it is closed. Leave the lower aperture open inside the rectum so that it becomes easier on the patient, and sometimes the catheter will come out in this condition.
And if you have inserted the reamer into the catheter and it is on one side of the rectum towards the surface of the skin with a band around the rectum, then take at that time a hollow-tipped reamer like an Eskaf needle in this shape:.
And insert into it an open thread of five threads or about that much, then insert the reamer with the thread into the catheter until it reaches its crater. If it is found to be flowing out in the margin of the rectum from inside close by.
Then take out the thread from that hole by inserting your finger into the rectum and taking out the end of the thread. Gather both ends together, pull them tight and leave it for a day or two. Every time the thread cuts through the flesh tighten it well until those clots between the ends of the threads are cut off and fall away. Then treat the wound until it closes and heals.
If the mouth of the catheter is not draining, then drain it however you can, but do not make it deep so that it cuts the muscle, for then you will have to make a different treatment with it until it heals.
