The eighty-first chapter.
Regarding hemorrhoids from which blood flows, and cutting them, and the treatment of fissures.
Haemorrhoids will be on two kinds, either they are inside the anus resembling red pustules or like clusters of grapes and they will be small or large and blood will flow from them always.
And it will be one, and many, and will be outside the anus on its edges, except that those which are from outside the anus will be in most cases few in moisture and yellow or slightly red water will flow from them always, and they will have the colour of the body.
And the treatment of that which is from inside the anus, order the surgeon to defecate and become constipated until the anus comes out and the haemorrhoids appear to you, then hurry and grasp them with trephines or hold onto them with your fingers, then cut them at their roots. If the trephines do not stick in them due to their moisture and looseness.
Then rub it with a rough cloth or a piece of dry dung or pull on it with your fingers, then cut it, then apply some sharp cauteries to it so that they take the place of ligatures, or follow what has been mentioned in the chapter of ligatures.
Then treat it with the rest of the treatment until it heals, if the anus does not come out for you then have the surgeon inject a syringe containing a little hot water to clean inside the anus and to make it go out quickly when the patient becomes constipated, then tie the haemorrhoids that are outside the anus and order them lightly.
And it is that you take hold of it with your fingernails or tie it with trephines and cut it, then treat it as we mentioned until it heals, and if one dislikes cutting with iron, then it is advisable to use its cord in this manner: take a loose thread and insert it into the syringe.
Then bring the boil up and push it out with a needle from the opposite side. Bend the ends of the thread below the needle and tie the boil tightly, then coil the thread and pull out the needle. Do this to all boils except one that is not ripe for lancing.
So let the liquid blood drain, then put a cloth soaked in rose oil or violet on the boil and instruct the patient to be still. Then leave it until the boils drop off. If they drop off, treat them with ointments and all treatment until they heal.
And as for the treatment of ulcers, they are often exposed and held captive by the skin folds. If it has been cleaned and a medicine has not been effective in it, then it should be scraped with a lancet or your finger until it becomes soft and the top crust is removed that prevents it from healing.
Then treat it until it heals as it should. If it does not heal, repeat the procedure with a stronger scraping than the first one until it becomes necrotic and peels off. Then treat it and it will heal.
The Second Section Eighty-Nine.
In the treatment of bent nails, whether bent or not bent, and dry boils and scabies.
The nail is a round knot on the color of the body resembling the head of a nail, found in all parts of the body, especially in the lower legs and fingers, and it causes pain when walking.
It is necessary to cut around the nail and grasp with a knife or pincers and remove it from its root, then treat it. And if desired, purify it as has been mentioned in its chapter. As for dry boils, one of them is a small, rough, stuck, rounded knot on the surface of the body.
Often it is exposed in the hands of children, and its treatment may be to pull the boil and cut or cauterize it with a silk thread or hair until it falls. If you want to clean it as mentioned earlier by fire or quick remedy.
And the boils, whether turned inward or outward, can be pulled out with a device that I have described in treating the scabies. And as for scabies, it is also a small, thick blister on the surface of the body that goes deep and if it catches cold one feels something like the sting of ants within it.
And it will be in the whole body, and most of it is in the hands. And its treatment is to take a tube from the strong feather of a goose or an eagle and make that tube on the scabies until a circle of the tube surrounds it from all sides. Then turn your hand with the tube until it cuts around the scabies.
And it will go into the depth of the flesh and the scabies will come out from its roots. And if you want to do that with a copper or iron tube like this:.
Its top will be closed and movable, so that the fingers can grasp it easily. And if you want to clean the scabies as mentioned earlier with a cauterizer for boils in the book of cauterizers.
The Third and Eightieth Chapter.
In the images of devices that are used for injection in seated ulcers and diarrhea and cholera.
The syringe may be made from silver or tin or hammered or struck copper. And this device can be made small and large according to its users. So the one used to treat young children will be small and those with narrow seats or that are congested will have syringes that are very fine. The image of a large syringe:.
The top part of the syringe which connects to the tube is wide, like this shape, and has a barrier where the tube is connected as you see. The lower end of the syringe which enters the seated ulcer is closed and smooth up to the skin, with two holes on one side and one hole on the other side.
The size of the hole should be as thick as the rod or a little thicker. The tube in which medicines are placed from the bladder of an animal or from the gut of a goat is made in the shape of a small vessel and its diameter is one finger's breadth.
He makes many holes in it as it rotates, and after each hole is a thickness of a finger. Then he inserts a thin thread made from twisted yarn from ten strings or the like, and ties the tube together like a small vessel. If he places the medicine in it, then tightens the head of the syringe between the stones tightly and then injects with it. And this is the shape of the tube and the holes:.
The way to inject it is that the gut or bladder is filled with medicine while it is warmed up as much as possible for the patient, and beware that it should not be very hot or very cold, then the patient lies on his back and has his legs elevated upwards.
A cushion or mattress is placed under him, then the tip of the syringe is greased with fat or egg white or saliva from a camel's mouth or something similar. Then it is entered into the rectum gently, and the servant holds the tube with both hands and squeezes it strongly until everything in the syringe enters the intestines.
Then the syringe is removed and the patient's legs are elevated to the wall, if he feels the urge of the medicine to come out then let him hold on as long as he can, but if he sleeps through the whole night then that is the best remedy. If he was injected for diarrhea and hastened his excretion then let the injections be repeated until he recovers.
If he is in the rectum with hemorrhoids or painful ulcers, then the syringe should be very gentle and smooth like the syringes used for children. And this is an image of a soft syringe that has its skin stretched over it:.
The Fourth and Eightieth Chapter.
For the treatment of wounds.
I have mentioned in the classification of the treatment of some ulcers that I am here reminding their treatment by hand and with medicine perfectly, so I say that wounds differ according to what thing is the wound and according to the place where it falls.
The things that the wounds are with are many such as a stone splinter or cuts of sword or knife or a spear stab or stick or arrow and like that from many things.
And as for the wounds according to the places of the body, such as a wound on the head or neck or chest or belly or liver and like them from the organs.
And I am describing the treatment of some wounds to make them a measure and law for all the other wounds, and I begin with simple head wounds especially because complicated ones will be mentioned in the first part of the third chapter of this book.
And I say that if a simple wound happened in the head and there was no bone fracture, then look at it; if it was from a stone splinter or like it and the skin had been only pulled back and the wound was large and I feared the formation of an abscess, then quickly apply the poultice to the place. Do not delay doing that and bleed him according to his strength if he is prevented from being bled by an obstacle, especially if the bleeding from the wound is slight; let the bleeding be from against the injured side.
And warn the patient against filling and drinking and coarse food, for if he is prevented from being bled by an obstacle let him reduce his food and not approach meats or drinks; apply a compress to the wound if it happens that there is a hot abscess. It should be made of lint soaked in rose oil alone or with a drink containing opium.
If you have cooled the boil then bring him to the wound if it is fluid with his blood and has not been changed by the hot air which I will describe to you shortly, and as for if it has been changed by the hot air, then put some ointments on it.
Until it discharges pus then treat him until he recovers, if the wound is large and was caused by a sword or the like and its edges have not joined together with the skin then sew it up in the way I described for sewing abdominal wounds.
If the skin has been torn away from the bone and is hanging and it was not stuck except in a small place, then cut it off then treat the wound with remedies that cause hard flesh to form in its place instead of the skin and order the patient to eat nutritious foods like heads and shoulders and similar things.
If a decay occurs in the skin and it does not stick to the bone, then cut out all that is rotten and burn it up then treat him. And if there is an artery or vein bleeding blood from it and the bleeding has not stopped with medicines then search for the artery.
If it bleeds and does not stop then cut him with the forceps and tie him. And if necessity dictates and what we have mentioned does not benefit, then fill him up until the blood stops. And if these wounds are small and shallow then they are easy to treat by applying this powder on them while they are bleeding with their own blood.
Before the air changes it, the recipe of the powder is that you take a part from the opium and two parts from the aloeswood and three parts from extinguished or unextinguished clay, all crushed together, sifted and filled into the wound and tied tightly until it sticks on him with good glue.
And it is tied with the blood then bound from above with a cloth and left without being unwound as long as it does not become swollen, for indeed the treatment will not come out of him until he recovers. And the clay itself may do that if the opium and aloeswood are not available to you.
And he can also do this act on the lint in many large incisions, if he is skilled in placing and tightening it, and as long as the incisions are moist with blood without the air having changed them. But if the air has caused some change to them, especially during the summer months.
So there is no meaning in placing this lint that we mentioned, on top of it carrying some ointments or a paste made from barley flour with water and honey so as to make the pus come out then treating it with other treatments until it heals.
But if the fracture occurred with the wound, being a simple one, he should take hold of it with the lint. I have already mentioned the treatment of skull fractures in what is to be resumed about neck surgery. If the wound occurs in the neck, there is no difference in the treatment between this and a simple head wound.
And if a vertebra or artery has been cut, then there is no trick in it except that he should avoid treating it with a tight compress like the rope and the cord and similar things because they irritate the nerve and displace it.
And nothing cold should be put on the wound at all because of the cold nature of the nerve and its connection with the brain, which is the most noble of organs. And what he should treat it with from the oily medicines like the washed and dissolved powder in sweet water or oil or rose and vetch resin.
If it is also washed with sweet water and the other metal stones in this manner, and moist ointments. And if the wound is large, he should use suturing or bind his lips with lint then treat it until it heals.
If the wound has a depth and an abscess has formed at its bottom which has accumulated pus, he should tie it in the lowest part of it. And if an artery is cut off in the wound and its blood flows out, he should ligate it or bind it or cauterize it if necessity demands that.
If the wound has cut some or all of the ligaments of the neck and the arteries have been severed, gather the edges of the skin with a stitch on the trachea. Do not touch the trachea but rather suture it and shape it to its natural form and then tighten it tightly and leave it for several days.
Then treat it with poultices that contain papyrus and drying until it heals. If the wound has affected the bone, clean out the bone. If there are fragments of bone in it, extract all of them or as much of them as possible, and if you cannot do so then leave it alone until the wound heals and dries up and becomes easy to remove.
If the wound is suppurating, place on it the ointments which we have described. If a bone becomes encrusted in the wound and becomes as hard as a rock, treat it with what will be mentioned in its chapter, in thoracic surgery and between the shoulders.
If the wound is from a spear or dagger and you see it has an entrance but no exit, look; if air comes out of it when the patient breathes, know that it is a fighting wound. If it does not have an exit and was flowing with blood, do not place any poultice in it at first and do not tighten it lest the blood become trapped inside its depths.
It will lead to the heart and kill the patient, but place in it a wet poultice and apply it during the day twice. If you do not have a poultice, place in the mouth of the wound a thick cotton cloth so that it absorbs the moisture coming out of it, and make the patient sleep on top of the wound.
The pus that accumulates in it will drain, and if the wound has been three days or more since its occurrence and the patient's pulse has returned to normal and there is no fever or difficulty breathing and you see their condition good then know that the wound is safe. Treat it with honey and treat the rest of the treatment until it heals.
If the sight is obstructed and a probe is extended constantly, know that it has become dislodged from its place. The physician should let out what accumulates in the wound; if the chest or back wound has passed to where one has stitched as mentioned earlier.
If it is large or has purulent discharge, if it is small, the wound should be searched and act quickly to remove those fragments if they are septic; if they are not septic then leave them alone until.
The wound should heal; then it will be easier to remove them, and as for the other wounds occurring in other organs let their treatment be like what we have mentioned.
Chapter 84.
On a wound of the abdomen and evacuation of faeces and its suturing.
The rupture which exposes the abdomen may be large, small or middle-sized. The large one may discharge faeces or several intestines, making their insertion and suturing more difficult and harder.
And the small rupture also may be difficult in another way, requiring its return to be more difficult. And if faeces do not hurry to insert it into its place at its time it will swell and thicken, making it harder to insert. Therefore, the best ruptures are the medium-sized ones, because their return does not become as difficult as in these two types.
Know that suturing the abdomen is on four sides, two general types are suitable for suturing the abdomen and other wounds of the body, and the last two special types are specifically for suturing the abdomen.
And I will describe them to you one by one with explanation. So, I say if the wound is small and something from the faeces has come out of it and its return is difficult then that is for one of two reasons, either because of the smallness of the rupture as we said or because the intestine has been exposed to inflation by the cold air.
If so, then it is necessary to soften it by dipping a sponge or wet cloth into warm water alone, or by boiling in theriac and saffron and citron, and then pouring the decoction onto it until the gas escapes.
And he can do this with a drink that has aloes, and it is better than water alone in breaking the gas. If you see the gas has dissipated, then pour into the container water that has been boiled with licorice or baker's yeast, because it becomes calm on entry by easier passage.
And if it is difficult to return to it after this treatment, then slightly cut through the cloth with a tool that cuts leather flasks. The first treatment, if successful, is better than cutting and it is only necessary to cut when necessity requires and the device fails, and here is the picture of the tool.
Its single bend is limited and the other direction is unlimited, and the thin end will not be as sharp as the scalpel but rather a little thicker. It is a tool similar to the small cauter in appearance, as you see. If the wound becomes swollen and the container enters, then its return should be on its natural shape.
And its proper place for it, if you can, is better. But if the wound is wide and in the lower abdomen, then the patient should lie on his back and let his legs be higher than his head. And if it is in the upper abdomen, he should have his head and chest higher than his lower parts.
And also, if the wound is in one side of the abdomen, then always keep that side higher than the other. And so it should be used in great wounds and middle-sized ones.
And as for small wounds, then place it as you are able to, and then prepare a skilled assistant to take hold of the cloth entirely with his hands and gather its edges. Then he should expose bit by bit to the seamstress.
This is the description of general suturing and it is that one takes a needle or several needles according to the size of the wound, then leaves on one side of the incision as thick as the thickness of the forceps, and inserts a single thread without threading a suture in the edges of the skin. With the edges of the peritoneum which is under the skin from inside until they are pierced from that side and I have joined the two layers of skin and the two layers of the peritoneum and it became four folds, then draw with a doubled thread around the needle in all sides several times until the edges of the wound meet firmly.
Then leave also as thick as the finger and insert another needle then entwine it with the thread as was done with the first needle so continue doing that as many needles as needed until you have finished all of the wound and let the needles be moderate between thickness and thinness.
Because the thin needles are very quick to cut through flesh and thick ones have difficulty entering the skin, therefore it should be moderate in thickness and fineness. And it is not suitable that the needle penetrates into the edge of the skin closely.
So that the flesh does not quickly tear and the wound opens before it is sewn together, nor does it stretch too far with sewing so that the wound will refuse to heal. Then cut off the ends of the needles so that they do not hurt the surgeon when he sleeps and make for him a pad of linen rags from each side to hold the ends of the needles.
And leave them until he knows that the wound has healed, and this type of stitching with needles is most suitable for small wounds because it may be sufficient to sew them with one or two needles or something similar.
Or if the suture of general type is second, then gather with stitching the four folds, namely the two layers of skin and the two layers of peritoneum at once with a needle containing a moderately twisted thread in thickness and fineness, then when they were penetrated by this needle pull back the needle from the side where it started.
The thread is tied from above the wound so that the stitching is as per the stitch of a pouch which holds an object and one stitch is placed between each pair of stitches after thickening with the small finger, this stitch is well-known to all people.
With this stitch, an operation was performed on a man who had cut in his abdomen with a knife, the wound was more than a span and had exited from its pouch by about two spans of the middle pouch and the hole was in the middle of the abdomen.
Then I took him after keeping his pouches outside the wound for twenty-four hours, and the wound closed in about fifteen days and I treated him until he was completely cured and lived many years afterwards managing all his affairs, and the doctors used to give judgment on him that he would not be cured at all.
And it was amazing that I did not treat him with a dressing because I was in a place where there was no medicine, so I used to put on the wound two balls of cotton during the day and promise him to wash it with honey water until he recovered.
And as for one of the types of stitching which is particular to me, I mention it according to a literal statement by Galen that you start with the stitch from the skin and insert the needle from outside to inside, so if the needle has been carried out through the skin and through the muscle going in straightness throughout the whole abdomen.
I left the edge of the peritoneum in the side where I inserted the needle and carried out the needle in its other edge from inside to outside on the other edge of the fold, so if I carried it out then I carried it out again in this same edge itself from the fold from outside to inside.
And I left the edge of the peritoneum in this side and carried out the needle in its other edge from inside to outside, and I carried it out with carrying it into the peritoneum as far as the fold in his side until it is all carried out in it.
Then I also began from this side with it and drew the needle with the suture which is in the other side of the peritoneum, extracted the needle from the skin next to it, then returned it into that skin, drew a suture of the peritoneum which is on the other side together with this suture of the marker.
And I extracted it from the skin on his side, and I did this again another time and I did it once after another until all of the wound was sewn up in that way, the whole description of this suturing is to suture the seams of the furriers for the fur.
That the peritoneum should be sewn once from one side with the edge of the skin and that it should be left once from the other side until it is empty, and as for the second type of suturing which Galen also mentioned this is his word exactly.
And it is that they are sewn as the people of treatment sew them by gathering every part to its counterpart which has problems with it, so they bring together the edge of the peritoneum to its other edge and the edge of the marker to its other edge, this will be as I have described to you.
It is necessary that the needle should be pierced in the edge of the marker which is near you from outside and it should be done inside alone and leave the edges of the peritoneum then return the needle and pierce it from outside to inside in both edges of the peritoneum then also return it.
And it should be done from inside to outside in the edge of the other marker which is in the opposite side, and this type of suturing is better than the general easy suturing which I mentioned earlier, and this is the word of Galen exactly, and some of them said that the peritoneum may heal with two needles. And that is to put one thread in it and start by putting the needle from you and doing it through to the other side, and put another needle from the opposite side so that it comes out from you just like the suturing of the shoemakers.
Know that the incision in the middle of the abdomen is more difficult to suture than any other area of the belly. As for treating the wound, its treatment is like that of all wounds, namely: if you encounter the wound fresh with blood before the air changes it and you take the spoon, draw a line and tighten it firmly then apply the sticky resin.
If the wound has changed by the air, place some prepared poultice on it so that it becomes septic and the threads fall apart and the omentum and the peritoneum unite, then treat it like treating your other wounds until it heals.
If you do not have the necessary remedies, place on it since it becomes septic the absorbent cotton wool and change it twice a day as I have taught you until it heals. For in most cases if the wounds are simple, you will not need any other treatment; but if you fear that the wound may affect the main organs with pain.
It is necessary to soak linen wool in lukewarm oil or rose oil and place it around the places between the armpit and the groin. If you feel pain or decay in the abscess, often that one will discharge; rinse it with black cold tea drink.
And especially if the decay has reached in the abscess and become an open wound to its depth. Know that what was thick from the intestines is easier to heal and what was thin from them is harder to heal.
And as for the abscess known as Al-Sa'im, it does not accept healing from any surgery that touches it at all because of its many and thick veins and its softness and proximity to the nature of the nerve. But if what protruded from the wound was a purulent liquid and you received it fresh, return it like your returning the abscess.
If a period has passed and it has turned green or black, one should tie a thread above the place where it turned black so that bleeding is not exposed. For in the wound there are vessels and sinews; then cut what is below this bandage.
And make the ends of the thread hanging from below the incision outside so that it is easy for you to pull and remove when the crust falls off and the wound becomes foul. Mentioning a wound which shows in the anus, if a small tear appears in the anus.
For it is possible that in some people it may become gangrened because of a spear thrust which I saw, so that a man had become gangrened in his belly and there was an incision on the right side of the stomach. I treated him by cauterizing the wound and it became purulent with stool and gas coming out of it, so I treated him accordingly as I did not have hopes for his recovery. I did not stop cauterizing it until he healed and the place closed up. When I saw that the place had closed, I was afraid that a worse accident might occur inside him but no such bad accident happened to him at all and he remained in his best state. True, he eats and drinks and copulates and enters the bath and serves him, and some people of experience have mentioned that if a small tear appears in the anus, it is to be cauterized like this.
And it is that the large ants with red heads are taken, then the edges of the wound are brought together, and an ant is placed on them, with its mouth open, on the edges of the wound. If it closes its jaws tightly, cut off its head and it will adhere without coming apart; then another ant is placed close to the first one.
And it still does that with many ants as much as the wound, then turn it over and sew the wound. For those red heads will stick to the anus until it heals and becomes clear without any further harm to the anal region. And it is also possible for the anus itself to be sutured with fine thread.
What is taken from the sinew of an animal that is glued to it after it enters into a needle, is yes; this end of the thread is taken and attached to it a very thin and twisted flaxen thread, then that thread is entered into the needle. There is a thread of sinew which is sewn with the intestines and then returned to the body, and this kind of sewing with beeswax and sinew is only for hope and desire.
And if the rent is large and wide, especially if it is in one of the rectum-like intestines, there is no remedy for it at all.
Chapter 88.
For the treatment of fever and colic.
Know that every ulcer or tumor, if it heals and ages and becomes a carbuncle, and the pus constantly flows without stopping, is called in general a colic wherever it was located, and we call it fever.
It is a hard white abscess with no pain in it, having a cavity like the cavity of bird's down.
And for this reason, some of them called it "bird's down", and it can be a liquid that constantly discharges pus, and sometimes the liquid may stop, and the amount of this liquid can be much or little, thick or thin.
And I mentioned in the classification when talking about wounds, that every carbuncle which does not heal and does not form healthy flesh within it, is for one of nine reasons: either because there is a lack of blood in the body, or because it is encased, or because there is hardened flesh inside it and on its edges preventing good flesh from growing. Or because it is many and dirty, or because the carbuncle itself has badness and the material that fills it is of poor quality, or because the treatment does not agree in its cure, or because there was corruption in the city from the kind of plague, or because of a peculiarity in the city.
Or because it is many and dirty, or because the carbuncle itself has badness and the material that fills it is of poor quality, or because the treatment does not agree in its cure, or because there was corruption in the city from the kind of plague, or because of a peculiarity in the city. In the city of Zaragoza, where diseases take a long time to mature and ulcers heal slowly by nature; either because there is a single bone or several bones. I have mentioned all these causes, their signs and treatments with medicines in the classification.
And here I have to inform you about the treatment of abscesses and catarrhs which occur by the hand, know that abscesses occur in all parts of the body; some of them reach large ulcers and veins or nerves.
Or to a sac or to the bladder or to the urinary tract or to a rib among ribs or to a vertebra among the vertebrae of the back or to a joint from the composite joints such as the hand and foot; and some lead to a nearby main organ in this manner.
And whatever of these abscesses is in this condition it is a difficult disease to treat which does not accept treatment and intervention because of its difficulty and ignorance. If one of the abscesses has not reached the places I mentioned, wished and hoped for its treatment.
And I wanted you to know that, take a probe of copper or iron if the abscess passes straight, and probe it with it; and if the abscess is tortuous, probe it with a leaden probe because lead makes its body soft.
So it will be discharged upon entering and will turn towards the tortuosity; if the abscess has many openings which you cannot probe with a probe, inject one of its mouths and one of them, because the moisture that you inject into it will flow towards the other openings and discharge.
Then again investigate the probing in any way you can to know if there is a bone or nerve; or was the abscess deep or close, or were there several abscesses with many openings and be aware of all that within your ability to perceive through the pain when you press with your finger on the place.
You look at all the signs and causes of the tumor, so if you have looked at everything with certainty, then trust in the treatment, which is to look.
The abscess is apparent, near or in a healthy place, far from a joint or nerve or artery or vein or one of the places mentioned to you. Cut the abscess as described above and remove what is inside it of pus, bad meat and excessive meat.
And what grows in his mouth from flesh or boil and similar things, treat it until it heals. If the abscess is deep-seated and was straight then you should cut it deeply as much as possible and then clean him of all bad flesh.
Then use the rotten poultice in sharp medicines and pour it into the bottom of the abscess which you reach with an iron, do that until it eats that sharp medicine all what remains in the bottom of the abscess from corruption.
Then force him with the ointments that cause flesh to grow correctly until he heals. And if he doesn't heal with that, then do it as its description was mentioned above. And if the reason for the abscess is a bone and you knew this, then excise it and cut it as I informed you, unless something prevents you.
Bone or nerve or main organ as we said, and if the bone is revealed to you and it has some corruption and blackness then take it out until its corruption goes away, then treat him with what will cover his flesh until he heals. And if he doesn't heal and the pus accumulates as it used to.
And know that you have not reached the complete removal of corruption, so cut all what is on him again and take out his contents thoroughly with your utmost effort then force him. And if he heals, otherwise know that this corruption is deep inside from the other corruption, so cut all what is on him again.
Examine his leg thoroughly and carefully. If the bone is rotten, treat it as a small piece of bone and if possible to remove it then take it out with soft calabashes suitable for that purpose.
If there are many bones then examine their extraction carefully and do not leave any of them; if some ligaments hinder you from taking it out, and cutting into them is not dangerous, cut those ligaments and the flesh that may be over it and clear the bones.
If you cannot extract the bones within your time, load onto the wound what will cleanse it and leave it for a few days until the flesh and ligaments surrounding those bones decay; preserve the wound so that the cut which you made during your work does not close up.
Place on it some linen dipped in sulphur powder with oil or some linen dipped in the Egyptian ointment or one of the green ointments; then when those ligaments decay and the bones are softened, it will be easy to remove and extract them.
If there is one big bone, such as the tibia or femur and the like, which has decayed from only one side, scrape it thoroughly so that the blackness and decay go away then close the wound; if what has decayed from it is a large part and the decay has reached inside the bone, its removal is necessary.
And cut it all the way to where the decay ends; then treat it until it heals, and I inform you of an ulcer that was shown to a young man in his leg as an example and guidance for your treatment. This man was young.
For a man near thirty years, an inflammation appeared in his leg because of movement inside the body until the materials adhered to the leg and swelled with a large abscess which was not caused by something from outside; then time passed along with the mistakes of the physicians until the abscess burst open.
Materials were extracted from it in abundance, but its treatment was so poor that the leg became gangrenous and numerous openings appeared on it, all discharging pus and bodily secretions. Many physicians struggled with it for two years, but none among them was skilled with manual work.
Until I decided to look at it, and I saw his leg, and the materials were flowing from those openings in great quantity; the man had eaten away a part of his body and turned yellow. So I inserted the instrument into one of the openings, and the instrument went through to the bone, then I searched all the openings.
I found that some of them were connected to each other from all parts of the leg. I probed and incised one of those openings until I exposed some bone, and I found it to be putrid, having clotted, turned black and rotten until the hole went through to the brain; then I drained what was revealed to me.
I was able to remove the putrid bone, and I think that there is no bone except for the putrid one which I cut and drained. Then I made him apply a dressing of strong medicines over the wound for a longer period so it wouldn't heal; then I went back and uncovered the bone again, above the first incision.
I found that the putridness was connected to the bone, so I drained what appeared to me also from that putridness. Then I made him reapply a dressing and it didn't heal nor cover; then I uncovered him also and it didn't close. So I kept cutting away parts of the bone little by little and making him apply dressings but it wouldn't heal until I cut out about a palm's width from the bone.
And I extracted it with his brain, then I made him apply dressings and he healed quickly and was cured. But this repetition in the operation and incision was because of the weakness of the patient's constitution and his inability to withstand, and my fear that he would die on me because of vomiting too much, a very weak red liquid that became clear completely.
A lump of dense flesh has formed in the place of the bone. Its condition had improved, its power had decreased and it had been behaving abnormally without being exposed to a condition that would harm it, but if there is a fractured bone in some part of the body.
It should be spread over this condition and it should take a bandage and pull it to the fractured bone end and order someone to hold it upwards and make another bandage from thicker wool than the first one.
Then tie it on the flesh under the bone and extend its end so that the flesh is pulled down and you expose the flesh to the place where you want to spread it, lest the file harm the flesh. And put a wooden wedge or board firmly under the bone from below.
Because if you do that, the file will not be prevented from cutting the rotten bone. And it is necessary for the spread to be a little above the place of decay so that the decay inside the bone does not show in its surface for the sense, so you are forced to spread again.
If the bone is rotten but not fractured, rather it connects some of its parts to each other and there is decay in the middle or in some of its parts, then you remove the flesh from all sides, then put the wooden wedge below, then spread him on the first side where the decay is.
If you have finished spreading it, then spread him from the other side and let the spread be a little away from the decay as we said. If there is decay in a joint, cut out the rotten joint itself and spread the bone where it connects from the other side.
If the decay is in the connection of two joints, there is no remedy for it. If the decay is in the palm or sole of the foot, the matter of its treatment is very difficult but you should scrape off the decay as soon as it appears to you and clean it out and wash it however you can.
When you are to set a bone, if the skin or nerve does not interfere with you, and know that splints and bandages are used for cutting these bones in accordance with the position of the bones, their setting and thickening, roughness, size, suppleness, and disjointedness. Therefore, it is necessary that you provide an instrument for each type of work.

Chapter Seventy-eight.
In cutting limbs and spreading bones.
The limbs may decay either from a cause outside or from a cause inside, so if you treated that decay with the treatment of medicine and the treatment did not cure it and you saw the decay spreading in the member without being stopped by anything.
So you should cut that member to where the decay has reached, so that the patient may be saved from death or a great calamity which is greater than losing the member; and a sign that it has been shown to him is that the member becomes blackened until you think fire has burned it.
Or it may decay after becoming black until the decay spreads to what is behind that member and takes possession of the body altogether, so hasten to cut it; similarly if the cause of the decay was due to being bitten by some venomous creatures such as the scorpion or snake or lizard etc.
If the decay or bite is in the tip of a finger, cut off the finger and do not wait for the decay to spread to the hand; similarly if it has taken possession of the hand, cut it from the wrist without waiting for the decay to spread until it takes possession of the arm.
And similarly if it has taken possession of the arm, cut off the arm at the elbow in the joint itself; and if the decay spreads and you see it reaching towards the shoulder, do not cut off the shoulder at all because that would be the death of the patient, and use instead another treatment according to his strength.
Also do the same with a man if the corruption took place in the finger, cut off the finger at one of the joints, and if it took place in the male's comb, cut off the leg entirely. If it rose to the knee, cut the thigh at the knee joint.
And if the corruption has reached above the knee, there is no remedy but to leave it and let the cause of corruption lead to death. The formula for cutting off a member or releasing it is that you draw a bandage at the bottom of the place which you want to cut off and tie another bandage above the place.
A servant holds the lower bandage down and another servant holds the upper bandage up, while you strip off the meat in between with a broad knife until all the flesh is exposed then cut or release, and it should be placed from all sides khatan gauze.
So that the knife doesn't touch the correct place and cause additional pain and inflammation, if there is bleeding in your work, take the place quickly or put some cutting pads on it then go back to your treatment until you finish.
Then bind the injured member with a bandage that is suitable for it and treat it until it heals, and I am telling you an example presented to a man in his leg, this remedy with its eye which I have described to you, and it happened to him in his leg blackness with heat like fire.
And that corruption was the first thing to happen in his finger until he took all of it, and when the man saw the corruption seeking in the member with intensity of what he found from pain and heat, he cut it off at the joint so it healed.
When a long time had passed, the corruption presented itself to him with its eye in his other hand's pinky finger, so he came to me and I applied the remedy that I had brought to him on his body after cleaning it. But the corruption did not stop and started seeking in the other finger.
Until I took him by the hand with ulcers and begged me to cut off his hand, I refused on my behalf to conceal this fault, and I also feared for him at the time of cutting his hand death, because the man's strength was about falling over, so when I gave up hope he departed to his country.
It was told to me that he was able only after cutting his hand completely was cleared, and I only mentioned this story as a help for what happens from the kind of this disease and as an example which is relied on and worked upon.
The Eighth and Eighty Chapter.
In the treatment of ulcers and how to inject them with medicines.
If an abscess occurs in some of the venous organs and its duration prolonged until its duration accumulated then it burst or ruptured and all that was in it of pus remained and the place became empty as if it were a vessel.
And the skin over it like a cloth had rotated and was not very rotten that it affected bone or nerve or tendon, hence it deserved to be called an abscess and not ulcers unless its duration prolonged until the corruption affects something of these organs.
So then it is called ulcers or zekama, and its treatment is to cut off that skin completely as it rotates, and especially if it has rotated and become like a cloth and it was certain that it does not adhere to the place due to its rottenness.
So if I hoped that the skin would adhere and it was not rotten to that degree, and there was a thickness of flesh in the skin which activates its treatment with an injection, which is that you look at the abscess, if it is large and the pus emanating from it has a strong odor, inject it with Egyptian medicine.
Which is kohl and oil and honey and zingiber, in equal parts gathered together in a vessel and cooked on the fire until the medicine thickens and comes to be like a thickness of honey, then take from it what you need and dissolve it with water and honey, and inject it into the abscess and close its mouth and leave the medicine in it for as long as two hours.
Then take it out at dawn. It will come out after a few days until the cavity is cleaned and the impurity has gone, and if this medicine is not available to you, moisten it with ash water. Take the ashes of grapevine or walnut wood and mix them with water.
Then arrange it and irrigate with it until you are certain that the cavity has been cleaned, if there is no hope for the Egyptian medicine or ash water then irrigate it with honeyed water in which a thing of ground galena has been mixed.
Or plug it with honey and drink mixed together because the honey can purify and clean, and the drink closes the cavity, especially if the drink contains a sediment that has thickened and congealed. If you do this several times and have confirmed that the impurity of the cavity has gone, then irrigate it with what brings growth to the flesh.
Such as taking from the simple ointment and mixing it with rose honey and a constricting drink or plugging it with some of the other medicines and ointments whose properties we have mentioned in the treatise on ointments. If the mouth of the cavity is narrow and does not fit with the irrigating tube.
So bind it with a little iron or place in him a powder that has been mixed in the Egyptian ointment or the srigon ointment until it is widened. And also if the mouth is too wide bring his lips together by stitching and leave from it as much as the irrigating tube enters without excess.
And also if the mouth through which the pus is flowing is raised upwards then cut it in a lower place so that the pus may flow out downwards, because if the pus becomes congealed in the depth of the cavity prevents flesh from growing in it.
And if you are unable to cut the cavity towards its lower part as you wish then construct a support for the organ so that the pus may flow out easily from it, and do not let any of the pus remain in it whatever.
As for the medicinal pastes which are put on the hidden place from outside and how to put them on it, take a paste of your choice and apply it to a linen cloth so that the whole thing is covered by it. Then cut it with scissors opposite to the mouth of the abscess a hole slightly wider than the mouth of the abscess. Then take some of the soft paste and apply it to another cloth on the size of the hole, then place it over it in a different position from the mouth of the abscess so that it may be easy for the pus to come out and do not remove the large cloth except afterwards.
A number of days, and as for the one on the mouth of the abscess it is to be taken off at all times so that what has accumulated in it from pus may come out and you may know how much liquid or thick or bloody or not bloody there is.
And also examine the place of the abscess itself whether its owner feels pain in it or not and whether there is a swelling or not in it. If your treatment has reached this point and you have seen that the matter which comes out on the mouth of the abscess is slight.
Then know that the abscess has adhered or is about to adhere. So dissolve it with vinegar on the third day or tomorrow and when you have cleansed the wound, replace the cloth with a new one and renew the ointment. If matter comes out from the abscess after a long time being liquid, do not despair that it will coagulate.
The recovery will be near because there are people whose flesh takes a long time to heal in their wounds and others who are the opposite of that. If matter comes out from the abscess after many days being not bloody pus, then know that the abscess has not coagulated, for if the coagulation of the abscess is delayed.
And if the matter takes a long time, add moisture to the drying of the remedies and let them be in a consistency that is wet and in strength dry like the ointment of aloes resin, if it has been increased in it. And among the most effective treatments is to take the ointment of aloes resin.
He cures with a concoction of rose and sprinkles over it the old wine in moderation. He mixes them together and uses it, and he may do this act if he does not have the ointment made from the resin of acacia tree honey, if he has cooked it until it is well combined and used it. Or he takes a mixture of myrrh, storax, and aloeswood, crushes all of them together and sprinkles over it on the honey that is on fire. Then he applies it to a cloth and binds him to the hiding place or anoints with the honey that he has cooked until it thickens, sprinkles over it medicines and puts on a cloth and binds him.
And he may use in the same manner long zirahwand, and the root of esfand and angelica, and the powder of kerseneh and the isolated or grouped quintarine that has been crushed, sieved and sprinkled on the honey that I have described and used. If the affair of the hideout is prolonged and it does not recover with this treatment then know that in its depths there is corruption.
And it may affect the bones or any of the hard nerves or tendons a treatment with aloes as mentioned previously.
The Ninetieth Chapter.
In the treatment of tetanus and infected abscess, cutting the excess finger and splitting the fingers that are stuck together.
Tetanus is a thick flesh that grows under the thumb nail of the hand or foot and perhaps in other fingers, if its affair is prolonged and it is neglected, it becomes swollen and hot.
Or it becomes rotten and gangrenous until the base of the nail is eaten away and perhaps all of it becomes rotten and the decay reaches the bone so that it has a foul odor, and the tip of the finger becomes swollen and its color changes to blue. If you treat him with what we mentioned in the classification and he does not recover from your treatment.
It is necessary to cut with iron all the pustules that sprout from the nail, and then to cauterize the wound after that. For cauterizing in this case is very beneficial. But if the bone was sound and also the nail was sound.
And if the angle that contains the nail had constricted the flesh towards the inside and made it become necrotic, then it is necessary to put a thin probe under the angle of the nail that has constricted the flesh and lift it up and cut that flesh gently.
And she puts on the remaining flesh from the incendiary medicines that are effective until it all goes away, and then treats him with ointments until he recovers. And if corruption has affected the bone, it is necessary to cut out that bone and remove it because it will not recover as long as there is a corrupt bone in it.
If you see the inflammation and corruption moving in the finger, cut it off at one of its joints as was mentioned earlier and treat it until it recovers. And if the nail is struck by a blow or hurt and severe pain occurs in it, then relieve the pressure first.
Then cut the nail with a sharp lancet an oblique incision from top to bottom, and be careful not to reach with the cut to the flesh under the nail because you will cause severe pain in the pressure point and it will be a reason for the growth of excessive flesh in the place then treat the place with what calms the pains.
And as for the extra finger that is formed in some people's hands, it may be all flesh, or in some of it there may be bones, and sometimes it may have a nail, and some of it may grow from the joint of some fingers.
Or its growth may be in some joints of the fingers and those that grow in some joints of the fingers do not move, and those that grow at the joint of the finger perhaps it moved. So cut what is of flesh only it will come out easily, and this by cutting it at its root with a blunt lancet.
As for the one that grows in the joint's origin, its treatment is difficult; therefore, refrain from cutting it. But as for the one that grows in the finger at the level of a joint, it should first be cut with a curved incision into the bone, then have the bone spread apart with one of those instruments suitable for this purpose.
Then treat it until it heals. And as for the adhesion that brings fingers together with each other, often this occurs in a person who is born with it or due to damage of a wound or burning by fire and the like; therefore, you should cut through this adhesion.
Until the fingers return to their natural state, then place between them a piece of cloth or netting soaked in rose oil so that they do not adhere quickly; or separate them and put a thin sheet of tinplate between them until the place heals as it should.
And also if the adhesion is exposed to some of the fingers by the palm, cut through that adhesion as it becomes suitable and suitable for the shape of the member.
Chapter Ninety.
On Cutting Tumors.
The doulai are twisted blood vessels filled with clotted black blood which occur in most parts of the body and most often occur in the legs, especially in those who have a tendency to fatigue and weakness. It is necessary first that the body be washed with the black soap several times vigorously.
Then bleed the owner of it, and as for treating them with iron there are two ways: one is to cut and let out the black blood, and the other is to have the vein release and come out entirely. As for cutting, first warm the leg with hot water.
Until the thick black blood liquefies, then pull up the leg of the afflicted from above his knee to below it with a bandage, then cut the vein in one place or two places or three cuts wide.
Then you will let out the black blood with your hand from below the leg to above and from above to below until it comes out of the blood what seems sufficient or as much force the instrument can then tie it and order it to abstain from foods produced for the black bile. Then repeat suction and leeching.
When the veins become full and harm the instrument, as for its cure it is to shave the leg of the instrument if it has much hair then immerse its leg in hot water until it reddens or there is a strong sweating.
If it does not become warm with the bath until the part becomes hot, then cut the skin over the sweat longitudinally either at its end near the knee or below at the ankle, then open the skin with scalpels and scrape off the sweat from all sides until it appears to the touch.
And when it appears, you will see it red and swollen, if it is freed from the skin then you will also see it like a cord, then insert under it an instrument until it rises and comes out of the skin, tie it with a blind and smooth instrument, then cut another incision about that incision by three fingers.
Then scrape the skin off from over the cord until it appears, then lift it up with the instrument as you did and tie it with another instrument just like you did first, then cut another incision or many incisions if you need that.
Then pull it and cut it at the end of the incision near the ankle, then pull it and let it out until it comes out of the second incision, then pull it to the incision above it and do that until you pull it from the third incision above all the incisions together, when they all come out then cut it.
If it does not yield to a probe with strong double thread and pulling, then insert an iron stylus under the skin and rotate your hand in all directions until it emerges. Take care that it does not break off; if it breaks off, it will be very difficult for you to extract it.
It enters into the wound an inflammation. If you have made him bleed all, put on place of the cuts a wool moistened in rose water or red oil or fat and treat him until he heals. If the sinew is twisted with folds and a knot to one side.
But it was not straight as we said, you must cut on each of its folds and places of twisting, then tie them with thread until they are all aligned. Take care when cutting into it that you do not cut the tendon or bruise it; for if you do, it will be difficult for you to extract it and you will exhaust yourself.

It should not have a hook like the other sewing needles, nor be sharp at the end lest it cut the tendon and bruise it. It should be thick in the bend smooth so that if it is thin it cuts the tendon with its roughness; but let its thickness be as we said.
The Ninetieth Chapter.
For the extraction of the tendon that is slack.
This tendon is generated in the legs in hot countries such as Hijaz and the lands of the Arabs, and in the hot temperate regions with little rainfall. It may also be generated in other places on the body besides the legs and it is generated due to an inflammation that occurs under the skin.
As it occurs in the living bodies, the worm, and the tapeworm, and the flea and the worm that is generated between the skin and flesh. A sign of the beginning of this tendon's occurrence is that there is severe inflammation in one leg then it subsides, then the tendon begins to come out from that place of inflammation.
As if it were the root of a plant or an animal, if its end appears, one should wrap it on a small piece of lead whose thickness is from half a dirham to a dirhem and tie it up. Then leave the lead hanging from the leg.
Whenever anything comes out of it to the outside, wrap it in lead and tie it. If it lasts long, cut some of it off and wrap the rest. Do not cut it from its origin before all of it has come out, for if you do so, it will contract and enter into the flesh, causing a bad ulcer and inflammation at the site and an ugly wound.
For that reason, it should be pulled out and pulled little by little until all of it has come out, without anything remaining inside the body. And in some people, what comes out from this abscess may reach a length of five ells and ten.
And it has been reported to me that in a man, twenty spans came out. If the abscess breaks off for you during your treatment of him, insert a rod into its cavity and insert a cloth, a long one with the body, so that all the matter contained within it is evacuated. Then try to clean the site with medicines for a few days.
Then treat it with the treatment of boils. This abscess may have many ramifications, especially if it appears in a joint of the leg or in the leg itself; it will then develop many mouths and each mouth will discharge a branch that causes it pain, as we mentioned in the classification and what has been said before.
Chapter Ninety-Two.
Concerning the cut for worms that come forth under the skin and is called the sickness of cattle.
This disease is called in some of our countries the sickness of cattle, because it often affects cows; it is a small worm that is generated between the skin and flesh and moves up and down throughout the body.
The abscess becomes apparent to the touch when it is punctured from one member to another until it bursts whereever it burst in the skin, coming out and forming pus from some of the humors as it is exposed to maggots and living creatures and love's boil in the belly.
And the consequence of her damage is that if she boils in the body and rises to the head and reaches the eye, it may open there and come out and destroy the eye; this often occurs. If you want to treat her and have her come out, this happens only when she is punctured and becomes apparent to the touch.
You should tie tight a bandage over what is above her and below her, then cut into her and take it out; if she burrows into the flesh and you do not find it, carry hot coals to the place until they burn her. And more than what we said is feared, that she will corrupt the eye.
If you see it in the head close to the eye, tie under it a tight bandage on the forehead then cut into her and take it out. It is advisable for the doctor to cleanse his body with easy remedies for the foul humors and abstain from nutrient-giving foods that foster corruption.
Chapter Ninety-Three.
In the incision for the disease known as the abscess-maker.
This disease which is known in our land as the abscess-maker is a pain that appears in some organs then moves from organ to organ and I have seen it as I described to you.
I was called to an old woman in some villages, I uncovered her arm and inflated it with a small puff of air through the vein of the arm. As soon as a minute passed I saw that puff moving along with the bandage like a worm advancing upward towards her armpit as quickly as possible.
If it moves from one place to another, the pain leaves that spot and settles in the shoulder. Then I sat for an hour while he moved through the entire body until he reached the other arm. Then she told me that her whole body was spinning as I had seen.
I was amazed at the speed of his movement from limb to limb, and I had never seen this disease so clearly before. Except that I saw a group of people who found the pain moving from limb to limb but I didn't see it like I did in this woman.
And I didn't consider it (a normal movement of the pain) except that the woman was a Bedouin, her body rough and her veins exposed. So the heat of the disease moved in this way, and it should not appear like this on people who are well-nourished and have soft bodies with hidden veins.
If you wanted to treat him and he felt pain, then it would appear to you clearly as we have mentioned. So bind the wooden roller above and below him and pass over him until that congested heat comes out and the place is cleared.
And if you didn't see it clearly, then treat him by sprinkling his body with the body-rubbing agents which expel and drive out the heat, such as mint paste and similar medicines.
The Fourth Section Ninety.
In Removing Arrows.
Arrows can vary according to their kinds and the places they are lodged in the body. As for their difference according to their kinds, there are big ones and small ones, some with transparent glass tips and some with blunt glass tips, some with three corners and some with four corners.
And some of them have tongues, and some of them have shreds. And as for those that are according to the organs they are lodged in, they are two kinds: either the organs are major organs such as the brain, heart, liver, lungs, kidneys, stomach, bladder and similar ones. If a spear has hit one of these organs and symptoms of death which I have described to you appear, it is advisable to avoid extracting the spear from it, for death usually befalls its owner in most cases. And if these bad symptoms have not appeared to you and the spear has not been hidden in the organ, then remove it and treat the wound. And among the signs of the brain if a spear has hit it and perforated the bone and wounded the membrane over the brain is that severe headache, confusion and dizziness result from this.
And if these bad symptoms have not appeared to you and the spear has not been hidden in the organ, then remove it and treat the wound. And among the signs of the brain if a spear has hit it and perforated the bone and wounded the membrane over the brain is that severe headache, confusion and dizziness result from this. And redness in the eyes and red tongue, tremors and disorientation of mind and vomiting once perhaps or maybe bleeding comes out from the nostrils or ears and maybe speech is cut off and voice gone and liquid white like porridge comes out from the place of the wound and a discharge like serum flows from it.
So if these symptoms appear to you, then stop treating the patient and extracting the spear if it has not come out, and as for the signs of a spear that has pierced the heart and was close to the left breast and felt by you as if it had sunk into something hard and not in an empty space.
And maybe the spear had a movement like the pulse and blood, black as tar, would flow from the wound, followed by coldness of the limbs and chilliness and shivering, so know that death is inevitable. And a sign of the spear if it has wounded the lung is that blackish blood comes out from the wound.
And the vessels near the neck will swell and the colour of the wound will change and he will breathe with a high breathing and ask for cold air inhalation. And if the spear has pierced the membrane inside the chest then it is close to the small ribs and there will be great difficulty in breathing with severe pain.
And he will strain and move all the members of the neck, and if the spear has pierced the liver then severe pain will follow and blood will come out from the wound that is similar in colour to the liver. And if the spear has pierced the stomach then maybe something undigested will come out from the wound.
He is to be exposed, and if the arrowhead has pierced his belly and something comes out of him from the wound or discharge or abscess that has burst, then there is no hope for his treatment nor for removing the arrow. If the arrow has entered his bladder and urine has come out.
And if something protrudes from it and pain intensifies on the patient, then know that he is doomed to die. As for the other organs such as the face, eye, throat, shoulder, elbow, back, ribcage, thigh, leg and similar organs, assume the worst in this case.
When the arrow does not hit an artery or a nerve, and the arrow itself is not poisoned, and I am telling you some of what I have seen regarding these arrows so that you can use it as a guide for your treatment, that an arrow had pierced a man in his cheek into the beginning of the nose.
So I extracted it from him on the other side under his earlobe and he recovered without any harm to his eye. And I extracted another arrow that had pierced a Jew in the corner of his eye beneath the lower eyelid, and the arrowhead itself had disappeared except for its small tip which was lodged in the bone.
And it was a large arrow from the composite arrows made of hardened iron, square in shape and smooth, without any head to it. The Jew recovered and no harm occurred to his eye. And I extracted another arrow from a Christian's throat, and the arrow was Arab-made.
And he had two heads, so I cut him in half between the vertebrae and he had gone into his throat. I twisted him until I extracted it and the Christian was saved and recovered. And I extracted another arrow from a man who had been pierced in the abdomen, and we had estimated that he would die from it.
So when a period of thirty days or more had passed and nothing had changed in his condition, I cut the arrow off from him and extracted it and he recovered without any further harm. And I saw a man who had been pierced by an arrow in his back, so the wound healed over it.
When seven years had passed, the arrowhead emerged from its tip, and I saw a woman in whom an arrow had been lodged in her belly. The wound became inflamed, but the arrow remained unchanged and caused no harm in anything of her natural functions.
And I saw another man in whom an arrow had been lodged in his face, and the wound became inflamed. But he felt little pain from it, as was similar with many others. And I extracted an arrow from a knight of the Sultan that had struck him in the middle of his nose which had slightly tilted to the right side.
And the arrow was extracted entirely. I was summoned to treat him three days after the arrow had been removed. And I found that the wound from the arrow was very narrow, so I searched it with a fine probe and did not feel anything. But he felt numbness and pain under his ear on the right side.
And I suspected that the numbness was from one end of the arrow, so I applied a strong adhesive to the site and let it dry in order for the area to become inflamed and show a sign of the arrow. Then I incised him, but nothing happened in the site indicating that the tip of the arrow had reached it.
And I continued applying the adhesive to him for many days, but nothing happened. Then I closed up the wound and left the arrow inside until he felt it one day in his nose. And I was informed of this news. So I placed a hot and sharp medicine on the wound for many days.
Until it was opened and I probed him, and I felt the thin tip of the arrow which had stuck in the wooden part. Then I continued to open up the wound with that hot medicine until we saw with our eyes the end of the arrow, and he went on for a period of time around four months.
Then, when the wound had expanded and I was able to insert forceps into it, I grasped it and moved it. But it did not respond by coming out, so I did not leave off applying various instruments to him until one day I caught hold of it with forceps in a firm grasp as shown in the picture at the end of this chapter.
And the physicians would judge that his nasal cartilage could not be stitched, so I stitched it and the wound closed and the patient was completely healed without any problem. And I will tell you how I removed some arrows to make this a measure and a guide for what I did not mention.
For the details of this craft and its intricacies are not comprehensible by description nor can they be contained in a book. Rather, it is the ingenious craftsman who measures little against much and deduces what is lacking from what has been done; and creates a new action and a new tool for strange and unfamiliar emergencies.
If I were to descend from this craft, then I would say that arrows come out of the organs in which they have penetrated in two types; either by being pulled out from the place where they entered or by being extracted on the opposite side of the wound.
Either the arrow is prominent in a place of fat, and it is pulled out; or if it has been lodged for too long in its time, then it should be left for some days until the fat surrounding it becomes putrid, making it easy to pull out and remove; similarly when it has penetrated bone.
And if it does not come out, then leave it also for some days and pull and move it every day, and it will come out; but if it still does not come out after a few days, then drill around the arrow in the same bone from all sides with a fine drill until the space is widened to allow the arrow to be pulled out. Then pull it out.
And if the arrow that has penetrated into the skull bone has become sharp in one of the ventricles of the brain and some of those symptoms I have mentioned have appeared from the wound, then refrain from pulling out the arrow and leave it until it becomes clear after a few days.
Take a thread and pull the arrow out, if it is deeply lodged and does not yield to pulling, use a probe around the arrow as I have described to you, then treat the area until it clears up. And as for the arrow having disappeared in some part of the body. and he has lost feeling for it, probe him with a catheter, if you feel the arrow, then pull it out with some instruments that are suitable to extract it. And if you are unable to do so because of the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow in the organ, and there is no bone, nerve or vessel.
then cut him open until the wound expands and you are able to extract the arrow. And if he has ears, hold onto them, then remove the lodged flesh from all around with any means you can manage to do so. And occupy yourself with it, even if you cannot manage to clear the flesh from the cracked ears, loosen them until you are rid of it.
And if you try to remove the arrow in any place, then use your hand with linens all around until you clear it and be gentle so that the arrow does not break and it will be difficult for you to pull it out. And if you are unable to do so within a timely manner.
Then leave it for a few days until the flesh around it rots, then try again and it will be easy. And if bleeding occurs, treat it with what we have mentioned in its section, and conserve your effort from cutting a vessel or nerve or tendon and use cunning.
You can free the arrow with any means, and it may be that by being gentle and cautious, you cut into it firmly as I have described to you. And it is necessary for you when pulling out the arrow to make the wound similar in shape to what it was like at the time of the injury, this is more suitable.
If you cannot do that, use what can be done from the shapes. And as for the arrow which comes out on the other side, either something has come out of it to the outside or you will find the tip of the arrow by touch from above the skin, close and coming out.
Split it open and let the incision be as much as can fit the calipers, then pull him out. If he is stuck in a bone, bend your hand until the arrowhead works into the bone and opens itself, then pull him out.
Otherwise, leave him for a few days until it recedes and comes out. If the string of the arrow is in it, push him with it. And if the string has fallen and you want to use the pushing, insert into it the bent tool so that it enters its cavity into the hollow of the shaft then push him with it.
If the arrow is hollow, push him with a tool that enters into that cavity because the arrow becomes easy to come out from it. And if the arrow has poison in it, you should remove all of the flesh which has been poisoned, if possible, then treat him as what suits this.
If the arrow is in the chest or in the abdomen or in the bladder or in the rib and it was close to what can be felt by touch with the fingers and you could make an incision on him, then make an incision and guard against cutting a nerve or artery and take him out.
Then sew the wound if it needed sewing then treat him until he heals. Picture of calipers which attract arrows:.

The Ninetieth Chapter.
In the section on draining of veins.
The veins which are usually accustomed to being drained in the body are thirty; among them are sixteen in the head, namely the two carotids behind the ears known as the husasain and the two jugulars in the temples known as the zhaahrans and the two nasals in the corners of the eyes known as the nazaarians.
And the vein standing in the middle of the forehead and the vein at the tip of the nose and the two jugular veins in the neck and the two facial veins in the upper lip and the two facial veins in the lower lip and these veins are known as the jaharik and the two veins under the tongue.
And as for the veins which are drained in the arm and hand, they are five; one of them is the cephalic, which is on the fleshy side and which the common people call vein of the head, and the basilic which is the middle one, which is composed of a branch of the cephalic and a branch from it and which the common people call body vein.
And the basilic which is on the anterior side and also called the axillary vein, and which the common people call arm vein and tendon of the arm which is located on the tendons and which adheres to it and which appears above the elbow clearly and distinctly.
And it is the vein between the malleolus and the fibula, which has two branches, and in the leg and foot there are three veins, one of them being under the knee from the fleshy side, the second being the saphenous and its place is behind the ankle from the anterior side, and the vein of the achilles and its place is behind the heel from the fleshy side.
In the other leg are three veins like it. As for the two veins behind the ears, their benefit is to repel chronic and acute colds, catarrh, and the poor, long-standing headaches, and how to repel them as I have described.
And it is that you shave the head of the patient and scratch his back in the place of the veins with a rough cloth, then strangle the patient's neck with a hood until the veins appear, and they are behind the ears in the two low places on the head, so you will feel them under your finger, and teach him to do it with ink.
Then take a thin lancet, also known as the nahl, and insert it under the vein in the skin until it reaches the bone, then lift your hand with the vein and skin upwards and cut the vein along with the skin into separate cuts of about two fingers length.
Or similarly and send out the amount of blood that you want, then tie them with ligatures and leave them until they heal. And as for the arteries in the temples, their benefit is to repel chronic colds, difficult headaches and permanent swelling and sharp pus that has accumulated near the eyes.
And how to repel them as I have described to you, the patient ties his neck with a hood until the veins appear and can be felt under your finger, then teach him to write with ink, and then lift the skin from above the vein with your index finger.
And insert the thin lancet from below and lift the vein upwards and cut it as you did with the other veins, and send out the blood to the extent of your need, then remove the patient's stricture and place your finger on the vein for a moment.
Then put cotton and linen on it, tie from above tight and close, and leave it until he heals. Its mention and cut and thread were mentioned in the beginning of the book. As for cutting the facial veins, its benefit after cutting the varicose veins is for chronic face diseases such as freckles, ulcers and fine redness.
And the manner of its cure as I told you, it suffocates the vein in his neck with a turban until the vein appears then take the instrument which is called the saw and this is its shape.
Put the spike that is at the head of the saw on the same vein and strike from above with a comb or something else in its direction and leave the blood to flow into the vessel you want then untie the ligature and tie him until he heals.
And it may be opened with a wide syringe but it should not be that the syringe has an edge like other syringes but rather a slightly wide edge and he opens it with the syringe because the bone is close so the syringe might break if it is thin.
And as for the veins in the eye sockets, their benefit is for diseases of the eye such as jaundice, redness and ophthalmia and face diseases. And as for how to open them, it is that he ties the ligature around his neck with a turban then you open them while standing on his head and the opening should be at an angle to the length slightly with a small syringe which is slightly wide.
For the place is not fatty in it, so if the syringe has a thin edge then it may break, then the blood flows and you put cotton on them and tie them for one night then untie them. And as for cutting the vein of the nose its benefit is from acute fever.
And severe headache and face diseases such as red congestion which appears in the nose, especially if it is chronic. And as for how to cut it, he ties the ligature around his neck then you take his nose with your left hand and take a thin long syringe.
He wraps himself in the middle of the armrest, while keeping his nose straight because moisture does not appear there. Then blood comes out from his vein and he should put his finger on the probe a little and send what is needed then tie him at night, for it becomes dry quickly.
As for the warts, their usefulness is to remove them since they cause difficulty in breathing and are the beginning of leprosy and black diseases which appear on the surface of the skin such as black plaque, buboes and poor ulcers. And how to get rid of them, by tying a string under them in his neck and standing on it.
The patient sits on a chair then the moisture is drawn to length and lifted up slightly, then some blood is extracted in the amount that has been seen as needed, then the same is done with the other moisture and finally the bandage is wrapped.
The two moistures are tied tightly in the middle so that the patient does not suffocate and it is left until tomorrow, then the wound will heal. As for the veins of the neck, their usefulness is to remove them after having extracted the pus because they benefit from tumours in the mouth and decay of the gums and bad ulcers and cracks in the lips and ulcers.
The ones that are in the nose and around it.
